Secret Tazkiyah: Procedure for Witness Verification
Expansion of the ruling on secret tazkiyah with detailed procedure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the step-by-step procedure of secret tazkiyah and identify the conditions for a valid verifier and the appropriate notations.

Core Idea
Secret tazkiyah must be confidential to protect the process from bribery and harm.

This lesson explains the Hanafi procedure for secretly verifying witnesses' integrity (tazkiyah). You will learn the roles of the judge and verifier, the contents of the musturah letter, and how the verifier reports his findings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Secret tazkiyah is a procedure for verifying witnesses' uprightness. Its ruling is that it is a permissible and recommended practice to ensure the integrity of testimony.
2
List the conditions for the verifier (muzaqqi)
The verifier must be righteous, ascetic, trustworthy, knowledgeable, and socially connected. He should not be a recluse, greedy, or poor.
These conditions ensure the verifier can gather accurate information and is not easily corrupted.
3
Outline the steps of the procedure
The judge writes a musturah letter containing the witness's name, lineage, appearance, and mosque (or marketplace if a merchant). He sends it secretly via his trustee to the verifier. The verifier investigates by consulting neighbors, friends, and associates.
The entire communication must be confidential.
4
Describe the possible notations
If the witness is upright, the verifier writes 'huwa ‘adl marḍī maqbūl jā’iz al-shahādah'. If not upright, he writes nothing or 'Allahu a‘lam' to avoid exposure. If uncertain, he writes 'mustur'.
The verifier should not disclose specific faults unless necessary to prevent the judge from accepting false testimony.
5
Explain the importance of secrecy
Disclosure could lead to bribery of the verifier or harm to him. Therefore, the judge and verifier must keep the correspondence confidential.
This protects the integrity of the judicial process and all parties involved.

Source Text

تشریح تزکیہ اور تعدیل کسی کے عادل اور غیر عادل ہونے کی تحقیق کرنیکا نام ہے۔ مزکی اور معدل تعدیل اور تزکیہ کرنے والے کو کہتے ہیں ۔ مستورہ ، وہ خط ہے جس میں قاضی گواہوں کے نام ، نسب ، خلیہ اور ان کے محلہ کی مسجد لکھ کر اپنے امین کی معرفت خفیہ طریقہ پر مرگی کے پاس بھیجے گا۔ چونکہ اس خط کو عوام کی نظروں سے چھپانا مقصود ہوتا ہے اسلئے اس خط کا نام مستورہ رکھا گیا۔
تزکیہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔
تزکیہ فی السر -۲ تزکیہ فی العلانیہ
تزکیہ فی السر یہ ہے کہ قاضی گواہوں کی عدالت دریافت کرنے کے لئے مزکی اور معدل کے نام ایک خط لکھ کر چپکے سے اپنے [؟] امین کے ذریعہ مرگی کے پاس روانہ کر دے۔ خط میں گواہوں کا نام، ان کا نسب ، ان کا حلیہ اور ان کے محلہ کی مسجد تحریر کردے۔ اور اگر گواہ بازاری آدمی ہو تو اس کا بازار تحریر کرے۔ اور مناسب یہ ہے کہ مزکی (تعدیل کرنے والا) صالح ، زاہد، لوگوں میں زیادہ معتمد و پرہیز گار ہو اور امانت دار اور ذی علم ہو ، اور لوگوں سے مل جل کر رہتا ہو، بالکل گوشہ نشین اور صوفی منش نہ ہو کہ اپنی نیک بختی کی وجہ سے ہر شخص کو نیک سمجھتا یا ہر ایک کے کہنے پر اعتماد کر لیتا ہو۔ مزکی حریص اور فقیر بھی نہ ہو کیونکہ حریص اور فقیر آدمی مال کے چکر میں آ کر صحیح اطلاع پہنچانے میں ناکام ہو سکتا ہے۔
پس مزکی گواہوں کے بارے میں ان کے پڑوسیوں ، دوستوں ، ہم پیشہ لوگوں اور ان کے پاس اٹھنے بیٹھنے والوں سے دریافت کرے تحقیق و تفتیش کے بعد اگر مزکی کو ان کا عادل ہونا معلوم ہوا تو مزکی جو خط قاضی کے نام تحریر کرے گا اس میں گواہ کے نام کے نیچے یہ الفاظ تحریر کرے۔ هو عدل مرضى مقبول جائز الشهادة یعنی یہ گواہ میرے نزدیک عادل، پسندیدہ مقبول اور جائز الشہادت ہے۔ اور اگر انکا غیر عادل ہونا معلوم ہوا تو گواہ کے نام کے نیچے کچھ تحریر نہ کرے تا کہ اس کا پردہ فاش نہ ہو۔ یا صرف ( واللہ اعلم) لکھدے۔ حاصل یہ کہ تحقیق و تفتیش کے نتیجے میں گواہوں کے جن عیوب پر مطلع ہوا ہو ان کو تحریر نہ کرے۔ ہاں اگر مزکی کو یہ اندیشہ ہو کہ عیوب اور فسق کی صراحت نہ کرنے کی صورت میں قاضی ان کی گواہی پر فیصلہ کر سکتا ہے تو اس صورت میں گواہوں کے عیوب کی صراحت کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے ۔ اور اگر مزکی گواہ کی عدالت اور فسق دونوں پر مطلع نہ ہو سکا تو اس کے نام کے نیچے ( مستور ) لکھدے یعنی یہ لکھدے کہ اس کا حال پوشیدہ ہے۔ مرکی تمام باتوں کو لکھ کر قاضی کے امین کے ذریعہ اس خط کو قاضی کے پاس روانہ کر دے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قاضی کا مزکی کے پاس خط بھیجنا اور مزکی کا تحقیق کر کے اس کو قاضی کے پاس بھیجنا سب باتیں صیغہ راز میں رہنی چاہئیں۔ کیونکہ ظاہر ہونے کی صورت میں گواہ مزکی یا مدعی مزکی کو رشوت دے کر خرید سکتا ہے۔ اور رشوت قبول نہ کرنے کی صورت میں گواہ مزکی کو ایذاء پہنچا سکتا ہے۔ پس ان خطرات کے پیش نظر پوری کارروائی خفیہ ہونی چاہئے۔
Explanation: Tazkiyah and ta'dil are terms for investigating whether someone is upright or not. Muzaqqi and mu'addil refer to the verifier. Musturah is the letter in which the judge writes the names, lineage, appearance, and mosque of the witnesses and sends it secretly via his trustee to the verifier. Because this letter is intended to be hidden from the public, it is called musturah. Tazkiyah is of two types: secret and public. Secret tazkiyah is that the judge writes a letter to the verifier to inquire about the witnesses' integrity, sending it secretly via his trustee. In the letter, he writes the names, lineage, appearance, and mosque of the witnesses. If the witness is a market person, he writes his marketplace. It is appropriate that the verifier be righteous, ascetic, most trusted among people, pious, trustworthy, and knowledgeable; he should mix with people and not be a recluse or a Sufi who considers everyone good due to his own piety or trusts everyone's word. The verifier should not be greedy or poor because a greedy or poor person may be deceived by wealth and fail to convey accurate information. Then the verifier inquires about the witnesses from their neighbors, friends, colleagues, and associates. After investigation, if the verifier finds them upright, he writes under the witness's name in his letter to the judge: 'He is upright, acceptable, qualified to testify.' If he finds them not upright, he writes nothing under the name to avoid exposing them, or he simply writes 'Allah knows best.' The conclusion is that he should not write the faults he discovers. However, if the verifier fears that without specifying faults the judge might still accept their testimony, then he may specify the faults. If the verifier is unable to ascertain either integrity or transgression, he writes 'mustur' (concealed) under the name. The verifier then sends the letter back to the judge via the judge's trustee. The author of al-Hidayah says: The sending of the letter by the judge to the verifier and the verifier's reply should all remain confidential, because if disclosed, the witness might bribe the verifier, or if the bribe is refused, harm him. Therefore, the entire process must be kept secret.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary expanding on the ruling of secret tazkiyah. It first defines key terms: tazkiyah/ta'dil (verification), muzaqqi/mu'addil (verifier), and musturah (confidential letter). It then explains the procedure step by step: the judge sends a musturah containing the witness's name, lineage, appearance, and mosque (or marketplace if the witness is a merchant). The verifier must be a trustworthy, knowledgeable, and socially connected person, not a recluse or easily deceived. He investigates by consulting neighbors, friends, and associates. If the witness is upright, he writes 'huwa 'adl marḍī maqbūl jā'iz al-shahādah' (he is upright, acceptable, qualified to testify). If not upright, he writes nothing to avoid exposing the witness, or writes 'Allahu a'lam' (Allah knows best). He should not specify faults unless necessary to prevent the judge from mistakenly accepting the testimony. If uncertain, he writes 'mustur' (concealed). The entire correspondence must remain confidential to prevent bribery or harm. This commentary emphasizes the importance of secrecy to protect the integrity of the judicial process and the well-being of all parties involved.

Key Terms
مزکی (muzaqqi): The person assigned to verify the integrity of witnesses
مستور (mustur): A notation meaning the witness's condition is unknown to the verifier
عادل ('adil): A witness who is upright and whose testimony is accepted

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should the verifier write if he cannot determine whether the witness is upright or not?
A) 'He is upright.'
B) Nothing.
C) 'Mustur' (concealed).
D) 'Allahu a'lam' only.

Key Takeaway
The verifier must maintain confidentiality and write only the appropriate notation based on his investigation.

Required Wording in Tazkiya: Is 'Adl' Enough?
Explains the necessity of mentioning both 'hurr' and 'adl' in tazkiya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi preferred view on the required wording in tazkiya and distinguish it from alternative views within and outside the school.

Core Idea
For tazkiya, saying 'huwa adl' alone is sufficient per the preferred Hanafi view.

When vouching for a witness in court, the muzzaki must confirm the witness's integrity. But does the law require him to explicitly state that the witness is free? This lesson explores a dispute among Hanafi scholars and across schools on whether mentioning 'hurr' is necessary. By understanding the reasoning and tarjih, you will grasp how the Hanafi school prioritises practicality while preserving the conditions for testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central act and its ruling
The act is tazkiya (vouching for a witness). The passage discusses what wording makes it valid, not the act's own conditions.
The ruling is on the form of tazkiya, not the witness's status.
2
State the two Hanafi views
One group requires explicit mention of both 'adl' and 'hurr'. Another group (including Sahib al-Hidayah) says 'adl' alone is sufficient.
Identify which view is presented as 'asahh' (more correct).
3
Analyse the rationale for each view
The stricter view argues that a slave can be just but his testimony is rejected, so free status must be verified. The permissive view counters that free status is presumed in Dar al-Islam.
Note the presumption (zahir) of freedom in a Muslim polity.
4
Identify cross-madhhab positions
Imam Malik requires both attributes; Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad accept the permissive view. This shows the dispute extends beyond the Hanafi school.
Cross-madhhab awareness helps in comparative fiqh.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Sahib al-Hidayah declares the permissive view as 'asahh', making it the relied-upon position for fatwa in the Hanafi school.
The authority is al-Marghinani, a later Hanafi master.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بارے میں هو عدل جائز الشهادة پر اکتفاء نہ کرے۔ بلکہ حر کا لفظ کہنا بھی ضروری ہے۔ یعنی یہ کہے کہ یہ گواہ آزاد ہے عادل ہے، جائز الشہادت ہے کیونکہ بسا اوقات غلام بھی عادل ہوتا ہے حالانکہ اس کی شہادت معتبر نہیں ہوتی اس لئے گواہ کے آزاد ہونے کی وضاحت کرنا بھی ضروری ہے۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ گواہ کے بارے میں هو عدل کہنا کافی ہے حسد اور جائز الشہادۃ کہنا شرط نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ گواہ کے دار السلام میں ہونے کی وجہ سے آزاد ہونا ظاہر ہے۔ صاحب بدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہی قول زیادہ صحیح ہے۔ اسی کے قائل شوافع اور امام احمد ہیں۔ اور امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ مزکی کے لئے گواہ کے بارے میں عادل مرضی کہنا ضروری ہے۔ ان دونوں و صفوں میں اسے ایک وصف پر اکتفاء کرنا جائز نہیں۔
Regarding 'he is just, permissible testimony', one should not be satisfied with that alone, but it is also necessary to say the word 'free'. That is, he should say: this witness is free, just, permissible of testimony, because sometimes a slave is also just while his testimony is not considered. Therefore, it is necessary to clarify that the witness is free. And some mashayikh said that saying 'he is just' is sufficient, and saying 'just and permissible testimony' is not a condition, because due to the witness being in Dar al-Islam, being free is apparent. Sahib al-Hidayah says that this statement is more correct. The Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad are of this view. And Imam Malik said that for the muzzaki, it is necessary to say regarding the witness 'just and acceptable', and it is not permissible to suffice with one of these two attributes.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage discusses the wording required when vouching for a witness (tazkiya). The default view mentioned is that one must explicitly state both that the witness is free (hurr) and just (adl), because a slave can be just but his testimony is not accepted. However, some later Hanafi scholars deem it sufficient to say only 'adl', as free status is presumed in Dar al-Islam. Sahib al-Hidayah (the commentator of the Hidayah) declares this latter view as more correct ('asahh'), and it aligns with the Shafi'i and Hanbali positions. Imam Malik, however, requires both attributes. Thus, the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school (according to this text) is that mentioning 'hurr' is not a condition for valid tazkiya.

Key Terms
تزكية (tazkiyah): The act of vouching for a witness's integrity and justness before the judge
عدل ('adl): A person who is just, avoiding major sins and minor sins habitually, and maintaining good character
حر (hurr): Free person as opposed to slave; a condition for testimony

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in Ashraf ul Hadaya, what is sufficient to say when vouching for a witness?
A) 'Huwa adl' alone
B) 'Huwa adl wa hurr'
C) 'Huwa adl wa jai'iz al-shahada'
D) 'Huwa adl wa mardi'

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the preferred view is that a tazkiya mentioning only 'adl' is valid, as free status is presumed in Dar al-Islam.

Defendant's Tazkiya of Plaintiff's Witnesses: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on defendant's tazkiya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether a defendant's statement about witnesses' justice constitutes valid tazkiya, and distinguish between Zahir al-Riwayah and the Sahibayn's views.

Core Idea
A defendant's tazkiya is unreliable because he is not considered just, but Sahibayn allow it under conditions.

This passage tackles a subtle issue in the law of testimony (shahadat): Who can vouch for the justice of witnesses? The defendant, though a party, might offer tazkiya, but the Hanafi school is split. Understanding this dispute reveals deeper principles about the conditions for tazkiya and the epistemological weight of court statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the legal question
The act is the defendant's statement that the plaintiff's witnesses are 'adl (just). The legal question: Is this statement accepted as valid tazkiya?
Tazkiya is the process of establishing a witness's justice; the person who vouches is a muzzaki.
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position
In Zahir al-Riwayah (the authoritative transmission), the defendant's statement is not accepted as tazkiya.
This is attributed to Abu Hanifa and is the default position in the school.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it, but with an important condition: the defendant himself must be just. Muhammad further requires a second muzzaki.
This is from the Nawadir (non-mainstream transmissions).
4
Analyze the reasoning (talil) behind each view
The Zahir al-Riwayah reasoning: the defendant is presumed lying in his denial of the claim, so he cannot be a just muzzaki. The Sahibayn's reasoning: the statement is tazkiya, not an admission; it can be accepted if the defendant is just.
The text addresses an objection: 'they are just but they erred' is tazkiya, not an admission. If the defendant says 'they are truthful', it is an admission.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
If not accepted, the judge must independently investigate the witnesses' justice. If accepted (and conditions met), the case proceeds based on that tazkiya.
This practical consequence matters for court procedure.

Source Text

مدعی علیہ کے قول کہ گواہ عادل ہیں کا اعتبار کیا جائے گایا نہیں

قال وفى قول من راى ان يسأل عن الشهود لم يقبل قول الخصم انه عدل معناه قول المدعى عليه وعن أبى يوسف و محمد انه يجوز تزكيته لكن عند محمد يضم تزكية الاخر الى تزكيته لأن العدد عنده شرط ووجه الظاهر ان فى زعم المدعى وشهوده ان الخصم كاذب فى انكاره مبطل فى اصرارة فلا يصلح معدلاً وموضوع المسألة اذا قال هم عدول الا انهم اخطأ وا اونسوا اما اذا قال صدقوا اوهم عدول صدقة فقد اعترف بالحق

ترجمہ فرمایا کہ جس کے اجتہاد میں گواہوں کا حال دریافت کرنا ضروری ہے (اس کے قول پر ) شخصم یعنی مدعلی علیہ کا قول کہ گواہ عادل ہے قبول نہ ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کی تعدیل جائز ہے لیکن امام محمد کے نزدیک مدعلی علیہ کے تزکیہ کے ساتھ دوسرے کا تزکیہ ملالیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ امام محمد کے نزدیک عدد شرط ہے۔ اور ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مدعی اور اس کے گواہوں کے گمان میں مدعی علیہ اپنے انکار میں جھوٹا اور اپنے اصرار میں باطل پر ہے۔ لہذا وہ مز کی ہونے کے لائق نہ ہوگا۔ اور مسئلہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ جب مدگی علیہ نے کہا کہ یہ گواہ عادل ہیں مگر یہ چوک گئے یا بھول گئے۔ لیکن اگر مدعی علیہ نے کہا کہ ان گواہوں نے سچ کہا یا یہ گواہ عادل بچے ہیں تو اس نے حق کا اقرار کر لیا۔

تشریح گذشتہ سے پیوستہ تشریح کے تحت ذکر کیا گیا کہ اگر مدعی علیہ، مدعی کے گواہوں پر طعن نہ کرے تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزد یک گواہوں کی ظاہری عدالت پر اکتفاء کیا جائے گا۔ ان کی تعدیل اور ان کا حال دریافت کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی گواہوں کی تعدیل اور ان کا حال دریافت کرنا ضروری ہے۔ پس صاحبین کے قول پر تفریح بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ اگر مدعی علیہ نے مدعی کے گواہوں کے بارے میں کہا کہ یہ گواہ عادل ہیں تو ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق مدعی علیہ کا یہ قول یعنی مدعی علیہ کا گواہوں کی تعدیل کرنا مقبول اور معتبر نہ ہو گا۔ اور نوادر میں صاحبین سے مروی ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کی تعدیل کافی ہے یعنی اگر مدعی علیہ نے مدعی کے گواہوں کے بارے میں کہا کہ یہ گواہ عادل ہیں تو مدعی علیہ کا یہ قول معتبر ہوگا اور ان کی گواہی پر فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا لیکن امام محمد کے نزدیک مدعلی علیہ کی تعدیل کے ساتھ دوسرا تعدیل کرنے والا ملا لیا جائے گا یعنی مدعی علیہ کی تعدیل کے تعدیل کے ساتھ ایک دوسرے آدمی کا تعدیل کرنا بھی ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ حضرت امام محمد کے نزدیک تعدیل میں کم از کم دو مزکیوں اور

معدلوں (تعدیل کر نیوالوں) کا ہونا شرط ہے۔ یہ واضح رہے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک مدعی علیہ کی تعدیل اُسی وقت معتبر ہوگی جب کہ مدعی علیه خود عادل ہو۔ کیونکہ معدل مرکی ( تعدیل کرنے والے ) کا عادل ہونا سب کے نزدیک شرط ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر مدعی علیہ فاسق ہو یا اس کا حال پوشیدہ ہو اور مدعی علیہ کے دعوی کا انکار نہ کیا ہو بلکہ سکوت کیا ہو پھر مدعی کے گواہوں کے بارے میں کہا کہ یہ گواہ عادل ہیں تو مدعی علیہ کی یہ تعدیل درست اور معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مدعی اپنا دعویٰ ثابت کرنے کے لئے گواہ اس وقت پیش کرتا ہے جب مدعی علیہ، مدعی کے دعوئی کا انکار کرتا ہو اور اپنے انکار پر جمار ہے۔ اور مدعی اس کو دعوی کا انکار میں جھوٹا اور باطل پر سمجھتا ہو ۔ پس مدعی اور اس کے گواہوں کے اعتقاد میں مدعی علیہ اپنے انکار میں جھوٹا اور اپنی ہٹ کرنے میں باطل پر ہوگا۔ اور جب مدعلی علیہ، مدگی اور اسکے گواہوں کے اعتقاد میں جھوٹا اور باطل پر ہے اور جو شخص جھوٹا اور باطل پر ہو وہ عادل نہیں ہو سکتا تو مدعی علیہ مُعدّل اور مر کی بننے کے لائق نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مزکی کے لئے عادل ہونا بالاتفاق شرط ہے۔ وموضوع المسألة ... الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کا گواہوں کی تعدیل کرنا در بیت اپنے او پر مدعی کے حق کا اقرار کرنا ہےاور مقر کا عامل ہونا بالاتفاق شرط نہیں ہے لہذا فاسق ہونے کے باوجود مدعی علیہ کی تعدیل مقبول ہونی چاہئے۔

جواب ... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس مسئلہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ جب مدعی علیہ نے کہا کہ یہ گواہ عادل ہیں لیکن یہ چوک گئے یا بھول گئے ہیں اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ اس طرح کا کلام کسی حق کا اقرار نہیں ہوتا یعنی مدعی علیہ کے اس کلام کو مدعی کے حق کا اقرار نہیں کہا جا سکتا ہے بلکہ یہ گواہوں کی تعدیل ہے اور یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی ہے کی تعدیل کرنے والے کا عادل ہونا شرط ہے۔ لہذا مدعی علیہ ، جو مدعی کے گواہوں کی تعدیل کرنے والا ہے اس کا عادل ہونا بھی شرط ہے۔ حالانکہ مدعی علیہ، مدعی اور گواہوں کے اعتقاد میں دعوی کا انکار کرنے کی وجہ سے جھوٹا اور غیر عادل ہے۔ پس جب مدعی علیہ جھوٹا اور غیر عادل ہے تو اس کا مدعی کے گواہوں کی تعدیل کرنا بھی مقبول اور معتبر نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر مدعی غلیہ نے کہا کہ مدعی کے گواہ بچے ہیں یا کہا کہ عادل بچے ہیں تو گویا مدعی علیہ نے اپنے اوپر مدعی کے حق کا اقرار کر لیا اور جب مدعی علیہ نے مدعی کے حق کا اقرار کر لیا تو قاضی ، مدعی علیہ کے اقرار کرنے کے وجہ سے فیصلہ کرے گا نہ کہ گواہوں کی گواہی کی وجہ سے۔
The statement of the defendant that the witnesses are just, will it be accepted or not? He said: And according to the opinion of one who holds that the judge should inquire about the witnesses, the statement of the opponent (meaning the defendant) that he is just is not accepted. And from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is narrated that his tazkiya is permissible, but according to Muhammad, the tazkiya of another is joined to his tazkiya because number is a condition for him. And the apparent meaning is that in the assumption of the plaintiff and his witnesses, the opponent is lying in his denial and wrong in his insistence, so he is not suitable as a muzzaki. The subject matter is when he says: They are just, but they made a mistake or forgot. However, if he says: They told the truth or they are just and truthful, then he has admitted the right. The translation: for one whose ijtihad requires inquiring about the witnesses, the statement of the defendant that the witness is just will not be accepted. And from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is narrated that the defendant's tazkiya is permissible, but according to Muhammad, another tazkiya is joined to his tazkiya because number is a condition for him. And the reason in Zahir al-Riwayah is that in the assumption of the plaintiff and his witnesses, the defendant is lying in his denial and wrong in his insistence, so he is not worthy of being a muzzaki. The scenario is when the defendant says: These witnesses are just but they erred or forgot. But if the defendant says: They spoke truth or they are just and truthful, then he has admitted the right. The commentary attached to the previous explanation stated that if the defendant does not impugn the plaintiff's witnesses, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the apparent justice of the witnesses is sufficient; there is no need to investigate their tazkiya or condition. According to the Sahibayn, in this case also, investigating tazkiya and condition is necessary. So elaborating on the Sahibayn's view, it is said that if the defendant says about the plaintiff's witnesses that they are just, then according to Zahir al-Riwayah, this statement of the defendant (i.e., the defendant's tazkiya of the witnesses) is not acceptable or valid. And in the Nawadir, it is narrated from the Sahibayn that the defendant's tazkiya is sufficient, meaning if the defendant says about the plaintiff's witnesses that they are just, then this statement is valid and judgment will be made on their testimony, but according to Imam Muhammad, along with the defendant's tazkiya, another muzzaki is to be added, i.e., another person's tazkiya is also necessary alongside the defendant's tazkiya, because Imam Muhammad holds that at least two muzzakis are required. It should be clear that according to the Sahibayn, the defendant's tazkiya is valid only when the defendant himself is just, because the muzzaki being just is a condition for all. So if the defendant is a sinner or his condition is hidden, and he has not denied the claim but remained silent, then if he says about the plaintiff's witnesses that they are just, this tazkiya of the defendant is not correct or valid. The reason in Zahir al-Riwayah is that the plaintiff brings witnesses to prove his claim when the defendant denies the claim and persists in his denial, and the plaintiff considers him lying in his denial and wrong. So in the belief of the plaintiff and his witnesses, the defendant is lying in his denial and wrong in his insistence, and a person who is lying and wrong cannot be just, so the defendant is not suitable to be a muzzaki, because the muzzaki being just is a condition by consensus. The phrase 'the subject matter of the case' etc. answers a question. The question is: the defendant's tazkiya of the witnesses is in reality an admission of the plaintiff's right against himself, and the justness of the admission is not a condition by consensus, so even if the defendant is a sinner, his tazkiya should be accepted. The answer: the scenario of this case is when the defendant says 'these witnesses are just but they erred or forgot', and it is clear that such speech is not an admission of any right, i.e., it cannot be called an admission of the plaintiff's right. Rather, it is tazkiya of the witnesses, and it has passed that the condition of the muzzaki being just is required. Therefore, the defendant, who is doing tazkiya of the plaintiff's witnesses, being just is also a condition, even though the defendant, in the belief of the plaintiff and witnesses, is lying and unjust due to denying the claim. So when the defendant is lying and unjust, his tazkiya of the plaintiff's witnesses will not be accepted or valid. Yes, if the defendant says 'the plaintiff's witnesses are truthful' or says 'they are just truthful', then he has admitted the plaintiff's right against himself, and when he admits the right, the judge will judge based on his admission, not on the testimony of the witnesses.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage deals with whether the defendant's (mudda'a alayh) statement that the plaintiff's witnesses are 'adl can serve as valid tazkiya. The Zahir al-Riwayah position (attributed to Abu Hanifa) is that it is not accepted because the defendant is considered untrustworthy in this context—he is presumed lying in his denial of the claim, so he cannot be a just muzzaki. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it, but Muhammad adds the condition that a second muzzaki is required because he requires two muzzakis in general. Furthermore, all agree that the muzzaki himself must be just; thus, if the defendant is a sinner, his tazkiya is invalid even according to the Sahibayn. The text also answers an objection: when the defendant says 'they are just but they erred', this is tazkiya, not an admission of the claim. But if he says 'they are truthful', it is an admission, and judgment is based on that.

Key Terms
مدعی علیہ (mudda'a alayh): The defendant, the person against whom a claim is made
تزكية (tazkiyah): The act of vouching for a witness's justice
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted position in the Hanafi school from the six books of Imam Muhammad

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, why is the defendant's tazkiya not accepted?
A) Because he is a party to the case
B) Because he is not considered just
C) Because he might lie
D) Because he has no personal knowledge

Key Takeaway
The defendant's tazkiya of plaintiff's witnesses is not accepted in Zahir al-Riwayah because the defendant is not considered just for this purpose, though Sahibayn allow it with conditions.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Number of Muzzakis Required for Tazkiya
Discusses whether one or two muzzakis are needed for tazkiya according to the Hanafi imams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the required number of muzzakis for tazkiya and explain the reasoning behind the majority view vs. Imam Muhammad's view.

Core Idea
One muzzaki suffices for tazkiya according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; Imam Muhammad requires two.

When a witness's character needs verification, a muzzaki vouches for their justice. But how many muzzakis are needed? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: the majority of Hanafi imams accept one, while Imam Muhammad insists on two, analogizing tazkiya to testimony. Understanding this difference reveals how Hanafi jurists apply qiyas and distinguish between similar legal acts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: one muzzaki is permissible, two is better.
This is the well-known position in the school.
2
Identify Imam Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad requires two muzzakis; without them, tazkiya is not valid.
He is the dissenting voice among the three principal imams.
3
Follow Imam Muhammad's proof
He analogizes tazkiya to testimony (shahada), because both aim to establish justice. Since testimony requires two witnesses, tazkiya should also require two muzzakis.
This is a qiyas based on the underlying cause (illa): establishing justice.
4
Analyze the majority's response
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue that tazkiya is not fully analogous to testimony; it lacks other conditions like specific wording (lafz al-shahada) and assembly in court. Therefore, the numerical condition of testimony is not extended to tazkiya.
They limit the analogy to avoid imposing extra conditions.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If only one muzzaki is available, the majority would accept the tazkiya, while Imam Muhammad would not. This affects the admissibility of witnesses in court.
Later Hanafi practice generally follows the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مز کی شہود کی تعداد ، اقوال فقہاء

قال واذا كان رسول القاضى الذى يسأل عن الشهود واحد اجاز والاثنان افضل وهذا عند ابي حنيفة و ابي يوسف وقال محمد لا يجوز الا اثنان والمراد منه المزكى وعلى هذا الخلاف رسول القاضي الى المزكي والمترجم عن الشاهد له ان التزكية فى معنى الشهادة لان ولاية القضاء تبتنى على ظهور العدالة وهو بالتزكية فيشترط فيه العدد كما يشترط العدالة فيه و تشترط الذكورة فى المذكى في الحدود والقصاص ولهما انه ليس في معنى الشهادة ولهذا لا يشترط فيه لفظة الشهادة و مجلس القضاء واشتراط العدد امر حكمى فى الشهادة فلا يتعداها
The number of tazkiya witnesses, statements of the jurists. He said: And if the messenger of the judge who asks about the witnesses is one, it is permissible, and two is better. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: it is not permissible except with two. And what is meant is the muzzaki. And upon this difference is the messenger of the judge to the muzzaki and the translator from the witness. He (Muhammad) argues that tazkiya is in the meaning of testimony, because the authority of the judge is based on the manifestation of justice, and that is through tazkiya, so number is required just as justice is required in it, and masculinity is required in the muzzaki in cases of hudud and qisas. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), it is not in the meaning of testimony, therefore the wording of testimony is not required, nor the assembly of the judge, and the requirement of number is a ruling specific to testimony, so it is not extended.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage discusses the required number of people who vouch for a witness's justice (muzzakis). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that one muzzaki is sufficient, though two is better. Imam Muhammad requires two muzzakis, analogizing tazkiya to testimony because both aim to establish justice. However, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf argue that tazkiya is not literally testimony, so the conditions of testimony (like number, specific wording, and judge's assembly) are not required. This dispute has practical implications: if only one muzzaki is available, the majority Hanafi position would accept the tazkiya, while Muhammad would not.

Key Terms
مزکی (muzzaki): The person who vouches for a witness's justice
تعدیل (ta'dil): The act of vouching for justice; synonymous with tazkiya in this context
شهادة (shahada): Testimony in court; requires specific conditions including number, wording, and assembly
تزكية (tazkiya): The process of verifying a witness's justice; synonymous with ta'dil

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, how many muzzakis are required for tazkiya?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
The number of muzzakis required for tazkiya is disputed within the Hanafi school: one suffices according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, while Imam Muhammad requires two.

Shahadat — Testimony

Condition of 'Adalah for the Muzzaki and the Defendant's Tazkiyah
Ruling with rational proof on defendant's tazkiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the condition of 'adalah for a muzzaki, apply it to the defendant's tazkiyah scenario, and distinguish tazkiyah from acknowledgment.

Core Idea
A muzzaki must be 'adl; a defendant who denies the claim is considered non-'adl, so his tazkiyah is invalid unless it constitutes an acknowledgment.

This lesson examines a key rule in court proceedings: the person certifying the integrity of witnesses (muzzaki) must themselves be of upright character ('adalah). We will focus on a specific case where the defendant acts as muzzaki for the plaintiff's witnesses, and why the defendant's own 'adalah becomes critical. The discussion includes a rational proof and addresses a common objection about acknowledgment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Recognize that by consensus, a muzzaki must be 'adl. This is the foundational condition.
2
Examine the Specific Scenario
Understand that when the defendant himself certifies the plaintiff's witnesses, the same condition applies: the defendant must be 'adl for his tazkiyah to be valid.
This is the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
3
Analyze the Rational Proof
The proof is that the plaintiff and his witnesses necessarily believe the defendant to be a liar due to his denial of the claim. A person deemed a liar cannot be considered 'adl, so the defendant cannot serve as a reliable muzzaki.
This is a dalil 'aqli (rational evidence) based on the context of litigation.
4
Distinguish Tazkiyah from Acknowledgment
If the defendant says the witnesses are 'udul but he adds that they erred or forgot, this is tazkiyah, not an acknowledgment. However, if he simply says they are children (or another clear acknowledgment), it becomes an admission of the claim, and 'adalah is not required.
This distinction resolves the potential objection.

كتاب الشهادة
اشرفی الہدایہ جلد دومر
معدلوں (تعدیل کر نیوالوں) کا ہونا شرط ہے۔ یہ واضح رہے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک مدعی علیہ کی تعدیل اُسی وقت معتبر ہوگی جب کہ مدعی علیه خود عادل ہو۔ کیونکہ معدل مرکی ( تعدیل کرنے والے ) کا عادل ہونا سب کے نزدیک شرط ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر مدعی علیہ فاسق ہو یا اس کا حال پوشیدہ ہو اور مدعی علیہ کے دعوی کا انکار نہ کیا ہو بلکہ سکوت کیا ہو پھر مدعی کے گواہوں کے بارے میں کہا کہ یہ گواہ عادل ہیں تو مدعی علیہ کی یہ تعدیل درست اور معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مدعی اپنا دعویٰ ثابت کرنے کے لئے گواہ اس وقت پیش کرتا ہے جب مدعی علیہ، مدعی کے دعوئی کا انکار کرتا ہو اور اپنے انکار پر جمار ہے۔ اور مدعی اس کو دعوی کا انکار میں جھوٹا اور باطل پر سمجھتا ہو ۔ پس مدعی اور اس کے گواہوں کے اعتقاد میں مدعی علیہ اپنے انکار میں جھوٹا اور اپنی ہٹ کرنے میں باطل پر ہوگا۔ اور جب مدعلی علیہ، مدگی اور اسکے گواہوں کے اعتقاد میں جھوٹا اور باطل پر ہے اور جو شخص جھوٹا اور باطل پر ہو وہ عادل نہیں ہو سکتا تو مدعی علیہ مُعدّل اور مر کی
بننے کے لائق نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مزکی کے لئے عادل ہونا بالاتفاق شرط ہے۔ وموضوع المسألة ... الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ مدعی علیہ کا گواہوں کی تعدیل کرنا در بیت اپنے او پر مدعی کے حق کا اقرار کرنا ہےاور مقر کا عامل ہونا بالاتفاق شرط نہیں ہے لہذا فاسق ہونے کے باوجود مدعی علیہ کی تعدیل مقبول ہونی چاہئے۔
جواب ... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس مسئلہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ جب مدعی علیہ نے کہا کہ یہ گواہ عادل ہیں لیکن یہ چوک گئے یا بھول گئے ہیں اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ اس طرح کا کلام کسی حق کا اقرار نہیں ہوتا یعنی مدعی علیہ کے اس کلام کو مدعی کے حق کا اقرار نہیں کہا جا سکتا ہے بلکہ یہ گواہوں کی تعدیل ہے اور یہ بات پہلے گزر چکی ہے کی تعدیل کرنے والے کا عادل ہونا شرط ہے۔ لہذا مدعی علیہ ، جو مدعی کے گواہوں کی تعدیل کرنے والا ہے اس کا عادل ہونا بھی شرط ہے۔ حالانکہ مدعی علیہ، مدعی اور گواہوں کے اعتقاد میں دعوی کا انکار کرنے کی وجہ سے جھوٹا اور غیر عادل ہے۔ پس جب مدعی علیہ جھوٹا اور غیر عادل ہے تو اس کا مدعی کے گواہوں کی تعدیل کرنا بھی مقبول اور معتبر نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر مدعی غلیہ نے کہا کہ مدعی کے گواہ بچے ہیں یا کہا کہ عادل بچے ہیں تو گویا مدعی علیہ نے اپنے اوپر مدعی کے حق کا اقرار کر لیا اور جب مدعی علیہ نے مدعی کے حق کا اقرار کر لیا تو قاضی ، مدعی علیہ کے اقرار کرنے کے وجہ سے فیصلہ کرے گا نہ کہ گواہوں کی گواہی کی وجہ سے۔
Book of Testimony. Ashrafi al-Hidayah, Volume 2. The presence of those who certify (muzakkis) is a condition. It should be clear that according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the defendant's tazkiyah is only valid when the defendant himself is 'adl (just). Because the one who certifies must be 'adl, by consensus. So if the defendant is a fasiq (sinner) or his condition is unknown, and he did not deny the claim but remained silent, then said about the plaintiff's witnesses 'these witnesses are 'udul,' then this tazkiyah by the defendant is not valid. The reason from Zahir al-Riwayah is that the plaintiff brings witnesses to prove his claim only when the defendant denies the claim and persists in his denial. The plaintiff believes the defendant is lying and false in his denial. So in the belief of the plaintiff and his witnesses, the defendant is lying and false. And a person who is lying and false cannot be 'adl, so the defendant is not suitable to be a muzzaki because 'adalah of the muzzaki is a condition by consensus. This is the answer to a question. The question is: The defendant's tazkiyah of the witnesses is effectively an acknowledgment of the plaintiff's right, and for an acknowledgeer, 'adalah is not a condition by consensus, so even if the defendant is fasiq, his tazkiyah should be accepted. The answer is that the issue's form is when the defendant says 'these witnesses are 'udul but they erred or forgot,' and it is clear that such speech is not an acknowledgment of any right; rather it is a tazkiyah of witnesses, and it has already been established that the tazkiyah-maker must be 'adl. So the defendant's 'adalah is also a condition. Since the defendant is lying and non-'adl in the belief of the plaintiff and his witnesses because of his denial, his tazkiyah is not acceptable. But if the defendant says 'the plaintiff's witnesses are children' or says 'they are 'adil children,' then he has effectively acknowledged the plaintiff's right, and the judge will decide based on the acknowledgment, not the witnesses' testimony.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage, from Ashraf ul-Hidayah, discusses the condition of 'adalah (uprightness) for the one who certifies the integrity of witnesses (muzakki). It first states the general rule: the muzzaki must be 'adl. Then it clarifies a specific scenario: if the defendant (mudda'a 'alayh) himself acts as muzzaki for the plaintiff's witnesses, his tazkiyah is only acceptable if the defendant himself is 'adl. The reason is that the plaintiff and his witnesses inevitably view the defendant as a liar due to his denial of the claim, so they cannot consider him 'adl. This is a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) based on the necessary implications of the dispute. The passage then addresses an objection: the defendant's statement that the witnesses are 'udul might be seen as an acknowledgment of the claim, and acknowledgment does not require 'adalah. The response explains that the scenario in question is when the defendant adds that the witnesses 'erred or forgot,' which makes it a tazkiyah, not an acknowledgment. Thus the defendant's 'adalah is required. However, if the defendant says the witnesses are 'children' (meaning immature or incapable of testimony), that amounts to an acknowledgment of the claim, and the judge rules on that basis. This nuanced ruling shows the Hanafi school's attention to the precise wording and context in legal proceedings.

Key Terms
معدل (mu'addil): The person who certifies the 'adalah of witnesses; also called muzzaki.
تعدیل (ta'dil): The act of declaring witnesses as 'udul (just).
عادل ('adil): A person with upright character, free from major sins and persistent minor sins, and not lacking in virtue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the defendant says about the plaintiff's witnesses, 'They are 'udul but they erred or forgot,' how does the judge treat this statement?
A) As an acknowledgment of the claim, so the judge rules for the plaintiff.
B) As a valid tazkiyah only if the defendant himself is 'adl.
C) As a rejection of the witnesses, so the plaintiff must bring new witnesses.
D) As irrelevant, because the defendant is a party to the case.

Key Takeaway
The muzzaki's own 'adalah is a non-negotiable condition for tazkiyah to be valid, even if the muzzaki is the defendant; only clear acknowledgment bypasses this requirement.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Number of Muzzakis: One or Two Required
Dispute on required number of persons for tazkiyah of witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the required number of muzzakis, identify the proofs for each view, and explain why the mufta bihi is one muzzaki.

Core Idea
One muzzaki suffices in Hanafi school; the requirement of two is not transferred from testimony.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a practical question in judicial procedure: how many people are needed to certify the reliability of witnesses? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that one muzzaki is sufficient, while Imam Muhammad requires two. This dispute hinges on whether tazkiyah is considered a form of testimony. The lesson unpacks the proofs and shows the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds according to the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and according to Imam Muhammad.
Note that both views are within the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam Muhammad is the opponent here; also note that other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, one narration of Ahmad) agree with Muhammad.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine Imam Muhammad's dalil: tazkiyah is in the meaning of testimony because the judge's authority depends on 'adalah established through tazkiyah, and the judge's authority derives from testimony qualifications.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Sahibayn's rebuttal: tazkiyah lacks the formal requirements of testimony (specific wording, court session), so the condition of number is a specific ruling limited to testimony that does not extend to tazkiyah.
The Sahibayn restrict the analogy.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Appreciate the practical consequence: if only one muzzaki is available, the court can proceed according to the Sahibayn but not according to Muhammad. The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is the Sahibayn's view.
This affects efficiency of judicial proceedings.

مز کی شہود کی تعداد ، اقوال فقہاء
قال واذا كان رسول القاضى الذى يسأل عن الشهود واحد اجاز والاثنان افضل وهذا عند ابي حنيفة و ابي يوسف وقال محمد لا يجوز الا اثنان والمراد منه المزكى وعلى هذا الخلاف رسول القاضي الى المزكي والمترجم عن الشاهد له ان التزكية فى معنى الشهادة لان ولاية القضاء تبتنى على ظهور العدالة وهو بالتزكية فيشترط فيه العدد كما يشترط العدالة فيه و تشترط الذكورة فى المذكى في الحدود والقصاص ولهما انه ليس في معنى الشهادة ولهذا لا يشترط فيه لفظة الشهادة و مجلس القضاء واشتراط العدد امر حكمى فى الشهادة فلا يتعداها

ترجمہ اور جب قاضی کا ایسا قاصد (مرکی ) جس سے گواہوں کا حال دریافت کیا جائیگا۔ ایک ہو تو جائز ہے اور دو افضل ہیں۔ اور یہ البوحنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ہے اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ جائز نہیں مگر دو اور اس سے مراد مز کی ہے اور اسی اختلاف پر قاضی کا اینچی ہے جو مزکی کے پاس بھیجا ہے۔ اور گواہ کا بیان ترجمہ کر نیوالے میں ہے۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تعدیل کرنا گواہی کے معنی میں ہے۔ اس لئے مہ ولایت قضاء، عدالت ظاہر ہونے پر مبنی ہے اور ظہور عدالت چونکہ تزکیہ اور تعدیل سے ہوتا ہے اس لئے تعدیل میں عدد شرط ہو گا جیسا کہ اس میں عدالت شرط ہے اور ( جیسے ) حدود و قصاص کے گواہوں کی تعدیل کر نیو الے کا مذکر ہونا شرط ہے۔ اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تزکیہ ، شہادت کے معنی میں نہیں ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے تزکیہ میں لفظ شہادت اور مجلس قضا شرط نہیں ہے۔ اور شہادت میں عدد کا شرط ہونا ایک امرضی ہے۔ لہذاوہ شہادت سے متجاوز نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح بدر الدین عینی ،علامہ ابن الہام اور صاحب عنایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ متن میں لفظ يُسأل مجہول کا صیغہ ہے ۔ اور الذی يُسال عن الشهو درسول کی صفت اور اس کی تفسیر ہے۔ معنی ہوں گے قاضی کا ایسا قاصد جس سے گواہوں کے بارے میں دریافت کیا جائے گا۔ اور جس سے گواہوں کے بارے میں دریافت کیا جاتا ہے۔ وہ منز کی اور معدل کہلاتا ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ متین ہیں۔ رسول سے مراد وہ مز کی ہے جس سے قاضی گواہوں کا حال دریافت کرے گا۔ اب حاصل مسئلہ یہ ہو گا ۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام - البو یوسف کے نزدیک تزکیہ میں ایک شخص کا ہونا کافی ہے۔ یعنی اگر گواہوں کا حال دریافت کرنے کے لئے قاضی نے ایک شخص کو مز کی مقرر کیا ہو تو جائز ہے۔ مگر دو کا ہونا افضل ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر قاضی نے مزکی کی طرف ایک شخص کو قاصد بنا کر بھیجایا مزکی نے قاضی کی طرف ایک شخص کو قاصد بنا کر بھیجا تو جائز ہے۔ اور اسی طرح گواہ کے بیان کا ترجمہ کرنے والا اگر ایک آدمی ہو تو جائز ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح تزکیہ اور تعدیل کرنے کے لئے ایک شخص کا ہونا کافی ہے دو کا ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح قاضی سے مزکی کی طرف اور - مزگی سے قاضی کی طرف پیغام رسانی کے لئے اور گواہ کے بیان کا ترجمہ کرنے کے لئے دو شخصوں کا ہونا ضروری ہے ۔ یہی امام شافعی کا قول ہے۔ اس کے قاتل امام مالک ہیں۔ اور امام احمد کی ایک روایت بھی یہ ہے ۔ حضرت امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ تزکیہ اور پیغام رسانی اور گواہ کے بیان کا ترجمہ کرنے کیلئے دو شخصوں کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ یہی امام شافعی کا قول ہے اور امام احمد کی ایک روایت بھی
یہی ہے۔
امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ترکیہ اور تعدیل کرنا شہادت کے معنی میں ہے کیونکہ قاضی کی ولایت ، گواہوں کی عدالت ظاہر ہونے پر موقوف ہے یعنی جب گواہوں کی عدالت ظاہر ہو جائیگی ، تب قاضی قضاء اور فیصلہ کرنے کا مجاز ہوگا ۔ اور گواہوں کی عدالت کا ظاہر ہونا تزکیہ اور تعدیل پر موقوف ہے یعنی گواہونی کا عادل ہونا اسوقت ظاہر ہو گا جب مزکی ان کی تعدیل اور تزکیہ کرے گا۔ پس جب ولایت قضاء، عدالت ظاہر ہونے پر موقوف ہوئی اور گواہوں کی عدالت کا ظاہر ہونا، تزکیہ پر موقوف ہوا تو نتیجہ کے طور پر ثابت ہوا کہ ولایت قضاء، تزکیہ اور تعدیل پر موقوف ہے اور ولایت قضاء مستفاد ہے ولایت شہادت سے یعنی قاضی بنے کا اہل وہی شخص ہو گا جو شہادت کا اہل ہوتا ہے۔ پس جب ولایت قضاء تزکیہ پر موقوف ہے تو ولایت شہادت بھی تزکیہ پر موقوف ہوگی، یعنی گواہ گواہی دینے کے اہل اسی وقت قرار پائیں گے جب مزکی ان کے عادل ہو نیکی شہادت دیگا اور جب گواہوں کا گواہی دینا اسپر موقوف ہے کہ مزکی گواہوں کے عادل ہونے کی شہادت دے تو مزکی کا تزکیہ، شہادت کے ہم معنی ہوا اور جب تزکیہ شہادت کے معنی میں ہوا تو تزکیہ کے لئے وہی شرطیں ہوں گی
Number of muzzakis: statements of jurists. He said: 'And when the messenger of the judge who asks about the witnesses is one, it is permissible, and two are better. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: It is not permissible except two.' And by this is meant the muzzaki, and on this same disagreement are the messenger of the judge to the muzzaki and the translator of the witness. His (Muhammad's) proof is that tazkiyah is in the meaning of testimony because the authority of judging depends on the manifestation of 'adalah, and it is by tazkiyah, so number is required in it just as 'adalah is required in it, and masculinity [of the muzzaki] in hudud and qisas is required. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) that it is not in the meaning of testimony, therefore the wording of testimony and the court session are not required in it. And the requirement of number is a ruling matter in testimony, so it does not extend beyond it. Translation: And when the judge's messenger from whom the condition of witnesses is inquired is one, it is permissible, and two are better. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad said it is not permissible except two. And by this is meant the muzzaki. And on this same disagreement is the judge's messenger sent to the muzzaki and the translator of the witness. Imam Muhammad's proof is that ta'dil is in the meaning of testimony because the authority of judging is based on the manifestation of 'adalah, and the manifestation of 'adalah occurs through tazkiyah and ta'dil, so number is required in ta'dil just as 'adalah is required in it, and (like) the muzzaki in hudud and qisas must be male. And the Sahibayn's proof is that tazkiyah is not in the meaning of testimony; therefore the wording of testimony and the court session are not required in tazkiyah. And the requirement of number is a ruling matter specific to testimony, so it does not extend beyond it. Explanation: Badr al-Din al-Ayni, Allama Ibn al-Humam, and Sahib al-'Inaya said that in the matn, the word 'yus'alu' is in the passive form. And 'alladhi yus'alu 'an al-shuhud' is a description of 'rasul' and its interpretation. The meaning: the judge's messenger from whom inquiry about the witnesses will be made. And the one from whom inquiry is made is called muzzaki and mu'addil. So it is known that by 'rasul' is meant the muzzaki from whom the judge will inquire about the witnesses. Now the conclusion of the issue: According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, one person is sufficient for tazkiyah. That is, if the judge appoints one person as muzzaki to inquire about the witnesses, it is permissible, but two is better. Similarly, if the judge sends one person as a messenger to the muzzaki, and the muzzaki sends one person as a messenger to the judge, it is permissible. Likewise, if the translator of the witness's statement is one person, it is permissible. That is, just as for tazkiyah and ta'dil one person suffices and two are not necessary, similarly for messaging from judge to muzzaki and from muzzaki to judge, and for translating the witness's statement, two persons are required. This is the same as the view of Imam Shafi'i; its proponent is Imam Malik, and one narration from Imam Ahmad is also this. Imam Malik said that for tazkiyah, messaging, and translation, two persons are required. This is the same as Imam Shafi'i's view, and one narration from Imam Ahmad is also this. Imam Muhammad's proof is that tazkiyah and ta'dil are in the meaning of testimony because the authority of judging depends on the manifestation of the witnesses' 'adalah, i.e., when their 'adalah becomes manifest, the judge is authorized to judge. And the manifestation of the witnesses' 'adalah depends on tazkiyah and ta'dil. So when the authority of judging depends on the manifestation of 'adalah, and the manifestation of 'adalah depends on tazkiyah, the result is that the authority of judging depends on tazkiyah. And the authority of judging is derived from the authority of testimony; that is, the one eligible to be a judge is the one who is eligible to testify. So when the authority of judging depends on tazkiyah, then the authority of testimony also depends on tazkiyah. That is, the witnesses become eligible to testify only when the muzzaki testifies to their 'adalah. And since the witnesses' testifying depends on the muzzaki's testimony of their 'adalah, the muzzaki's tazkiyah is synonymous with testimony. And when tazkiyah is synonymous with testimony, the same conditions apply to tazkiyah [as to testimony].
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf ul-Hidayah addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: how many people are required to perform tazkiyah (certification of witnesses' integrity)? The matn states that according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, one muzzaki is sufficient, though two is better. Imam Muhammad, however, requires two muzzakis. The disagreement extends to the messenger sent to the muzzaki and the translator of the witness's statement. Imam Muhammad's proof (dalil) is that tazkiyah is effectively testimony (shahada) because the judge's authority to decide cases depends on the manifest 'adalah of witnesses, and that 'adalah is established through tazkiyah. Since the judge's authority is derived from the same qualification as testimony, and testimony requires two witnesses, tazkiyah also requires two. The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that tazkiyah is not the same as testimony because the formal requirements of testimony (specific wording, court session) are not necessary in tazkiyah. The requirement of two witnesses is a specific ruling ('amr hukmi) confined to testimony and does not extend to tazkiyah. The commentary then cites later Hanafi authorities (Ayni, Ibn al-Humam, Sahib al-'Inaya) who clarify the wording of the matn and elaborate that the same ikhtilaf applies to messengers and translators. Interestingly, the passage also notes that other schools (Shafi'i, Malik, and one narration from Ahmad) require two for tazkiyah, messaging, and translation. Despite Imam Muhammad's view, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that one muzzaki suffices, as it is the view of the Sahibayn and is more practical. This lesson illustrates how a seemingly procedural issue can have significant practical implications for the administration of justice.

Key Terms
مزکی (muzakki): The person who performs tazkiyah, certifying the 'adalah of witnesses.
تزکیہ (tazkiyah): The act of certifying the integrity of witnesses; also called ta'dil.
رسول القاضی (rasul al-qadi): The messenger sent by the judge to the muzzaki to inquire about the witnesses' condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), how many muzzakis are required to certify witnesses?
A) Two muzzakis are required.
B) One muzzaki suffices, and two is better.
C) Three muzzakis are required.
D) No muzzaki is needed; the judge can decide based on personal knowledge.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, one muzzaki suffices for tazkiyah because the number requirement of testimony does not transfer to tazkiyah.

Number of Persons Required for Tazkiyah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on number required for tazkiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the number of muzakkis required for tazkiyah and explain the qiyas argument that supports the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
One reliable person suffices to validate a witness — the number requirement for testimony does not extend to tazkiyah.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: how many people are needed to certify that a witness is upright? While Imam Muhammad insists on two, the founding imams of the school allow one. Understanding why the Shaykhayn’s view prevailed requires a precise grasp of how qiyas operates — and when it cannot override a textual exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
Tazkiyah is the process of declaring witnesses upright. The dispute centers on the number of muzakkis (persons performing tazkiyah) required.
2
State the Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Shaykhayn) hold that one muzakki suffices, though two are better. Imam Muhammad holds that two are required.
3
Examine Imam Muhammad's proof
Imam Muhammad argues that tazkiyah is akin to shahada because the judge's authority depends on establishing the witnesses' uprightness. Thus, the conditions of shahada, including the number two, apply.
He also notes consistency: in hudud and qisas, the muzakki must be male, just as witnesses must be male.
4
Analyze the Shaykhayn's response
The Shaykhayn respond that tazkiyah is not shahada; it does not require the formalities of a court or the word 'shahada'. The requirement of two witnesses in shahada is established by the Quran (2:282) contrary to qiyas, and such rulings cannot be extended to tazkiyah.
Key rule: What is established by nas contrary to qiyas does not extend to other cases.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Shaykhayn: one muzakki suffices. The practical consequence: a judge's appointment of a single muzakki is valid.

دو کے عدد سے نہ تو یقین حاصل ہوتا ہے اور نہ عمل کرنا ثابت ہوتا ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ قیاس ، شہادت میں دو کے عدد کا تقاضہ نہیں کرتا ہے بلکہ دو کا عدد شہادت میں خلاف قیاس نص سے ثابت ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جو چیز نص سے خلاف قیاس ثابت ہو وہ دوسرے کی طرف متعدی اور متجاوز نہیں ہوتی پس عدد یعنی دو کا ہونا شہادت سے تزکیہ کی طرف متعدی اور متجاوز نہیں ہوگا اور تزکیہ میں عدد یعنی دو مر کیوں کا ہونا شرط نہ ہوگا۔
Translation: When the judge sends a messenger to inquire about the witnesses, one person is permissible, and two are better. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad said: Not permissible except with two. And this refers to the muzakki (validator). Similarly, the judge's messenger sent to the muzakki, and the interpreter of the witness's statement. Imam Muhammad's proof is that ta'dil (declaring uprightness) is in the meaning of shahada (testimony). Therefore, since the authority of qada depends on the manifestation of uprightness, and the manifestation of uprightness occurs through tazkiyah and ta'dil, so number is required in ta'dil just as uprightness is required. Similarly, in the ta'dil of witnesses for hudud and qisas, masculinity is required. The proof of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that tazkiyah is not in the meaning of shahada. For this reason, the word 'shahada' and the presence of the court are not required in tazkiyah. And the requirement of number in shahada is a matter of nas (textual evidence). Therefore, it does not extend beyond shahada. Explanation: Badr al-Din al-Ayni, Allama Ibn al-Humam, and Sahib al-'Inaya said that the word 'yus'alu' in the matn is in the passive form, and 'alladhi yus'alu 'an al-shuhud' is a description of the messenger, meaning the judge's messenger who will be asked about the witnesses. The one asked about the witnesses is called muzakki and mu'addil. Thus the ruling: Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf hold that one person suffices for tazkiyah; two are better. Similarly, if the judge sends one messenger to the muzakki and the muzakki sends one messenger to the judge, it is permissible. And similarly, one interpreter for the witness's statement suffices. However, Imam Muhammad holds that two are required for tazkiyah. This is also the view of Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and one narration from Imam Ahmad. Imam Muhammad's proof: Tazkiyah and ta'dil are in the meaning of shahada because the judge's authority is dependent on the manifestation of the witnesses' uprightness, which is achieved through tazkiyah. Since qada's authority is derived from shahada's authority, the conditions of shahada apply to tazkiyah. Thus, just as shahada requires two witnesses, tazkiyah requires two muzakkis. Hence, in hudud and qisas, the muzakkis must be male, and in zina, four muzakkis are required. The proof of the two shaykhs: Tazkiyah is not in the meaning of shahada because the word 'shahada' is not used and the presence of the court is not required. Even if we accept that some conditions of shahada apply, the requirement of number in shahada is established by nas (the verse 'wastashhidu shahidayn min rijalikum') contrary to qiyas. Qiyas does not require two witnesses because even with two, the possibility of falsehood remains; certainty comes from tawatur and the preponderance of truth comes from uprightness, not number. A rule: What is established by nas contrary to qiyas does not extend to other cases. Therefore, the number requirement does not transfer from shahada to tazkiyah.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of persons required for tazkiyah (validation of witnesses). The author presents the positions of the three major Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) hold that one person suffices, while Imam Muhammad requires two. The commentary elaborates on their proofs. Imam Muhammad argues that tazkiyah is essentially a form of shahada because the judge's authority to adjudicate depends on the witnesses' uprightness being established through tazkiyah; thus the conditions of shahada apply, including the requirement of two witnesses. The Shaykhayn respond that tazkiyah is not shahada—it does not require the formalities of a court or the word 'shahada'. The requirement of two witnesses in shahada is established by the Quranic verse (2:282) contrary to qiyas, and such a ruling cannot be extended to tazkiyah by analogy. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school: one reliable person suffices for tazkiyah.

Key Terms
تزکیہ (tazkiyah): The process of declaring witnesses upright and reliable.
تعدیل (ta'dil): Synonym for tazkiyah; declaring witnesses 'adil (upright).
مزکی (muzakki): The person who performs tazkiyah; the validator of witnesses.
شہادت (shahada): Testimony given in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), how many muzakkis are required for tazkiyah?
A) Four muzakkis are required for all cases.
B) Two muzakkis are required.
C) One muzakki suffices; two are better.
D) No muzakki is needed; the judge may rely on personal knowledge.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, one reliable person suffices for tazkiyah; the two-witness requirement for testimony is a textual exception that does not extend by analogy.

Conditions of Muzakki in Secret vs. Public Tazkiyah
Clarifying eligibility and number requirements for muzakki

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the conditions of the muzakki in secret and public tazkiyah and apply the Hanafi ruling on eligibility and number requirement.

Core Idea
Secret tazkiyah: any 'adil person qualifies; public tazkiyah: eligibility and certain number required.

This lesson clarifies the key differences between secret and public tazkiyah in Hanafi fiqh regarding who can serve as muzakki and how many are needed. Understanding these conditions is crucial for proper witness validation in court proceedings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of tazkiyah
Determine whether the tazkiyah is conducted secretly (outside court) or publicly (in court). This affects all subsequent conditions.
Secret tazkiyah is informal; public tazkiyah is part of the court session.
2
Check eligibility requirement for muzakki
In secret tazkiyah, the muzakki need not possess ahliyyat al-shahada (eligibility to testify). In public tazkiyah, it is a condition.
A slave, who lacks full eligibility, can be a muzakki in secret but not in public.
3
Apply number requirement for muzakkis
In public tazkiyah, a specific number of muzakkis is required by consensus (generally two). In secret tazkiyah, one suffices.
Al-Khassaf is cited for the consensus on number requirement in public tazkiyah.
4
Note the exception for zina witnesses
According to Imam Muhammad, the tazkiyah of witnesses in a zina case requires four muzakkis, matching the number of witnesses needed for zina. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that two suffice.
This intra-Hanafi difference affects only public tazkiyah for zina witnesses.
5
Distinguish the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is the majority view: in secret tazkiyah, one muzakki with 'adala suffices, no eligibility required; in public tazkiyah, eligibility and two muzakkis are required (except for zina where two suffice).
Imam Muhammad's view on four is a minority and not practiced.

ولا يشترط اهلية الشهادة فى المركى فى تزكية السر حتى صلح العبد مزكيا فاما في تزكية العلانية فهو شرط وكذا العدد بالاجماع على ما قاله الخصاف لاختصاصها بمجلس القضاء قالوا يشترط الاربعة في زكية شهود الزناء عند محمد. ترجمہ اور خفیہ تزکیہ میں مزکی کے اندر شہادت کی اہلیت کا ہونا شرط نہیں ہے حتی کہ غلام کا مزکی ہونا جائز ہے۔ بہر حال تزکیہ علانیہ میں تو یہ شرط ہے اور ایسے ہی بالا جماع عدد شرط ہے اس بناء پر جس کو خصاف نے کہا ہے کیونکہ علانیہ تعدیل مجلس قضاء کیساتھ مختص ہے۔ اور مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ امام محمد کے نزدیک زنا کے گواہوں کی تعدیل کرنے میں چار مردوں کا ہونا شرط ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ خفیہ تعدیل و تزکیہ کی صورت میں مزکی کا شہادت کی اہلیت رکھنا شرط نہیں ہے یعنی جس شخص کو مز کی مقرر کیا گیا ہے اس کا اہل شہادت میں سے ہونا شرط نہیں ہے اگر چہ عادل ہونا شرط ہے چنانچہ غلام کا مز کی ہونا جائز ہے پس اگر
And the eligibility for shahada is not required in the muzakki in secret tazkiyah, so much so that a slave is valid as a muzakki. As for public tazkiyah, it is a condition. And similarly, number is required by consensus, according to what al-Khassaf said, because public tazkiyah is specific to the court. They said: According to Muhammad, four are required in the tazkiyah of witnesses of zina. Translation: In secret tazkiyah, the muzakki's eligibility for shahada is not required; even a slave may serve as muzakki. However, in public tazkiyah, it is a condition. Similarly, number is required by consensus, as al-Khassaf stated, because public tazkiyah is specific to the court. The mashayikh said that according to Imam Muhammad, the ta'dil of witnesses of zina requires four men. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that in secret ta'dil and tazkiyah, the muzakki need not possess eligibility for shahada; that is, the person appointed as muzakki need not be among those eligible to be witnesses, although he must be 'adil. Thus, a slave may serve as muzakki. Then...
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between secret and public tazkiyah. In secret tazkiyah (where the inquiry is conducted discreetly, not in court), the muzakki does not need to be eligible to serve as a witness. For example, a slave, who is generally not eligible to be a witness in certain cases, can act as a muzakki in secret. In public tazkiyah (conducted in the court), the muzakki must be eligible to be a witness. Additionally, the number of muzakkis is required by consensus in public tazkiyah, as it is attached to the court session. Imam Muhammad goes further, requiring four muzakkis for the tazkiyah of witnesses in a zina case, matching the number of witnesses required for zina itself. This shows the principle that the conditions of the original shahada may apply to its tazkiyah, especially in public and in serious cases like zina.

Key Terms
خفیہ تزکیہ (tazkiyah siriya): Secret tazkiyah conducted privately, outside the court.
علانیہ تزکیہ (tazkiyah alaniya): Public tazkiyah conducted in the court session.
اہلیت شہادت (ahliyyat al-shahada): Legal capacity to serve as a witness (free, adult, Muslim, 'adil).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which type of tazkiyah is the muzakki not required to possess eligibility for shahada?
A) Public tazkiyah
B) Secret tazkiyah
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Secret tazkiyah requires only 'adala in the muzakki; public tazkiyah requires ahliyyat al-shahada and number (generally two).

Shahadat — Testimony

The Requirement of Number in Testimony Does Not Extend to Tazkiyah
Arguing that two validators are not required in tazkiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not require two validators in tazkiyah and apply the principle that rulings established by nass against qiyas do not extend by analogy.

Core Idea
The number two in testimony is a textual exception, not a general rule; it does not apply to tazkiyah.

In this passage, the author addresses a common confusion: since testimony (shahada) requires at least two witnesses, one might think that the process of validating witnesses (tazkiyah) also requires two validators. However, the Hanafi position is different. You will learn the key distinction and the usul principle that justifies it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent analogy
Recognize the initial argument: because tazkiyah is similar to shahada, it seems logical to require two validators.
This is the position that the text refutes.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that two validators are not required in tazkiyah.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof for the number condition in shahada is the Quranic verse 2:282: 'And call to witness two witnesses from among your men.'
Text is quoted in the passage.
4
Analyse wajh al-dalalah
Understand that this requirement is khilaf al-qiyas. Normally, a single just witness should suffice for establishing truth, as in hadith narration. The number two is an exception established by nass.
The passage explains that number does not eliminate falsehood; justice does.
5
Apply the usul principle
A ruling established by nass contrary to qiyas does not extend to other matters. Therefore, the number condition does not transfer from shahada to tazkiyah.
This is the decisive principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة جو شرطیں شہادت کیلئے ہیں۔ اور شہادت میں جس طرح گواہوں کا عادل ہونا شرط ہے اسی طرح گواہوں کا کم از کم دو ہونا بھی شرط ہے پس جب گواہوں کا شہادت میں کم از کم دو ہونا شرط ہے تو تزکیہ جو شہادت کے ہم معنی ہے اس میں بھی کم از کم دو مزکیوں کا ہونا شرط ہوگا یہی وجہ ہے کہ حدود و قصاص میں چونکہ گواہوں کا مذکر ہونا شرط ہے تو ائمہ اربعہ کا اسپر اتفاق ہے کہ حدود و قصاص کے گواہوں کے تزکیہ اور تعدیل کرنے والوں کا بھی ذکر ہونا شرط ہے۔ حد زنا میں چونکہ گواہوں کا چار ہونا ضروری ہے تو ان کے مزکیوں کا بھی چار ہونا ضروری ہوگا۔ یخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تزکیہ، شہادت کے معنی میں نہیں ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ تزکیہ میں نہ لفظ شہادت شرط ہے اور نہ مجلس قضاء شرط ہے حالانکہ یہ دونوں باتیں شہادت میں شرط ہیں پس جب تزکیہ شہادت کے معنی میں نہیں تو تزکیہ میں وہ چیزیں بھی شرط نہ ہوں گی جو شہادت میں شرط ہیں اور اگر ہم یہ تسلیم بھی کر لیں کہ تزکیہ میں اتنی چیزیں شرط ہیں جو شہادت میں شرط ہیں تو مزکیوں کا دو ہونا تب بھی ثابت نہ ہو گا ۔ کیونکہ شہادت میں عدد یعنی دو ہونے کی شرط خلاف قیاس نص واستشهدوا شهيدين من رجالکم سے ثابت ہے ورنہ قیاسی کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ شہادت میں عدد دو کا ہونا شرط نہ ہو کیوں کہ گواہ اگر ایک کے بجائے دو ہوں تو کذب کا احتمال تب بھی رہتا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ کذب کا بالکلیہ انقطاع تو تواتر سے ہوتا ہے اور رہا صدق کا راجح ہونا تو وہ عدالت سے ہو جاتا ہے جیسے روایت حدیث میں ایک عادل آدمی کی حدیث بھی قبول کی جاتی ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ رجحان صدق عدد سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ عدالت سے ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ یقین تو تواتر سے حاصل ہوتا ہے اور عمل ایک عادل کی خبر سے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے نہیں دو کے عدد سے نہ تو یقین حاصل ہوتا ہے اور نہ عمل کرنا ثابت ہوتا ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ قیاس ، شہادت میں دو کے عدد کا تقاضہ نہیں کرتا ہے بلکہ دو کا عدد شہادت میں خلاف قیاس نص سے ثابت ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جو چیز نص سے خلاف قیاس ثابت ہو وہ دوسرے کی طرف متعدی اور متجاوز نہیں ہوتی پس عدد یعنی دو کا ہونا شہادت سے تزکیہ کی طرف متعدی اور متجاوز نہیں ہوگا اور تزکیہ میں عدد یعنی دو مر کیوں کا ہونا شرط نہ ہوگا۔
The Book of Testimony. The conditions for testimony. And just as in testimony the witnesses being just is a condition, similarly the witnesses being at least two is also a condition. So when in testimony the minimum of two witnesses is a condition, then tazkiyah, which is synonymous with testimony, should also require at least two validators. This is why in hudud and qisas, since the witnesses being male is a condition, the four Imams agree that the validators of the witnesses in hudud and qisas must also be male. In hadd zina, since four witnesses are required, their validators must also be four. Yaheen's proof is that tazkiyah is not in the meaning of testimony. For this reason, in tazkiyah neither the word 'shahada' is a condition nor is the court session a condition, although both are conditions in testimony. So when tazkiyah is not in the meaning of testimony, then those things which are conditions in testimony will not be conditions in tazkiyah. And even if we concede that all those things are conditions in tazkiyah, the requirement of two validators would still not be proven. Because the condition of number, i.e., two, in testimony is established by the text 'And call to witness two witnesses from among your men' (Quran 2:282), contrary to qiyas. Otherwise, qiyas would require that the number two is not a condition in testimony, because even if there are two witnesses instead of one, the possibility of falsehood still remains. The complete elimination of falsehood occurs only through tawatur, and the preponderance of truth is achieved through justice, just as in hadith narration the report of a single just person is accepted. So it is known that the preponderance of truth is not established by number but by justice. The conclusion is that certainty is obtained through tawatur, and action is established by the report of a single just person. Neither is certainty obtained from the number two, nor is action established. So it is established that qiyas does not require the number two in testimony; rather, the number two in testimony is established by text contrary to qiyas. The principle is that whatever is established by text contrary to qiyas does not transfer to others. So the number two from testimony will not transfer to tazkiyah, and the requirement of two validators will not be a condition in tazkiyah.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the number of validators in tazkiyah. The author begins by stating the apparent analogy: since shahada requires two witnesses, and tazkiyah is similar to shahada, one might think tazkiyah also requires two validators. However, the correct Hanafi position is that two validators are not required in tazkiyah. The proof is that the requirement of two witnesses in shahada is established by Quranic text against qiyas. The text is the verse 'واستشهدوا شهيدين من رجالكم' (Quran 2:282). Qiyas would not require two, because a single just witness should suffice, as in hadith narration where a single just person's report is accepted. Therefore, this requirement is a dispensation from the norm. The legal principle is that a ruling established by nass against qiyas does not extend to other matters. Thus, the number condition does not transfer from shahada to tazkiyah. The passage also notes that according to the four Imams, the requirement of male witnesses in hudud and qisas extends to their validators, because that condition is not against qiyas? Actually the text says the Imams agree that validators for hudud witnesses must also be male. For zina, since four witnesses are needed, four validators would be needed. But the main point is about number, not gender.

Key Terms
تزکیہ (tazkiyah): The process of validating the character and credibility of witnesses; equivalent to ta'dil.
شہادت (shahada): Testimony given in court; the act of bearing witness.
عدد (adad): Number; specifically the requirement of at least two witnesses in shahada.
خلاف قیاس (khilaf al-qiyas): A ruling that contradicts the apparent analogy; established by nass despite the qiyas indicating otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because tazkiyah is not considered a form of testimony.

C) Because Imam Abu Hanifa considered one validator sufficient in all cases.
D) Because the Quran explicitly states that one validator is enough.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms that the condition of two witnesses in testimony is a textual exception and does not extend to the validation process (tazkiyah).

Conditions for Validators in Secret and Open Tazkiyah
Explaining the differing conditions for secret and open tazkiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for validators in secret and open tazkiyah and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of validators.

Core Idea
In secret tazkiyah, even a slave can be a validator; in open tazkiyah, eligibility to testify is required, but whether two validators are needed is debated within the Hanafi school.

This passage delves into the rules governing tazkiyah (witness verification), distinguishing between secret and open procedures. The key question is whether the validator must be eligible to testify and how many validators are needed. The Hanafi school has nuanced positions, with Imam al-Khassaf requiring two validators in open tazkiyah, while others disagree. Understanding these details is crucial for judges and students of judicial procedure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of tazkiyah
The passage distinguishes secret (khafī) and open (ʿalāniyya) tazkiyah. Recognize that different conditions apply.
2
State the condition for secret tazkiyah
Eligibility for testimony is not required; only justice (ʿadāla) is needed. Thus a slave can be a validator.
A slave cannot testify for his master but can validate him secretly.
3
State the condition for open tazkiyah
Eligibility for testimony is required. According to al-Khassaf, two validators are needed by consensus; but this is contested.
4
Analyze the objection and response
The objection is inconsistency if the same person does both secret and open. The response: al-Khassaf holds they are different persons; the preferred view holds the same person does both, so number is not required.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The preferred Hanafi view is that number is not required in either type, and eligibility is not required in secret.
