مزکیوں کا ہونا ضروری ہوگا۔ جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Secret and open tazkiyah: is eligibility for testimony a condition in the validator or not? 'And eligibility for testimony is not a condition in the validator in secret tazkiyah, so much so that a slave is valid as a validator. As for open tazkiyah, it is a condition, and likewise number [is a condition] by consensus, according to what al-Khassaf said, because it is specific to the court session. They said: Four [validators] are required for the tazkiyah of witnesses of zina according to Muhammad.' Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri said that in the case of secret ta'dil and tazkiyah, it is not a condition that the validator possess eligibility for testimony; i.e., the person appointed as validator does not have to be among those eligible to testify, although being just is a condition. Thus, a slave may be a validator. So if the judge appoints a slave to validate his owner or another person, it is permissible. Similarly, if the judge appoints a father to validate his son, or a son to validate his father, it is permissible, even though a slave may not testify for his owner, nor a father for his son, nor a son for his father. However, in the case of open tazkiyah, the validator must be eligible for testimony. Similarly, according to Imam al-Khassaf, the validators in open tazkiyah must be two by consensus. Because open tazkiyah and ta'dil are specific to the court session. Being specific to the court session indicates that open ta'dil is in the meaning of testimony. And when open ta'dil is in the meaning of testimony, then just as in testimony, number is a condition in tazkiyah; i.e., at least two validators are required, and both validators must be eligible to testify. Objection: There is an objection that the requirement of number (two) in open tazkiyah contradicts the non-requirement of number in secret tazkiyah. Because the person who acts as a validator in secret would be the same who acts as a validator in open. So if secret tazkiyah does not require number, how can open tazkiyah require it? Or if open requires number, secret should also require it. Answer: The answer is that according to Imam al-Khassaf, the secret validator is different from the open validator; i.e., the one who does secret tazkiyah will not do open tazkiyah, and vice versa. Given that, it is possible that number is required in open but not in secret. And according to us, since the person who does secret ta'dil is the same who will also do open tazkiyah, therefore number (two) is not a condition in either secret or open tazkiyah. Sahib al-Hidayah said that because Imam Muhammad, regarding number, analogized tazkiyah to shahada, the mashayikh said that according to Imam Muhammad, for the tazkiyah and ta'dil of witnesses of zina, four validators are required. Just as four witnesses are required to prove zina, similarly for their tazkiyah, four validators are required. Jamil Ahmad 'Afā 'Anhu.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and ruling regarding the conditions for validators (muzakki) in tazkiyah. It distinguishes between secret (khafī) and open (ʿalāniyya) tazkiyah. The author begins by stating the rule: in secret tazkiyah, eligibility for testimony (ahliyat al-shahada) is not required in the validator; therefore, a slave can serve as a validator even though a slave cannot testify for his master. Similarly, a father can validate his son, etc. In open tazkiyah, however, eligibility for testimony is required. Additionally, according to Imam al-Khassaf, the number of validators in open tazkiyah must be two by consensus, because open tazkiyah is associated with the court session and is thus akin to testimony. The passage then raises an objection: if the same person serves as validator in both secret and open, then it is inconsistent to require two in open but not in secret. The answer is that according to al-Khassaf, the validators for secret and open are different persons; thus no inconsistency. However, according to the preferred Hanafi view (as per the author), the same person performs both, so number is not required in either. Finally, the passage notes that Imam Muhammad analogizes tazkiyah to shahada in number, and therefore he requires four validators for the witnesses of zina, just as four witnesses are needed to prove zina. This shows the range of views within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تزکیہ (tazkiyah): The process of verifying the integrity of witnesses; includes both secret (khafī) and open (ʿalāniyya) forms.
مزکی (muzakki): The person appointed to perform tazkiyah; the validator.
اہلیت شہادت (ahliyat al-shahada): The legal capacity to give testimony; includes being free, male (in some cases), just, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In secret tazkiyah, which of the following is NOT a condition for the validator (muzakki)?
A) Being just (ʿadl)
B) Being eligible to testify (ahliyat al-shahada)
C) Being a Muslim
D) Being of sound mind

Key Takeaway
The condition for validators in tazkiyah depends on whether it is secret or open: in secret, eligibility to testify is not required; in open, it is, but the number of validators is not required in the preferred Hanafi view.

The First Type of Testimony: Acts That Establish Their Own Ruling
Defining the first type of testimony that requires no formal appointment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the first type of testimony and explain why it does not require formal appointment, citing the Quranic and prophetic proofs.

Core Idea
If an act's legal effect is self-evident, the witness may testify without being summoned.

This lesson introduces a key category in the law of testimony: acts that carry their own legal consequences. The Hanafi school teaches that for certain events—like a sale, confession, or murder—the witness's direct knowledge suffices to permit testimony, even if no formal appointment was made. We will examine the ruling, its conditions, and the textual proofs from the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal effect
Read the list of examples (sale, confession, usurpation, murder, judge's verdict). Understand that these acts automatically create legal consequences without needing external validation.
The common feature is that the act itself indicates its own legal nature.
2
State the ruling for the witness
The passage says 'وسعه أن يشهد وإن لم يشهد عليه' – it is permissible for the witness to testify even if not appointed. This is the core ruling.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
The verse 'إلا من شهد بالحق وهم يعلمون' (43:86) is cited. The phrase 'وهم يعلمون' (while they know) indicates that knowledge is the basis for valid testimony.
The Hanafi usul holds that the exception implies the condition: testimony requires knowledge.
4
Analyze the prophetic proof
The hadith 'إذا علمت مثل الشمس فاشهد وإلا فدع' emphasizes certainty. Testimony must be based on clear, irrefutable knowledge.
The simile 'like the sun' underscores that doubt invalidates testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما يتحمله الشاهد على ضربين أحدهما ما يثبت حكمه بنفسه مثل البيع والإقرار والغصب والقتل وحكم الحاكم، فإذا سمع ذلك الشاهد أو رآه وسعه أن يشهد وإن لم يشهد عليه، لأنه علم ما هو الموجب بنفسه، وهو الركن في إطلاق الأداء. قال الله تعالى: {إلا من شهد بالحق وهم يعلمون} وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: 'إذا علمت مثل الشمس فاشهد وإلا فدع' ترجمہ گواہ جسکی گواہی اٹھاتا ہے دو قسم پر ہے۔ ان میں سے ایک وہ جس کا حکم بذات خود ثابت ہو جاتا ہے جیسے بیع ، اقرار غصب قبل اور حاکم کا حکم پس جب اس کو گواہ نے سنایا دیکھا تو اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ وہ گواہی دے اگر چہ وہ اس معاملہ پر گواہ نہ بنایا گیا ہو۔ کیونکہ گواہ کو وہ چیز معلوم ہوگئی ہے جو بذات خود موجب ہے، اور جانا ادائے شہادت کے جائز ہونے میں رکن ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ
'And what the witness bears witness to is of two types. One of them is that which establishes its own ruling by itself, such as sale, confession, usurpation, murder, and the ruling of a judge. So if that witness hears or sees it, it is permissible for him to testify even if he was not made a witness over it, because he knows what is the cause in itself, and that is the pillar in the permissibility of testifying. Allah Almighty said: 'Except one who testifies to the truth while they know' (Quran 43:86) and the Prophet ﷺ said: 'If you know it like the sun, then testify; otherwise, leave it.' Translation: The witness bears witness to two types. One is that which establishes its own ruling, like sale, confession, usurpation, murder, and the ruling of a judge. So when the witness heard or saw it, it is permissible for him to testify even if he was not made a witness over that matter. Because the witness has known that which is the cause in itself, and that is the pillar in the permissibility of performing testimony. Allah Almighty said: ...
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof defining the first type of testimony that a witness may bear. The author divides what a witness bears into two types. The first type includes acts whose legal effect is established by their very occurrence, such as sale (bayʿ), confession (iqrar), usurpation (ghasb), murder (qatl), and a judge's verdict (hukm al-hakim). In these cases, once the witness perceives the act (by hearing or seeing), he is permitted to testify even if he was not formally appointed as a witness. The reason is that he knows the underlying cause (al-mujib) of the legal effect, which is the pillar (rukn) for allowing testimony. The author supports this with two proofs: the Quranic verse 'Except one who testifies to the truth while they know' (Quran 43:86), which implies that knowledge is the basis for testimony, and the hadith 'If you know it like the sun, then testify; otherwise, leave it.' This hadith emphasizes that testimony must be based on certain knowledge, not conjecture. Thus, if a witness has direct knowledge of such an act, he may testify without being summoned, because the act itself generates the obligation to testify.

Key Terms
تحمل الشهادة (tahammul al-shahada): The act of bearing witness; what a witness undertakes to testify about.
الموجب (al-mujib): The cause or reason that necessitates the ruling; the intrinsic legal cause of the act.
الركن (al-rukn): The essential component; here, knowledge is the rukn that permits testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A witness who only heard rumors about a contract
B) A witness who saw a sale transaction take place
C) A witness who was told about a murder by a third party
D) A witness who has indirect knowledge of a judge's verdict

Key Takeaway
Testimony is valid if the witness has certain knowledge of a self-establishing act, even without formal appointment.

Appointment and Number of Verifiers in Tazkiyah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on number of verifiers for tazkiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on appointing a verifier even if he cannot testify for the subject, explain the condition for public tazkiyah, and contrast the intra-Hanafi positions on the number of verifiers required.

Core Idea
A verifier can be appointed even if he cannot testify, but public tazkiyah requires qualified witnesses; the number of verifiers is disputed: one, two, or four.

This passage addresses a key distinction between tazkiyah (witness verification) and shahadah (testimony). The qadi may appoint a verifier who would be ineligible to testify for the person being verified—such as a slave verifying his master. However, when the verification is conducted publicly in court, the verifier must be someone eligible to be a witness. The passage then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute about how many verifiers are needed. Imam al-Khasaf requires two for public tazkiyah, Imam Muhammad extends qiyas to require four for zina witnesses, but the preferred view (mufta bihi) is that a single verifier suffices in all cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the qadi appointing? What is the default ruling? The act is appointing a verifier (muzakki) for tazkiyah. The ruling is ja'iz (permissible). The examples of slave, father, son show the broad permissibility even though they cannot testify for those individuals.
Tazkiyah is not identical to shahadah.
2
Note the condition for public tazkiyah
For 'alaniyah (public) tazkiyah, the verifier must be eligible for shahadah (testimony). This condition does not apply to secret tazkiyah.
This condition is separate from the dispute on number.
3
State Imam al-Khasaf's position
Imam al-Khasaf requires two verifiers for public tazkiyah because it resembles testimony. He holds that secret and public verifiers are separate individuals.
This is based on the principle that public tazkiyah is specific to the court.
4
Understand the objection and answer
If the same person does both secret and public tazkiyah, requiring two for public but not secret is contradictory. Imam al-Khasaf's answer: the verifiers are different, so no contradiction. The preferred view rejects this distinction.
The preferred view holds that the same person does both, so number is not required in either.
5
Note Imam Muhammad's qiyas for zina witnesses
Imam Muhammad extends the qiyas: for zina witnesses, since four witnesses are needed, the tazkiyah of those witnesses also requires four verifiers.
This is an extension of the analogy to testimony.
6
Summarize the mufta bihi position
The text favors one verifier for all cases. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The commentator Ashraf al-Hidayah adopts this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاضی نے غلام کو خود اس کے مولیٰ یا دوسرے کسی آدمی کا تزکیہ اور تعدیل کرنے کے لئے مزکی مقرر کیا تو جائز ہے اسی طرح اگر باپ کو خود اس کے بیٹے کا تزکیہ کرنے کے لئے یا بیٹے کو خود اس کے باپ کا تزکیہ کرنے کے لیے مزکی مقرر کیا تو جائز ہے حالانکہ غلام کا اپنے مولیٰ کے حق میں اور باپ کا اپنے بیٹے کے حق میں اور بیٹے کا اپنے باپ کے حق میں شہادت دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ البتہ تزکیہ علانیہ کی صورت میں مزکی کا اہل شہادت میں سے ہونا شرط ہے۔ اسی طرح علانیہ طور پر تزکیہ کرنے والوں کا بقول امام خصاف کے بالاجماع دو ہونا شرط ہے۔ کیونکہ علانیہ تزکیہ اور تعدیل مجلس قضا کے ساتھ خاص ہے۔ اور مجلس قضا کے ساتھ مختص ہونا اس بات کی علامت ہے کہ علانیہ تعدیل شہادت کے معنی میں ہے اور جب علانیہ تعدیل شہادت کے معنی میں ہے تو شہادت کی طرح تزکیہ میں بھی عدد شرط ہوگا۔ یعنی کم از کم دو مزکیوں کا ہونا شرط ہوگا۔ اور دونوں مزکیوں کا شہادت کا اہل ہونا بھی ضروری ہوگا۔
اعتراض: یہاں ایک اعتراض ہے وہ یہ کہ علانیہ تزکیہ میں عدد (دو) کا شرط ہونا خفیہ تزکیہ میں عدد شرط نہ ہونے کے منافی ہے۔ یعنی علانیہ تزکیہ میں عدد کا شرط ہونا اور خفیہ تزکیہ میں عدد کا شرط نہ ہونا ان دونوں میں منافات ہے کیونکہ جو شخص خفیہ تزکیہ میں مزکی ہوتا ہے وہی علانیہ طور پر مزکی ہوگا پس جب خفیہ تزکیہ میں عدد شرط نہیں ہے تو علانیہ تزکیہ میں عدد کس طرح شرط ہوگا۔ یا جب علانیہ تزکیہ میں عدد شرط ہے تو خفیہ تزکیہ میں بھی عدد شرط ہونا چاہئے۔
جواب: اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ امام خصاف کے نزدیک یہ شرط ہے کہ خفیہ مزکی علانیہ مزکی کا غیر ہوتا ہے یعنی جو خفیہ مزکی ہوگا وہ علانیہ مزکی نہیں ہوگا۔ اور جو علانیہ مزکی ہوگا وہ خفیہ مزکی نہیں ہوگا اور جب یہ بات ہے تو ممکن ہے کہ علانیہ تزکیہ میں عدد شرط ہو اور خفیہ تزکیہ میں عدد شرط نہ ہو۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک جو شخص خفیہ تزکیہ و تعدیل کرتا ہے وہی شخص چونکہ علانیہ بھی تزکیہ کرے گا۔ اس لئے عدد (دو) کا ہونا نہ خفیہ تزکیہ میں شرط ہے اور نہ علانیہ تزکیہ میں شرط ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ امام محمد نے چونکہ عدد کے حق میں تزکیہ کو شہادت پر قیاس کیا ہے اس لئے مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ امام محمد کے نزدیک زنا کے گواہوں کا تزکیہ اور تعدیل کرنے کے لئے چار مزکیوں کا ہونا شرط ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح زنا ثابت کرنے کے لئے چار گواہوں کا ہونا ضروری ہے اسی طرح ان کا تزکیہ اور تعدیل کرنے کیلئے بھی چار مزکیوں کا ہونا ضروری ہوگا۔
The qadi appointing a slave to perform tazkiyah and ta'dil of his own master or of another person is permissible. Similarly, appointing a father to perform tazkiyah of his own son, or a son to perform tazkiyah of his own father, is permissible, even though a slave's testimony for his master, a father's for his son, and a son's for his father is not permissible. However, in the case of public tazkiyah, it is a condition that the verifier be qualified for testimony. Similarly, according to Imam al-Khasaf, it is condition by consensus that the verifiers in public tazkiyah be two, because public tazkiyah and ta'dil are specific to the court. Being specific to the court indicates that public ta'dil is in the meaning of testimony, and when it is in the meaning of testimony, the condition of number will apply as in testimony. That is, at least two verifiers are required. And it is necessary that both verifiers be qualified for testimony.
Objection: There is an objection here: that the requirement of number in public tazkiyah contradicts the non-requirement of number in secret tazkiyah. Because the person who is a verifier in secret tazkiyah is the same one who will be the verifier in public tazkiyah. So if number is not required in secret, how can it be required in public? Or if number is required in public, it should also be required in secret.
Answer: The answer is that according to Imam al-Khasaf, it is a condition that the secret verifier is other than the public verifier. That is, the one who performs secret tazkiyah will not be the one who performs public tazkiyah. And the one who performs public tazkiyah will not be the one who performs secret tazkiyah. When this is the case, it is possible that number is required in public but not in secret. However, according to our view, the person who performs secret tazkiyah and ta'dil is the same one who will perform public tazkiyah. Therefore, the presence of number is not a condition in either secret or public tazkiyah. The author of al-Hidayah said that since Imam Muhammad made qiyas of tazkiyah on testimony regarding number, the mashayikh said that according to Imam Muhammad, for the tazkiyah and ta'dil of witnesses of zina, four verifiers are required. Just as four witnesses are necessary to prove zina, similarly four verifiers are necessary for their tazkiyah.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the conditions for tazkiyah (witness verification). The author first rules on the permissibility of appointing a verifier who may not be a valid witness for the person he is verifying, such as a slave for his master or a father for his son. The ruling is that such appointment is valid even though they cannot testify for those individuals. However, for public tazkiyah conducted in court, the verifier must be qualified to be a witness. Imam al-Khasaf then adds a second condition: the verifier must be at least two in number for public tazkiyah, because public tazkiyah resembles testimony in its procedural form. This leads to an objection: if secret tazkiyah (done informally) does not require two, why should public tazkiyah require two, since the same person could do both? The answer, according to Imam al-Khasaf, is that the secret verifier and public verifier are different people in his view, so the inconsistency is resolved. However, the preferred view in the Hanafi school, as stated by the commentator, is that the same person can do both, and thus the condition of two is not required in either secret or public tazkiyah. Furthermore, Imam Muhammad extended the qiyas further: for zina witnesses, since four witnesses are needed, the tazkiyah of those witnesses also requires four verifiers. This shows the scope of qiyas in Hanafi reasoning.

Key Terms
تزکیہ (tazkiyah): Verification of a witness's credibility and integrity by a verifier (muzakki).
مزکی (muzakki): A person appointed by the qadi to verify witnesses.
علانیہ ('alaniyah): Public, done in the open court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One
B) Two
C) Four
D) None

Key Takeaway
A single verifier suffices for tazkiyah in all cases, despite earlier Hanafi imams requiring more.

Certain Knowledge: The Foundation of Testimony
Explains the first category of testimony and the necessity of knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify self-proving testimony, apply the requirement of certain knowledge, and explain the procedural rules for testimony without prior appointment.

Core Idea
Certain knowledge is the pillar of testimony; without it, even self-proving matters cannot be attested.

What makes a witness's testimony valid in court? The Hanafi school teaches that certain knowledge (علم یقینی) is essential. In this lesson, we examine the first category of testimony—self-proving matters—and explore why the witness must be absolutely certain, even without formal appointment. We'll also clarify a common confusion between 'pillar' and 'condition' and see how the scholars derive these rules from Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Self-Proving Matters
List the events that establish their own ruling without needing a witness to be appointed: sale, confession, usurpation, murder, and a judge's ruling.
These are acts that are inherently visible or audible and create a legal effect by themselves.
2
Extract the Proof for Knowledge Requirement
From the Quran verse (al-Zukhruf 43:86) and the hadith 'When you know it like the sun', derive that certain knowledge is a condition for valid testimony.
The verse uses a circumstantial clause ('while they know'), which in Arabic grammar indicates a condition.
3
Analyze the Rukn vs Shart Distinction
Note the author's metaphorical use of 'rukn' for knowledge and understand why it is actually a condition (shart), as clarified in the commentary.
The term 'rukn' is used to emphasize the importance of knowledge; the legal reality is a condition.
4
Apply the Wording Rule
The witness must say 'ashhadu' (I testify) and not 'ashhadani' (he made me testify), because the latter would be false if the witness was not appointed.
This prevents dishonesty and aligns with the principle that testimony is about truthfulness.
5
Determine the Scenario for Certainty
If a witness hears from behind a curtain, testimony is only allowed when there is absolute certainty that the voice belongs to the right person, e.g., after entering the house and ensuring no one else is present.
This illustrates the strict Hanafi requirement for certainty: any doubt blocks testimony.

Source Text

گواہی اور ادائے گواہی کا بیان گواہی کی پہلی قسم گواہی خود بخود کب ثابت ہو جاتی ہے
فضل وما يتحمله الشاهد على ضربين احدهما ما يثبت حكمه بنفسه مثل البيع والاقرار والغصب والقتل وحكم الحاكم فاذا سمع ذالك الشاهد ورآه وسعه ان يشهد ولم يشهد عليه لانه علم ما هو الموجب بنفسه وهو الركن فى اطلاق الاداء قال الله تعالى الا من شهد بالحق وهم يعلمون و قال النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا علمت مثل الشمس فاشهد والا فدع
ترجمہ گواہ جسکی گواہی اٹھاتا ہے دو قسم پر ہے۔ ان میں سے ایک وہ جس کا حکم بذات خود ثابت ہو جاتا ہے جیسے بیع ، اقرار غصب قتل اور حاکم کا حکم پس جب اس کو گواہ نے سنایا دیکھا تو اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ وہ گواہی دے اگر چہ وہ اس معاملہ پر گواہ نہ بنایا گیا ہو۔ کیونکہ گواہ کو وہ چیز معلوم ہوگئی ہے جو بذات خود موجب ہے، اور جانا ادائے شہادت کے جائز ہونے میں رکن ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ الا من شهد بالحق وهم يعلمون اور آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا جب تو آفتاب کے مانند اس کو جان لے تو گواہی دے ورنہ چھوڑ دے۔
تشریح مصنف مراتب شہادت کے بیان سے فراغت کے بعد اب ان چیزوں کے انواع اور اقسام کو ذکر کریں گے جن کی گواہی کو گواہ اٹھاتا ہے یعنی جن چیزوں کا گواہ بنتا ہے۔ چنانچہ گواہ جن چیزوں کا گواہ بن سکتا ہے انکی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ ایک وہ جن کا حکم بذات خود ثابت ہو جاتا ہے ان میں گواہ بنانے کی ضرورت نہیں پڑتی۔ جیسے بیع ، اقرار ، غصب قتل حاکم کا حکم ۔ پس جب گواہ نے کسی مسموع چیز کو سنا جیسے بیع ، اقرار، حاکم کا حکم یا کسی مبصر (جس کا تعلق دیکھنے سے ہو ) چیز کو دیکھا مثلاً غصب اور قتل تو گواہ کے لئے محض سن کر یا محض دیکھ کر گواہی دینا جائز ہے۔ اگر چہ اس کو گواہ نہ بنایا گیا ہو کیونکہ گواہ کو سن کر یا دیکھ کر اس چیز کا علم ہو گیا ہے جو چیز بذات خود موجب ہے۔ تو اس کے لئے شہادت اداء کرنا جائز ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے کہ علم ( جانا ) جو ادائے شہادت کے جواز کا رکن ہے وہ پایا گیا۔ اور علم ادائے شہادت کے جواز کارکن اس لئے ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے الا من شهد بالحق وهم يعلمون يعنى جولوگ حق کو جان کر حق کی گواہی دیتے ہیں اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ گواہی کے لئے علم (جانا) ضروری ہے اور رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا اذا علمت مثل الشمس فاشهد والا فدع يعنى جب تو آفتاب کے مانند اس کو جان لے تو گواہی دے ورنہ چھوڑ دے حاصل یہ کہ جب کسی کو کسی چیز کے بارے میں یقینی علم حاصل ہو جائے تو اس کے لئے گواہی دینا جائز ہے اور اگر علم نہ ہو تو گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔
بہر حال اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ گواہی کے لئے اس چیز کا جاننا ضروری ہے جس کی گواہی دی جائے گی۔ اعتراض اس جگہ ایک اشکال ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ ادائے شہادت کے جواز کیلئے علم (جانا) رکن ہے۔ حالانکہ آیت اور روایت دونوں علم کے شرط ہونے پر دلالت کرتے ہیں اور رکن ہونے پر دلالت نہیں کرتے اس طور پر کہ آیت میں وهم يعلمون‘ حال ہے اور حال شرط ہوتا ہے۔ اور حدیث میں لفظ اذا جو علم پر داخل ہے وہ شرط کیلئے موضوع ہے۔ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ لفظ رکن مجازاً استعمال کیا گیا ہے ورنہ صاحب ہدایہ کی مراد بھی لفظ رکن سے شرط ہی ہے اور شرط کو لفظ رکن کے ساتھ اسلئے تعبیر کیا گیا تا کہ یہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ ادائے شہادت کو علم کی طرف شدت احتیاج ہے۔ پہلی قسم میں گواہ اشھد کے لفظ سے گواہی دے گا اشھدنی نہیں کہے گا
قال و يقول اشهد انه باع ولا يقول اشهدنى لانه كذب ولو سمع من وراء الحجاب لا يجوز له ان شهد ولو فسر للقاضى لا يقبله لان النغمة تشبه النغمة فلم يحصل العلم الا اذا كان دخل البيت وعلم انه ليس فيه احد سواه ثم جلس على الباب وليس في البيت مسلك غيره فسمع اقرار الداخل ولا يراه له ان يشهد لانه حصل العلم في هذه الصورة
ترجمہ صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ یہ گواہ یوں کہے کہ میں گواہی دیتا ہوں کہ اس نے فروخت کیا اور یوں نہ کہے کہ اس نے مجھے گواہ بنایا اسلئے کہ یہ جھوٹ ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے پردہ کے پیچھے سے سنا ہو تو اس کے لئے گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے ۔ اور اگر اس نے قاضی سے
Statement of testimony and its performance: The first type of testimony is that which becomes self-proving.
What the witness bears witness to is of two types. One is that whose ruling is established by itself, such as sale, confession, usurpation, murder, and the ruling of a judge. When the witness hears this or sees it, it is permissible for him to testify even if he was not made a witness over it, because he knows what is the cause by itself, and knowledge is the pillar in the permissibility of performance. Allah Almighty said: 'Except he who testifies to the truth while they know.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When you know it like the sun, then testify, otherwise refrain.'
Translation: What the witness bears is of two types. One of them is that whose ruling is established by itself, like sale, confession, usurpation, murder, and the judge's ruling. When the witness hears or sees it, it is permissible for him to testify even if he was not appointed as a witness over it, because he has come to know that thing which is the cause by itself, and knowledge is a pillar in the permissibility of testimony. Allah Almighty said: 'Except he who testifies to the truth while they know.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When you know it like the sun, then testify, otherwise refrain.'
Explanation: The author, after completing the discussion of the ranks of testimony, will now mention the types and kinds of things that the witness bears testimony about, i.e., the things of which he becomes a witness. So the things that a witness can witness are of two types. One is that whose ruling is established by itself, without the need to be appointed as a witness. Such as sale, confession, usurpation, murder, and the judge's ruling. So when the witness heard something audible (like sale, confession, judge's ruling) or saw something visible (like usurpation and murder), it is permissible for him to testify merely by hearing or seeing, even if he was not made a witness, because through hearing or seeing he has gained knowledge of that thing which is itself a cause. Therefore, it becomes permissible for him to perform testimony because knowledge, which is the pillar for the permissibility of testimony, has been found. And knowledge is the pillar for the permissibility of testimony because Allah said: 'Except he who testifies to the truth while they know,' meaning those who testifies to the truth knowing it. This verse indicates that knowledge is necessary for testimony. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When you know it like the sun, then testify; otherwise, refrain.' Summary: When a person gains certain knowledge of something, it is permissible for him to testify; if he does not have knowledge, it is not permissible to testify.
In any case, this hadith also indicates that knowledge of the thing one testifies about is necessary. Objection: There is an objection here: The author of al-Hidayah said that knowledge is a pillar for the permissibility of performing testimony, whereas the verse and hadith indicate that knowledge is a condition, not a pillar. As in the verse, 'While they know' is a circumstantial clause, and circumstantial clause indicates a condition. And in the hadith, the word 'idha' (when) enters upon knowledge, which is used for conditions. Answer: The answer is that the word 'rukn' is used metaphorically; otherwise, the author of al-Hidayah also intends by 'rukn' what is a condition. It is expressed as 'rukn' to emphasize the great need testimony has for knowledge. In the first type, the witness will testify with the word 'ashhadu' (I testify), not 'ashhadani' (he made me testify).
He (al-Quduri) said: He says, 'I testify that he sold,' and does not say, 'He made me testify,' because it would be a lie. And if he heard from behind a curtain, it is not permissible for him to testify. And if he explained to the judge, the judge would not accept it, because the voice resembles another voice, so certainty is not achieved unless he enters the house and knows that there is no one else in it, then sits at the door while there is no other passage in the house, then hears the confession of the person inside without seeing him. In this case, it is permissible for him to testify, because certainty is achieved in this situation.
Translation: Al-Quduri said: This witness should say, 'I testify that he sold,' and should not say, 'He made me testify,' because that would be a lie. And if he heard from behind a curtain, it is not permissible for him to testify. If he explains to the judge, the judge will not accept it because voices resemble each other, so certainty is not achieved. Only if he enters the house, knows that no one else is there, then sits at the door while there is no other exit in the house, and hears the confession of the entrant without seeing him, it is permissible for him to testify because certainty is achieved in this form.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran and Sunnah, defining the first category of testimony: self-proving matters. The author explains that certain events—sale, confession, usurpation, murder, and a judge's ruling—establish their own legal effect without requiring the witness to have been specifically appointed. The witness may testify based on his own hearing or seeing, as long as he has certain knowledge. The Quranic verse (al-Zukhruf 43:86) and the hadith 'When you know it like the sun, then testify' are cited as evidence. An important objection arises: is knowledge a pillar (rukn) or a condition (shart)? The commentator clarifies that 'rukn' is used metaphorically; it is actually a condition, but the term 'rukn' emphasizes its critical importance. The passage then moves to procedural rules: the witness must use the wording 'ashhadu' (I testify) and not 'ashhadani' (he made me testify), because the latter would be false if he was not appointed. Finally, a detailed scenario is given for hearing testimony from behind a curtain: it is not permitted unless there is absolute certainty that the voice belongs to the right person, such as when the witness enters the house, ensures no one else is present, and there is no other exit. This illustrates the Hanafi emphasis on certainty ('ilm) as the foundation for testimony.

Key Terms
شہادت (shahadah): Testimony given in court about a legal right or event.
علم ('ilm): Certain knowledge that removes doubt, akin to seeing the sun.
ادائے شہادت (ada' al-shahadah): The performance of giving testimony in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum requirement for a witness to testify about a self-proving matter like a sale?
A) The witness must have been formally appointed by the seller or buyer.
B) The witness must have certain knowledge of the sale, acquired by hearing or seeing.
C) The witness must have a written document from the parties.
D) The witness must be a close friend of one of the parties.

Key Takeaway
Testimony on self-proving matters is valid only when the witness possesses certain knowledge, even without prior appointment.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Certain Knowledge as a Condition for Testimony in Self-Justifying Matters
Explains first category of testimony and conditions of knowledge with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement of certain knowledge for testimony, explain the metaphorical usage of 'rukn' in the Hidayah, and apply the rule to scenarios of hearing testimony without formal appointment.

Core Idea
Testimony requires certain knowledge (yaqin), not doubt; 'rukn' in the Hidayah means condition, emphasizing extreme necessity.

This lesson examines the first category of testimony: matters whose ruling is self-justifying, such as sale or acknowledgment. The central question is: what level of knowledge must a witness have? The Hanafi school, relying on the Quran and Hadith, requires certain knowledge (yaqin). We will also explore the apparent contradiction in the Hidayah's use of 'rukn' and its resolution, and apply these principles to cases where the witness hears from behind a curtain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category and the requirement
The passage divides testimony into categories. The first category: matters that are self-justifying (e.g., sale, acknowledgment). For these, the witness does not need to be formally appointed; hearing or seeing suffices. But why? Because the witness has obtained knowledge. The key is that knowledge must be certain.
Self-justifying matters are those whose legal effect is established by the act itself, like a sale contract.
2
Analyze the proof from Quran and Hadith
The Quranic verse (43:86) and the Hadith 'know like the sun' are cited. Identify the linguistic evidence: the word 'know' in the verse and the conditional 'when you know' in the Hadith. Both indicate that knowledge is a condition for testimony.
The verse: 'Except those who testify with the truth and they know.' The Hadith: 'When you know it like the sun, testify; otherwise leave it.'
3
Resolve the terminology: rukn vs shart
The Hidayah calls knowledge a 'rukn'. An objection is raised that the proofs show it is a 'shart'. The commentator explains that 'rukn' is used metaphorically to stress extreme need. Understand the usul distinction: rukn is internal, shart external; here it is a shart, but the term rukn is used to emphasize its crucial importance.
This clarification prevents misunderstanding about the nature of the requirement.
4
Apply the rule to a specific scenario: hearing from behind a curtain
Generally, hearing from behind a curtain does not yield certain knowledge because voices can be similar. Thus testimony is not allowed. However, if the witness takes measures to ensure certainty (enters, confirms no one else, sits at only door, hears without seeing), then certainty is attained and testimony is valid.
The exception requires active verification to eliminate doubt about the speaker's identity.

بہر حال اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ گواہی کے لئے اس چیز کا جاننا ضروری ہے جس کی گواہی دی جائے گی۔ اعتراض اس جگہ ایک اشکال ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ ادائے شہادت کے جواز کیلئے علم (جانا) رکن ہے۔ حالانکہ آیت اور روایت دونوں علم کے شرط ہونے پر دلالت کرتے ہیں اور رکن ہونے پر دلالت نہیں کرتے اس طور پر کہ آیت میں وهم يعلمون‘ حال ہے اور حال شرط ہوتا ہے۔ اور حدیث میں لفظ اذا جو علم پر داخل ہے وہ شرط کیلئے موضوع ہے۔ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ لفظ رکن مجازا استعمال کیا گیا ہے ورنہ صاحب ہدایہ کی مراد بھی لفظ رکن سے شرط ہی ہے اور شرط کو لفظ رکن کے ساتھ اسلئے تعبیر کیا گیا تا کہ یہ معلوم ہو جائے کہ ادائے شہادت کو علم کی طرف شدت احتیاج ہے۔ پہلی قسم میں گواہ اشھد کے لفظ سے گواہی دے گا اشھدنی نہیں کہے گا
قال و يقول اشهد انه باع ولا يقول اشهدنى لانه كذب ولو سمع من وراء الحجاب لا يجوز له ان شهد ولو فسر للقاضى لا يقبله لان النغمة تشبه النغمة فلم يحصل العلم الا اذا كان دخل البيت وعلم انه ليس فيه احد سواه ثم جلس على الباب وليس في البيت مسلک غیره فسمع اقرار الداخل ولا يراه له ان يشهد لانه حصل العلم في هذه الصورة
ترجمہ صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ یہ گواہ یوں کہے کہ میں گواہی دیتا ہوں کہ اس نے فروخت کیا اور یوں نہ کہے کہ اس نے مجھے گواہ بنایا اسلئے کہ یہ جھوٹ ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے پردہ کے پیچھے سے سنا ہو تو اس کے لئے گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے ۔ اور اگر اس نے قاضی سے تفسیر کر دی تو قاضی اس کو قبول نہیں کرے گا۔ اسلئے کہ ایک آواز دوسری آواز کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا علم حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ مگر جبکہ گواہ مکان میں داخل ہوا اور گواہ کو یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ مکان میں داخل ہونے والے مدعی علیہ کے سواء کوئی اور نہیں ہے۔ پھر گواہ دروازہ پر بیٹھ گیا۔ اور مکان میں جانے کا اس دروازے کے علاوہ کوئی اور راستہ نہیں ہے۔ پھر گواہ نے اندر والے آدمی کا اقرار سنا حالانکہ گواہ اس کو نہیں دیکھتا ہے۔ تو گواہ کے لئے اسکی گواہی دینا جائز ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اس صورت میں علم حاصل ہو گیا ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے دوسرے شخص سے اپنی بات سنی جو مسموعات کے قبیلہ سے ہے مثلا بیچنا خرید نا یا اقرار کرتا سُنا ، اور اس کو کسی نے اس پر گواہ بھی نہیں بنایا لیکن گواہی کی ضرورت پڑی تو یہ گواہ سکنے والا ) گواہی دیتے وقت یوں کہے کہ میں گواہی دیتا ہوں کہ اس نے فروخت کیا ہے یا اس نے خرید کیا ہے یا فلاں کے لئے اپنے اوپر اتنی رقم کا اقرار کیا ہے اور یوں نہ کہیے کہ اس نے مجھ کو گواہ بنایا ہے کیونکہ یہ بالکل جھوٹ ہے اور جھوٹ اسلئے ہے کہ اس کو کسی نے گواہ نہیں بنایا ہے جبکہ مدعی علیہ کا کلام سنکر یہ خود ہی گواہ بنا ہے اور اگر کسی نے پردہ کے پیچھے سے سنا ہو مثلاً اس کو آواز آئی کہ مکان کے اندر ایک نے کہا کہ میں نے بیچا اور دوسرے نے کہا کہ میں نے خریدا تو گواہ کیلئے جائز نہیں کہ وہ کسی خاص آدمی پر بائع یا مشتری ہونے کی گواہی دے اور اگر اس نے قاضی کے سامنے اس بات کی وضاحت کر دی کہ میں نے پردہ کے پیچھے سے سن کر گواہی دی ہے تو قاضی اس کی گواہی کو قبول نہیں کریگا کیوں کہ آوازیں آپس میں ایک دوسرے کی مشابہ ہوتی ہیں ۔ یعنی محض آواز سنکر یہ امتیاز نہیں کیا جا سکتا کہ بولنے والا کون ہے بلکہ تکلم مشتبہ ہو جاتا ہے اور مشتبہ چیز علم کا فائدہ نہیں دیتی ہے حالانکہ ادائے شہادت کیلئے گواہ کو اس چیز کا علم ہونا ضروری ہے۔ جس کے بارے میں وہ گواہی دیگا پس جب پردہ کے پیچھے سے سنکر یقینی علم حاصل نہیں ہوتا تو پردہ کے پیچھے سے سنکر گواہی دینا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا ۔ ہاں اگر گواہ کمرہ میں داخل ہوا اور اس کو معلوم ہو گیا کہ کمرے میں سوائے مدعی علیہ کے کوئی نہیں ہے پھر گواہ خود کمرے کے دروازے پر بیٹھ گیا اور اس کمرے میں اس دروازے کے علاوہ آمد و رفت کا کوئی دوسرا راستہ بھی نہیں پھر گواہ نے اندر والے آدمی ( مدعی علیہ ) کا اقرار سُنا حالانکہ گواہ اسکو نہیں دیکھتا ہے مثلاً اس نے اندر سے اقرار کیا کہ میں نے اپنا غلام خالد حامد بن شاہد کے ہاتھ فروخت کیا یا اس نے اندر سے حامد کیلئے ایک ہزار درہم کا اقرار کیا اور گواہوں نے اس کو دیکھا نہیں تو بھی گواہ کو اس کی گواہی دینا جائز ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں گواہ کو یقینی علم حاصل ہو گیا ہے اور جب گواہ کو یقینی علم حاصل ہو گیا تو گواہی کی شرط پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اس کی گواہی بھی قبول کی جائے گی۔
Except those who testify with the truth while they know. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: When you know it like the sun, testify, otherwise leave it. Commentary: After finishing the discussion of the ranks of testimony, the author will now mention the types and categories of matters for which a witness bears testimony, i.e., what he becomes a witness of. So the matters a person can witness are of two types. One: those whose ruling is self-established, where there is no need to be made a witness, such as sale, acknowledgment, usurpation, murder, and the judge's ruling. So when a witness hears an audible matter like a sale, acknowledgment, or judge's ruling, or sees a visible matter like usurpation or murder, it is permissible for him to testify by merely hearing or seeing, even if he was not made a witness, because he has obtained knowledge of that matter, which is self-justifying. So it becomes permissible for him to give testimony, because knowledge, which is the pillar (rukn) of permissibility of giving testimony, is present. And knowledge is the pillar because Allah said: 'Except those who testify with the truth and they know.' This verse indicates that knowledge is necessary for testimony. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When you know it like the sun, testify; otherwise leave it.' The conclusion is that when a person obtains certain knowledge of something, it is permissible for him to testify, and if he does not have knowledge, it is not permissible. Anyhow, this hadith also shows that knowledge of the matter being testified to is necessary. Objection: There is a problem here: the author of al-Hidayah said that knowledge is a rukn (pillar) for the permissibility of giving testimony, whereas both the verse and the hadith indicate that knowledge is a shart (condition), not a rukn. In the verse, 'while they know' is a hal (circumstantial clause), and a hal is a condition. In the hadith, the word 'when' (idha) is used for condition. Answer: The word rukn is used metaphorically; otherwise, the author of al-Hidayah also means by 'rukn' that it is a condition, but he used 'rukn' to express the extreme need of testimony for knowledge. In the first category, the witness will say 'Ashhadu' (I testify) and not 'Ashhadani' (he made me a witness). He said: He says 'I testify that he sold' and not 'he made me a witness' because that would be a lie. And if he heard from behind a curtain, it is not permissible for him to testify, and if he explains to the judge, the judge does not accept it, because one voice resembles another, so certainty is not attained. But if he entered the house and knew there was no one else there, then sat at the door, and there is no other entrance, and he heard the occupant's acknowledgment without seeing him, it is permissible for him to testify, because certainty is attained in this case. Translation: The author (al-Quduri) said: This witness should say 'I testify that he sold' and not 'he made me a witness' because that is a lie. And if he heard from behind a curtain, it is not permissible for him to testify, and if he explains to the judge, the judge will not accept it, because one voice resembles another, so knowledge is not obtained. But if the witness entered the house and knew that there was no one besides the defendant, then he sat at the door, and there was no other entrance to the house, then he heard the person inside acknowledge (without seeing him), it is permissible for him to testify, because in this case knowledge is obtained. Commentary: The case is: If a person heard another's statement which is from the category of audible matters, like a sale or purchase or acknowledgment, and no one made him a witness, but there is a need for testimony, then this (hearing) witness should say at the time of testifying: 'I testify that he sold' or 'he bought' or 'he acknowledged so much money for so-and-so', and should not say 'he made me a witness' because that is a lie. And if he heard from behind a curtain, e.g., he heard a voice inside a house saying 'I sold' and another saying 'I bought', it is not permissible for the witness to testify that a specific person is the seller or buyer. And if he explains to the judge that he heard from behind a curtain, the judge will not accept his testimony, because voices resemble each other. That is, merely hearing a voice does not identify the speaker; the speaker is ambiguous, and ambiguous things do not yield knowledge. Since giving testimony requires knowledge of the matter, and hearing from behind a curtain does not give certain knowledge, testifying is not permissible. However, if the witness entered the room and knew there was no one else besides the defendant, then he sat at the room's door, and the room had no other entrance or exit, and he heard the person inside (the defendant) speaking, e.g., he acknowledged selling his slave Khalid to Hamid ibn Shahid, or acknowledged one thousand dirhams for Hamid, and the witness did not see him, then it is permissible for him to testify, because in this case certain knowledge is attained, and since the condition for testimony is met, his testimony will be accepted.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya explains the first category of matters for which testimony is given: those whose legal ruling is self-established, meaning the act itself (like sale, acknowledgment, usurpation, murder, or judge's ruling) inherently justifies testimony. The author, commenting on al-Hidayah, emphasizes that the witness must have certain knowledge (ilm yaqini) for testimony to be valid. He cites the Quranic verse (43:86) and the Hadith 'When you know it like the sun, testify; otherwise leave it' as proofs. An objection is then raised regarding the terminology: the Hidayah says knowledge is a 'rukn' (pillar), but the proofs indicate it is a 'shart' (condition). The commentator resolves this by explaining that 'rukn' is used metaphorically to stress the extreme necessity of knowledge. The testimony must be phrased as 'Ashhadu' (I testify), not 'Ashhadani' (he made me a witness), unless the witness was formally appointed. The rule for hearing from behind a curtain is detailed: generally, it is not allowed because voices are similar and certainty is lacking. However, an exception is made when the witness has taken measures to ensure that only the specific person could be speaking, such as entering the room, confirming no one else is present, and sitting at the only entrance. In such a case, hearing the acknowledgment without seeing is sufficient for certain knowledge, and testimony is permissible. The author follows the order of the original matn, providing both the Arabic ruling and a detailed explanation.

Key Terms
علم (ilm): Certain knowledge (yaqini ilm) that is required for the validity of testimony, as opposed to doubt or suspicion.
ركن (rukn): Pillar; here used metaphorically to indicate an essential condition (shart) due to its importance.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court to establish a legal right or fact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann)
B) Certain knowledge (yaqin)
C) Hearsay
D) Any kind of knowledge

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, valid testimony requires certain knowledge (yaqin); 'rukn' in the Hidayah is a metaphorical emphasis on its necessity, not a change in its legal nature as a condition.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony on Testimony: The Requirement of Tahmil
Defines second category and ruling for shahada 'ala shahada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony on testimony and identify the condition of tahmil required for its validity.

Core Idea
Testimony on testimony is invalid without formal appointment; the original testimony lacks self-justifying force.

In this lesson, we examine a special category of testimony: shahada 'ala shahada, where a witness testifies based on hearing another witness's testimony rather than direct observation. The Hanafi school holds that such secondary testimony is invalid unless the secondary witness has been formally appointed (tahmil) by the original witness or litigant. Understanding this requirement is crucial for maintaining the integrity of evidentiary chains in court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is testimony on testimony (shahada 'ala shahada). The Hanafi ruling is that it is invalid (batil) without formal appointment.
The ruling applies when a person hears a witness testify and then attempts to testify on that same matter.
2
Understand the rationale
The passage states that testimony itself is not self-justifying (ghayr mujiba binafsiha); it only becomes effective when formally transmitted to the court. Therefore, the secondary witness cannot simply rely on hearing.
The legal effect (athar) of testimony depends on proper conveyance to the court, not on mere auditory perception.
3
Recognize the condition: tahmil
The secondary witness must be explicitly appointed (tahmil or inaba) by the original witness or the litigant to bear and convey the testimony. Without such appointment, the testimony is not transmitted validly.
Appointment can be made by the original witness saying, 'I commission you to bear witness on my testimony.'
4
Apply the rule
If a person hears a witness testify but has not been appointed, he cannot later testify on that matter. Even if he hears the witness testifying about another secondary testimony, it remains invalid because the chain of appointment is broken.
The exception: only when tahmil is present does the secondary testimony become admissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسری قسم ... گواہی کا خود بخود ثابت نہ ہونا
ومنه مالا يثبت حكمه بنفسه مثل الشهادة على الشهادة فاذا سمع شاهداً يشهد بشئ لم يجزله ان يشهد على شهادته الا ان يشهده عليها لان الشهادة غير موجبة بنفسها وانما تصير موجبة بالنقل الى مجلس القضاء فلا بد من الانابة والتحميل ولم يوجد وكذا لو سمعه يشهد الشاهد على شهادتلم يسع للسامع ان يشهد لأنه ما حمله و انما حمل غيره
ترجمہ اور ان میں سے ایک قسم وہ ہے جس کا حکم بذات خود ثابت نہ ہو جیسے گواہی پر گواہی دینا۔ پس جب کسی نے گواہ کوسنا کہ وہ
Second category: testimony whose ruling is not self-established. And among them is a type whose ruling is not self-established, such as testimony on testimony. So when someone hears a witness testifying to something, it is not permissible for him to testify on his testimony unless he appoints him (makes him bear witness) to it, because the testimony itself is not self-justifying; it only becomes justifying by transmission to the court session. So appointment and bearing (tahmil) are necessary, and they are not present. Similarly, if he hears the witness testifying on his testimony, it is not permissible for the listener to testify, because he has not borne the testimony; rather, someone else has borne it. Translation: And among them is a type whose ruling is not self-established, like testimony on testimony. So when someone heard a witness testifying that...
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage introduces the second category of matters for which testimony is given: those whose ruling is not self-established. The primary example is testimony on testimony (shahada ala shahada). The ruling is that a person who hears a witness testifying to a fact cannot himself testify to that fact based on hearing that testimony. This is because the first witness's testimony does not have self-justifying force; it only becomes effective when it is formally transferred to the court. Therefore, the secondary witness must be explicitly appointed (tahmil) by the original witness or the litigant to bear and transmit the testimony. Without such appointment, the secondary testimony is invalid. The text quotes the Arabic original and then provides an Urdu translation and further explanation.

Key Terms
شهادة على شهادة (shahada ala shahada): Testimony given by a witness who did not directly observe the event but heard another witness testify about it.
تحميل (tahmil): The act of loading or entrusting testimony; the formal appointment of a secondary witness to bear and convey testimony.
انابة (inaba): Appointment or commissioning of a representative to perform a task; here, it refers to appointing someone to bear testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The person must be a relative of the original witness
D) The person must be a judge

Key Takeaway
Testimony on testimony is invalid unless the secondary witness has been formally appointed (tahmil) by the original witness or the litigant.

Conditions for Testimony Based on Hearing: Certainty of Speaker Identity
Ruling on the validity of hearing-based testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which hearing-based testimony is valid in the Hanafi school and distinguish between scenarios that yield certain knowledge (yaqin) versus those that do not.

Core Idea
Hearing a voice alone is insufficient for testimony; certainty of the speaker's identity is required.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a critical issue in court testimony: when can a witness testify about something heard but not seen? The Hanafi school requires certainty (al-yaqin) about the speaker's identity. Mere voice recognition is not enough due to ambiguity. However, if the witness takes steps to ensure only the defendant could have been speaking, the testimony becomes permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two cases: hearing from behind a curtain (invalid) and hearing after entering the room and controlling access (valid). Distinguish them clearly.
The key difference is the degree of certainty about the speaker's identity.
2
Understand the basis for invalidity
Voices resemble each other, so hearing alone does not yield certain knowledge (yaqin). The witness cannot be sure who spoke. Thus, testimony is rejected.
This is based on the principle that testimony requires certainty (al-yaqin).
3
Understand why the second scenario yields certainty
When the witness enters the room, confirms only the defendant is inside, sits at the only door, and hears the admission, there is no possibility of another speaker. Certainty is achieved.
The controlled environment eliminates doubt.
4
Apply the general principle
Testimony about an oral statement is only valid if the witness has certain knowledge (ilm yaqini) of the speaker's identity. The conditions in the second scenario fulfill this requirement.
This ruling is specific to testimony on hearing (al-shahada bi al-sam').

Source Text

كتاب الشهادة
اشرف الہدایہ جلد - و ہم تفسیر کر دی تو قاضی اس کو قبول نہیں کرے گا۔ اسلئے کہ ایک آواز دوسری آواز کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے۔ لہذا علم حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ مگر جبکہ گواہ مکان میں داخل ہوا اور گواہ کو یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ مکان میں داخل ہونے والے مدعی علیہ کے سواء کوئی اور نہیں ہے۔ پھر گواہ دروازہ پر بیٹھ گیا۔ اور مکان میں جانے کا اس دروازے کے علاوہ کوئی اور راستہ نہیں ہے۔ پھر گواہ نے اندر والے آدمی کا اقرار شنا حالانکہ گواہ اس کو نہیں دیکھتا ہے۔ تو گواہ کے لئے اسکی گواہی دینا جائز ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اس صورت میں علم حاصل ہو گیا ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے دوسرے شخص سے اپنی بات سنی جو مسموعات کے قبیلہ سے ہے مثلا بیچنا خرید نا یا اقرار کرتا سُنا ، اور اس کو کسی نے اس پر گواہ بھی نہیں بنایا لیکن گواہی کی ضرورت پڑی تو یہ گواہ سکنے والا ) گواہی دیتے وقت یوں کہے کہ میں گواہی دیتا ہوں کہ اس نے فروخت کیا ہے یا اس نے خرید کیا ہے یا فلاں کے لئے اپنے اوپر اتنی رقم کا اقرار کیا ہے اور یوں نہ کہیے کہ اس نے مجھ کو گواہ بنایا ہے کیونکہ یہ بالکل جھوٹ ہے اور جھوٹ اسلئے ہے کہ اس کو کسی نے گواہ نہیں بنایا ہے جبکہ مدعی علیہ کا کلام سنکر یہ خود ہی گواہ بنا ہے اور اگر کسی نے پردہ کے پیچھے سے سنا ہو مثلاً اس کو آواز آئی کہ مکان کے اندر ایک نے کہا کہ میں نے بیچا اور دوسرے نے کہا کہ میں نے خریدا تو گواہ کیلئے جائز نہیں کہ وہ کسی خاص آدمی پر بائع یا مشتری ہونے کی گواہی دے اور اگر اس نے قاضی کے سامنے اس بات کی وضاحت کر دی کہ میں نے پردہ کے پیچھے سے سن کر گواہی دی ہے تو قاضی اس کی گواہی کو قبول نہیں کریگا کیوں کہ آوازیں آپس میں ایک دوسرے کی مشابہ ہوتی ہیں ۔ یعنی محض آواز سنکر یہ امتیاز نہیں کیا جا سکتا کہ بولنے والا کون ہے بلکہ تکلم مشتبہ ہو جاتا ہے اور مشتبہ چیز علم کا فائدہ نہیں دیتی ہے حالانکہ ادائے شہادت کیلئے گواہ کو اس چیز کا علم ہونا ضروری ہے۔ جس کے بارے میں وہ گواہی دیگا پس جب پردہ کے پیچھے سے سنکر یقینی علم حاصل نہیں ہوتا تو پردہ کے پیچھے سے سنکر گواہی دینا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا ۔ ہاں اگر گواہ کمرہ میں داخل ہوا اور اس کو معلوم ہو گیا کہ کمرے میں سوائے مدعی علیہ کے کوئی نہیں ہے پھر گواہ خود کمرے کے دروازے پر بیٹھ گیا اور اس کمرے میں اس دروازے کے علاوہ آمد و رفت کا کوئی دوسرا راستہ بھی نہیں پھر گواہ نے اندر والے آدمی ( مدعی علیہ ) کا اقرار سُنا حالانکہ گواہ اسکو نہیں دیکھتا ہے مثلاً اس نے اندر سے اقرار کیا کہ میں نے اپنا غلام خالد حامد بن شاہد کے ہاتھ فروخت کیا یا اس نے اندر سے حامد کیلئے ایک ہزار درہم کا اقرار کیا اور گواہوں نے اس کو دیکھا نہیں تو بھی گواہ کو اس کی گواہی دینا جائز ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں گواہ کو یقینی علم حاصل ہو گیا ہے اور جب گواہ کو یقینی علم حاصل ہو گیا تو گواہی کی شرط پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اس کی گواہی بھی قبول کی جائے گی۔
Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume - and if he explains, the judge will not accept it. Because one voice resembles another voice. Hence knowledge is not obtained. Except when the witness entered the house and the witness knew that there is no one other than the defendant entering the house. Then the witness sat at the door. And there is no other way to enter the house except this door. Then the witness heard the admission of the person inside, although the witness does not see him. Then it is permissible for the witness to give testimony. Because in this case knowledge is obtained. Explanation of the situation: The issue is that if someone heard his own words from another person which are of the category of audible matters, e.g., he heard selling, buying, or an admission, and no one made him a witness over it, but the need for testimony arose, then this witness... when giving testimony should say: I testify that he sold or he bought or he admitted such and such amount for himself for so-and-so, and should not say: He made me a witness, because this is a complete lie, and it is a lie because no one made him a witness; rather, upon hearing the defendant's speech, he himself became a witness. And if someone heard from behind a curtain, e.g., a voice came to him that inside the house one said 'I sold' and another said 'I bought', then it is not permissible for the witness to testify that a specific person is the seller or buyer. And if he clarifies to the judge that he testified by hearing from behind the curtain, the judge will not accept his testimony, because voices resemble each other. That is, merely hearing the voice, it cannot be distinguished who the speaker is; rather, the speech becomes ambiguous, and an ambiguous thing does not yield knowledge. While for the performance of testimony, the witness must have knowledge of that about which he will testify. So when certain knowledge is not obtained by hearing from behind the curtain, then testifying by hearing from behind the curtain is not permissible. Yes, if the witness entered the room and knew that there is no one in the room except the defendant, then the witness himself sat at the door of the room, and there is no other way of entry and exit in that room except that door, then the witness heard the admission of the person inside (the defendant) although the witness does not see him, e.g., he admitted from inside: 'I sold my slave Khalid to Hamid bin Shahid' or he admitted from inside for Hamid a thousand dirhams, and the witnesses did not see him, still it is permissible for the witness to give testimony, because in this case the witness obtained certain knowledge, and when the witness obtained certain knowledge, then due to the fulfillment of the condition of testimony, his testimony will be accepted.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school on the conditions for accepting testimony based on hearing. The author first establishes a general principle: a judge will not accept testimony if the witness merely explains that he heard from behind a curtain, because voices can be confused and certainty is not achieved. However, an exception is made when the witness enters the room, confirms that only the defendant is inside, sits at the only door, and hears the admission. In that scenario, even without seeing the speaker, certainty is attained because there is no possibility of another person. The commentary then expands on this: if a person hears a transaction or admission without being formally appointed as a witness, he may still testify, but he must state what he heard, not claim he was made a witness, as that would be false. If he only heard voices from behind a curtain without visual confirmation, the testimony is invalid due to uncertainty. The conditions for valid hearsay testimony are thus: visual confirmation of the speaker's identity or a controlled environment ensuring only the defendant could be speaking.

Key Terms
شهادة على الشهادة (shahāda ʿalā al-shahāda): Testimony on testimony; a secondary witness testifying based on the original witness's testimony.
علم يقيني (ʿilm yaqīnī): Certain knowledge; necessary for a witness to have before testifying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it permissible for a witness to testify about a statement he heard from behind a curtain?
A) Whenever he recognizes the voice
B) When he enters the room, knows only the defendant is inside, sits at the only door, and hears the admission
C) When he hears the admission clearly
D) When he sees the defendant through the curtain

Key Takeaway
Testimony based on hearing requires certain knowledge (yaqin) of the speaker's identity; hearing from behind a curtain is invalid, but hearing after controlling the environment is valid.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony on Testimony: The Requirement of Appointment
Explains that testimony on testimony requires original witness's appointment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for validity of testimony on testimony and apply it to determine when a secondary witness may testify.

Core Idea
Secondary witnesses cannot testify without explicit appointment from the original witness.

Testimony on testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) is a crucial mechanism in Islamic courts, allowing a chain of witnesses. However, the Hanafi school places a strict condition: the original witness must formally appoint the secondary witness to carry the testimony. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this requirement and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what 'testimony on testimony' is and the basic ruling: is it valid or invalid? When is it permitted?
The ruling is that it is not valid unless the original witness appoints the secondary witness.
2
Locate the key condition
Find the condition that makes testimony on testimony valid: the original witness must make the secondary witness a deputy (na'ib) and place the burden of testimony (tahmil) on him.
Without this appointment, the testimony is not binding.
3
Understand the reason (ta'lil)
The passage explains that testimony by itself does not create a ruling; it only becomes effective when presented in court. The original witness has authority (wilaya) over the testimony, and a secondary witness cannot assume that authority without permission.
This is a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) based on the nature of testimony.
4
Apply the rule to scenarios
Consider two scenarios: (1) someone hears an original witness testify outside court, and (2) someone hears the original witness appointing another person as a secondary witness. Determine whether the listener can testify.
In both cases, the listener cannot testify because they were not appointed.

چیز کی گواہی دیتا ہے تو اس کیلئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ اس کی گواہی پر گواہی دے۔ مگر یہ کہ وہ اس کو اپنی گواہی پر گواہ بنادے اس لئے کہ شہادت بذات خود موجب نہیں بلکہ وہ قاضی کی مجلس کی طرف منتقل کرنے سے موجب ہوتی ہے۔ پس ضروری ہے کہ (اصل گواہ ) اس کو اپنا " نائب بنائے اور اس پر گواہی کا بوجھ رکھے۔ حالانکہ ان میں سے کچھ نہیں پایا گیا اور اسی طرح اگر کسی نے اصل گواہ کو سنا کہ وہ شاہد فرع کو اپنی گواہی پر گواہ بنا رہا ہے تو سننے والے کے لئے گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے ۔ اس لئے کہ اصل گواہ نے سامع پر گواہی کا بوجھ نہیں رکھا بلکہ اس کے علاوہ پر رکھا ہے۔
تشریح مذکورہ دو قسموں میں سے دوسری قسم وہ ہے جس کا حکم بذات خود ثابت نہ ہو بلکہ اس میں گواہ بنانے کی ضرورت پڑتی ہو۔ جیسے شہادت علی الشہادت کہ جب تک اصلی گواہ کسی کو اپنی گواہی پر گواہ نہ بنائیں اس وقت تک شہود فرع کے لئے گواہی دینے کا حکم ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی نے مثلاً زید نے گواہ کو مثلا بکر کو جلس قاضی کے علاوہ میں سنا کہ بکر اس بات کی گواہی دیتا ہے کہ خالد کے حامد پر ایک ہزار درہم قرض ہیں تو شاہد فرع یعنی زید کے لئے یہ جائز نہیں ہے کہ وہ خالد کے حامد پر ایک ہزار درہم قرضہ ہونے کی گواہی دے۔ ہاں گر شاہد اصل یعنی بکر اس کو اپنی گواہی پر گواہ بنادے تو اس شاہد فرع یعنی زید کے لئے گواہی دینا جائز ہے۔ دلیل اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اصول کی شہادت بذات خود حکم واجب نہیں کرتی ہے۔ چنانچہ بکر کے محض گواہ ہونے سے حامد پر قرض واجب نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اصول (اصلی گواہوں) کی شہادت اس وقت حکم واجب کرتی ہے جب اصول اپنی شہادت قاضی کی مجلس میں منتقل کردیں۔ بہر حال اصل کی شہادت بذات خود موجب حکم نہیں ہے۔ پس جب اصول کی شہادت بذات خود موجب حکم نہیں ہے بلکہ موجب حکم بنانے کے لئے اسکو قاضی کی مجلس میں نقل کرنا ضروری ہے تو اصول (اصل گواہوں) کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ فروغ پر شہادت کا بوجھ رکھیں اور ادائے شہادت میں ان کو اپنا نائب مقرر کریں تا کہ فروع ، اصول کی شہادت کو قاضی کی مجلس میں نقل کر سکیں۔ اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ فروع کا گواہی دینا اصول کے حق میں تصرف کرنا ہے اس طور پر کہ مشہود علیہ ( مدعی علیہ ) کے خلاف قول نافذ ہونے میں اصول کو ولایت حاصل تھی۔ یعنی اصول کو یہ ولایت حاصل تھی کہ وہ اپنا قول ( گواہی ) مشہود علیہ کے خلاف نافذ کر دیں ۔ مگر جب فروع نے اصول کی طرف سے گواہی نقل کی تو گویا فروع نے اصول کی اس ولایت کو زائل کر دیا جو ولایت اصول کیلئے ثابت تھی۔ اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ کسی کو کسی کی ولایت اور حق بغیر اس کی رضا مندی کے زائل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے لہذا شہود فرع کی شہادت کے لئے بھی اصول کی رضامندی ضروری ہوگی۔ اور اصول کی رضا مندی یہ ہے کہ اصول ، فروع کو اپنی طرف سے شاہد اور نائب مقرر کر دیں۔ پس متن کے مسئلہ مفروضہ میں چوں کہ اصول کی طرف سے فروغ پر شہادت کا بوجھ رکھنا ( شاہد بنانا ) پایا گیا اور نہ نائب مقرر کرنا پایا گیا اس لئے فروع کا محض اصول کی گواہی سنگر گواہی دینا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
اسی طرح اگر کسی نے حقیقی اور اصلی گواہ سنا کہ وہ اپنی گواہی پر کسی کو گواہ کرتا ہے تو سامع ( سننے والے کو ) اصلی گواہ کی گواہی پر گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً حامد نے سنا کہ خالد (اصلی گواہ) اپنی گواہی پر شاہد کو گواہ کرتا ہے تو سامع یعنی حامد کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ وہ خالد (اصلی گواہ) کی گواہی پر گواہی دے۔ کیونکہ اصلی گواہ نے اپنی گواہی کا بوجھ اس سننے والے حامد پر نہیں رکھا بلکہ اس کے علاوہ شاہد پر رکھا ہے۔
ہاں شاہد جس کو خالد نے اپنی گواہی پر گواہ کیا ہے وہ گواہی دے سکتا ہے۔ لیکن حامد گواہی نہیں دے سکتا ہے۔
Second category: Testimony that does not become established by itself. And from it is that whose ruling does not become established by itself, such as testimony on testimony. So if he hears a witness testifying about something, it is not permissible for him to testify on his testimony unless he appoints him over it, because testimony is not effective by itself; rather, it becomes effective by transfer to the court of the judge. Hence, deputation and burden-carrying are necessary, and they were not present. Similarly, if he hears the witness testifying on someone else's testimony, it is not permissible for the listener to testify because he did not carry the burden from him; rather, he carried it from someone else. Translation: And among these is a category whose ruling does not become established by itself, like giving testimony on testimony. So when someone hears a witness testifying about something, it is not permissible for him to testify on his testimony, unless he makes him a witness over it, because testimony is not effective by itself; rather, it becomes effective by transfer to the court of the judge. So it is necessary for the original witness to make him a deputy and place the burden of testimony on him, but none of that was found. And likewise, if someone hears the original witness that he is making a secondary witness a witness over his testimony, then it is not permissible for the listener to testify, because the original witness did not place the burden of testimony on the listener; rather, he placed it on someone else. Explanation: The second of the two mentioned categories is that whose ruling does not become established by itself, but rather requires making someone a witness. Like testimony on testimony: as long as the original witness does not appoint someone as a witness on his testimony, the ruling for the secondary witnesses to give testimony is not established. For example, if someone (e.g., Zayd) hears a witness (e.g., Bakr) outside the judge's session testifying that Khalid owes Hamid one thousand dirhams, then it is not permissible for the secondary witness, i.e., Zayd, to testify that Khalid owes Hamid one thousand dirhams. Yes, if the original witness, i.e., Bakr, makes him a witness over his testimony, then it is permissible for the secondary witness, i.e., Zayd, to testify. The proof: the testimony of the original witnesses does not make a ruling obligatory by itself. Thus, by Bakr merely being a witness, the debt is not obligatory on Hamid; rather, the testimony of the original witnesses makes the ruling obligatory when they transfer their testimony to the judge's court. In any case, the testimony of the original is not effective by itself. So when the testimony of the original is not effective by itself, but rather to make it effective, it must be transferred to the judge's court, then it is necessary for the original witnesses to place the burden of testimony on the secondary witnesses and appoint them as their deputies in performing the testimony, so that the secondary witnesses can transfer the testimony of the original witnesses to the judge's court. The reason for this is that giving testimony by secondary witnesses is an act of disposal with respect to the right of the original witnesses, in the sense that the original witnesses had the authority to enforce their statement against the defendant. That is, the original witnesses had the authority to enforce their statement (testimony) against the defendant. But when the secondary witnesses transfer the testimony from the original side, they effectively nullify that authority of the original witnesses, which was established for them. And it is uncontested that it is not permissible to nullify someone's authority and right without his consent. Therefore, for the testimony of secondary witnesses, the consent of the original witnesses is necessary. And the consent of the original witnesses is that the original witnesses appoint the secondary witnesses as witnesses and deputies from their side. So in the assumed issue of the text, since neither placing the burden of testimony (making a witness) nor appointing a deputy was found from the original witnesses, therefore the secondary witnesses giving testimony merely by hearing the original witness's testimony is not permissible. Similarly, if someone heard the real and original witness that he is making someone a witness over his testimony, then it is not permissible for the listener to testify on the original witness's testimony. For example, Hamid heard that Khalid (original witness) is making a witness over his testimony, then the listener, i.e., Hamid, does not have the right to testify on the testimony of Khalid (original witness), because the original witness did not place the burden of his testimony on this listener, but rather on someone else. Yes, the witness whom Khalid made a witness over his testimony can testify, but Hamid cannot testify.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage discusses the second category of testimony: that which does not establish its ruling by itself, exemplified by testimony on testimony (shahada ala al-shahada). The Hanafi ruling is that a secondary witness (shahid far') cannot testify based solely on hearing the original witness (shahid asl) testify; the original witness must formally appoint the secondary witness to bear the testimony. The reasoning is that testimony itself is not self-executing; it becomes effective only when presented in court. The original witness has the authority (wilaya) to enforce his testimony against the defendant. For the secondary witness to convey that testimony to court, he must be deputized by the original witness, as failing to do so would usurp the original witness's authority without consent. Therefore, if someone merely hears an original witness testify outside court, he cannot repeat that testimony in court. Likewise, if someone hears an original witness appointing someone else as a secondary witness, the listener cannot testify because the burden was not placed on him. Only the specifically appointed secondary witness may testify. This ruling ensures that the chain of testimony remains clear and authorized.

Key Terms
شهادة على الشهادة (shahāda ʿalā al-shahāda): Testimony on testimony; a secondary witness testifying based on the original witness's testimony.
شاہد اصل (shāhid aṣl): Original witness; the person who directly witnessed the event and gives testimony.
شاہد فرع (shāhid farʿ): Secondary witness; a person who testifies on the testimony of the original witness.
تحمیل (taḥmīl): Placing the burden of testimony; the act of the original witness burdening the secondary witness to convey the testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for a secondary witness to validly testify on the testimony of an original witness?
A) The secondary witness must be present when the event occurred
B) The original witness must formally appoint the secondary witness to carry the testimony
C) The secondary witness must be a relative of the original witness
D) The secondary witness must hear the testimony in court

Key Takeaway
Testimony on testimony in Hanafi fiqh is valid only if the original witness explicitly appoints the secondary witness and places the burden of testimony on him.

Shahadat — Testimony

The Requirement of Deputization in Testimony upon Testimony
Explaining the need for original witness to deputize secondary witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for the validity of testimony upon testimony and explain the rationale based on the principle of deputization (tawkil).

Core Idea
No testimony upon testimony without deputization: the original witness must appoint the secondary witness as his deputy.

Testimony upon testimony (shahada ala al-shahada) allows a secondary witness to convey the testimony of an original witness to the court. However, the Hanafi school conditions this on the original witness explicitly appointing the secondary witness as his deputy. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this requirement and illustrates it with concrete examples from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The passage rules that a secondary witness (shahid far') may testify only if the original witness (shahid asl) has explicitly appointed him as a deputy (na'ib). Without such deputization, the secondary witness's testimony is not permissible.
The key term is 'tawkil' – deputization.
2
Understand the rationale (talil)
Testimony does not create a legal obligation by itself; it becomes binding only when transferred to the judge's court. The original witness must therefore delegate this transfer to the secondary witness. The secondary witness's testimony is a disposal of the original witness's authority (wilayah), which cannot be done without consent.
The analogy is drawn from the general principle that one cannot dispose of another's right without permission.
3
Apply the condition to the given example
If Zaid hears Bakr (original witness) state outside court that Khalid owes Hamid 1000 dirhams, Zaid cannot testify unless Bakr designated Zaid as his deputy. Mere hearing is insufficient.
The example emphasizes that the deputization must be explicit and specific.
4
Distinguish between direct and indirect hearing
Even if Hamid hears Bakr appointing someone else (e.g., 'Amr) as deputy, Hamid himself cannot testify because he was not the one appointed. The burden of testimony was placed on 'Amr, not Hamid.
This reinforces the requirement of individual deputization.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
Unlike the Hanafi school, other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may not require explicit deputization; they may accept the secondary witness's reliability alone. The Hanafi position is stricter to protect the original witness's authority.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions have their proofs.
