اسی طرح اگر کسی نے حقیقی اور اصلی گواہ سنا کہ وہ اپنی گواہی پر کسی کو گواہ کرتا ہے تو سامع ( سننے والے کو ) اصلی گواہ کی گواہی پر گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً حامد نے سنا کہ خالد (اصلی گواہ) اپنی گواہی پر شاہد کو گواہ کرتا ہے تو سامع یعنی حامد کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہے کہ وہ خالد (اصلی گواہ) کی گواہی پر گواہی دے۔ کیونکہ اصلی گواہ نے اپنی گواہی کا بوجھ اس سننے والے حامد پر نہیں رکھا بلکہ اس کے علاوہ شاہد پر رکھا ہے۔
ہاں شاہد جس کو خالد نے اپنی گواہی پر گواہ کیا ہے وہ گواہی دے سکتا ہے۔ لیکن حامد گواہی نہیں دے سکتا ہے۔
Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume Ten. A person who gives testimony, it is not permissible for him to give testimony upon his testimony unless he makes him a witness upon his testimony, because testimony by itself is not binding; rather, it becomes binding by transferring it to the court of the judge. So it is necessary that the original witness make him his deputy and place the burden of testimony upon him. When none of this was found, likewise if someone heard the original witness making the secondary witness a witness upon his testimony, it is not permissible for the hearer to give testimony, because the original witness did not place the burden of testimony on the hearer, but on someone else. Explanation: Of the two mentioned types, the second type is that whose ruling is not established by itself, but rather requires making a witness. Like testimony upon testimony: as long as the original witnesses do not make someone a witness upon their testimony, the ruling for the secondary witnesses to give testimony is not established. For example, if someone (e.g., Zaid) heard the witness (e.g., Bakr) outside the judge's session that Bakr testifies that Khalid owes Hamid one thousand dirhams, then it is not permissible for the secondary witness Zaid to testify that Khalid owes Hamid one thousand dirhams. Yes, if the original witness Bakr makes him a witness upon his testimony, then it is permissible for the secondary witness Zaid to give testimony. The proof for this is that the testimony of the original witnesses does not make the ruling obligatory by itself. Thus, merely Bakr being a witness does not make the debt obligatory upon Hamid; rather, the testimony of the original witnesses makes the ruling obligatory when they transfer their testimony to the judge's court. In any case, the original testimony by itself is not the cause of the ruling. So when the original testimony by itself is not the cause of the ruling, but rather to make it the cause of the ruling it is necessary to transfer it to the judge's court, then it is necessary for the original witnesses to place the burden of testimony upon the secondary witnesses and appoint them as their deputies in the performance of testimony, so that the secondary witnesses can transfer the testimony of the original witnesses to the judge's court. And the reason for this is that the secondary witnesses giving testimony is a disposal of the right of the original witnesses, in that the original witnesses had authority (wilayah) to make their statement effective against the defendant. When the secondary witnesses transferred the testimony on behalf of the original witnesses, they effectively nullified that authority which was established for the original witnesses. And it is established that it is not permissible to nullify someone's authority or right without their consent. Therefore, for the testimony of the secondary witnesses, the consent of the original witnesses is necessary. And the consent of the original witnesses is that they appoint the secondary witnesses as witnesses and deputies from themselves. So in the supposed case of the text, since placing the burden of testimony upon the secondary witnesses (making them witnesses) and appointing them as deputies from the original witnesses was not found, therefore the secondary witnesses merely hearing the testimony of the original witnesses will not permit them to give testimony. Similarly, if someone heard the real original witness that he is making someone a witness upon his testimony, then it is not permissible for the hearer to give testimony upon the testimony of the original witness. For example, Hamid heard that Khalid (the original witness) is making a witness a witness upon his testimony, then the hearer Hamid does not have the authority to give testimony upon the testimony of Khalid (the original witness). Because the original witness did not place the burden of his testimony upon this hearer Hamid, but upon someone else, the witness. Yes, the witness whom Khalid made a witness upon his testimony can give testimony, but Hamid cannot give testimony.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the ruling of testimony upon testimony (shahada ala al-shahada). The passage is of the type 'ruling with proof' as it provides a legal ruling and a rational argument (talil) for it. The central ruling is that a secondary witness (shahid far') can only testify if the original witness (shahid asl) has explicitly appointed him as a deputy to convey the testimony to the judge. The reasoning is that testimony (shahada) does not create a legal obligation by itself; rather, it only becomes effective when it is transferred to the judge's court. Therefore, the original witness must entrust this transfer to the secondary witness. The commentary elaborates using an example: if Zaid hears Bakr (original witness) say outside court that Khalid owes Hamid 1000 dirhams, Zaid cannot testify about this debt unless Bakr has designated Zaid as a deputy for that testimony. Similarly, if a person (e.g., Hamid) hears the original witness appointing someone else as a deputy, Hamid himself cannot testify, because the burden has not been placed on him. The underlying principle is that the secondary witness's testimony is a disposal (tasarruf) of the original witness's right (wilayah) to make his testimony binding. Disposing someone's right without consent is impermissible, hence the need for explicit deputization.

Key Terms
شہادت علی الشہادت (shahada ala al-shahada): Testimony upon testimony; a secondary witness testifying based on the testimony of an original witness.
شاہد اصل (shahid asl): The original witness who directly witnessed the event or transaction.
شاہد فرع (shahid far'): The secondary witness who testifies on the basis of the original witness's testimony.

Key Takeaway
Testimony upon testimony is valid only when the original witness explicitly deputizes the secondary witness.

Testifying by Seeing One's Own Handwriting: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony by writing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding testifying based on one's own handwriting, identify the illah (reason) for Abu Hanifa's position, and apply the dispute to the judge's own records.

Core Idea
Handwriting resembles handwriting—certainty is lost; recollection is required according to Abu Hanifa.

In Hanafi fiqh, the evidentiary value of handwriting is debated between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples. This lesson examines the ruling on a witness who sees his own writing but does not recall the event. We will also explore a parallel dispute concerning a judge finding testimony in his own court records.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling per Abu Hanifa
The act is a witness testifying based on seeing his own handwriting without remembering the testimony. Abu Hanifa rules it is not permissible (la yahillu).
The primary issue is lack of certainty (yaqin) due to resemblance.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's position and its basis
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold it is permissible. Their basis is that one's own handwriting is a reliable personal mark that provides assurance (ghalabat al-zann).
The text does not quote their dalil directly but implies trust in personal writing.
3
Trace the illah for Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa's illah is that handwriting resembles handwriting (al-khatt yushbihu al-khatt), so no certainty is obtained. Doubt prevents testimony.
This is a talil (reasoning) based on the nature of writing—it can be forged or mistaken.
4
Compare with the judge's record scenario
The text distinguishes between a judge finding testimony in his own sealed register (diwan/qadiyya) and in a document (sakk) in someone else's hand. The dispute extends: Abu Hanifa and Shafi'i do not allow ruling from memory alone; Sahibayn and Malik allow it.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in the judge's records, the seal ensures authenticity; in a sakk, there is no such guarantee.

اور مشتبہ چیز علم اور یقین کا فائدہ نہیں دیتی ہے۔ لہذا اس تحریر سے علم حاصل نہ ہو گا۔ حالانکہ شہادت کیلئے اس واقعہ کا علم ضروری ہے جس واقعہ سے متعلق شہادت دی جاتی ہے۔ پس جب شہادت دینے کیلئے مشہور بہ کا جاننا ضروری ہے اور ندوره تحریر سے علم حاصل نہیں ہوتا تو نہ کر تحریر کو دیکھ کر گواہی دینا بھی جائز نہ ہو گا۔ صاحب قدوری نے اس مسئلہ میں کسی کا کوئی اختلاف و کر نہیں کیا ہے البتہ فقیہ ابو اللیث اور شمس الائک وغیرہ نے اختلاف ذکر کیا ہے۔ چنانچہ ان حضرات نے فرمایا ہے کہ تحر یا کچھ کر گوانین دینے کا جائز نہ ہونا حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کا مذہب ہے۔ کیونکہ حضرت امام صاحب تحریر پر عمل نہیں کرتے ہیں بلکہ تان کے وقت سے لے مراد نے شہادت کے وقت تک اس کو یا ور کھنا شرط قرار دیتے ہیں۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک تحریر دیکھ کر شہادت دینا جائز ہے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے فرمایا ہے کہ تحریر دیکھ کر شہادت کا جائز نہ ہونا متفق علیہ ہے۔ اور اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے جب قاضی نے اپنی فائل میں دیکھا کہ گواہوں نے اس کی عدالت میں گواہی دی ہے۔ لیکن حکم نہیں دیا گیا۔ پھر مشہودلہ ( مدعی ) نے اگر قاضی سے حکم کی درخواست کی مگر قاضی کو اس واقعہ سے متعلق اپنے پاس گواہوں کا گواہی دینا یاد نہ آیا تو حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس شہادت کی بنیاد پر حکم دینا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اس کے قائل امام شافعی ہیں اور امام احمد کی ایک روایت بھی یہی ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جب قاضی نے گواہ کی گواپنی کو اپنی فائل اور سل میں اپنی مہر کے تحت پایا تو اس گواہی کی بنیاد پر قاضی کا فیصلہ دینا جائز ہے۔ اس کے قائل امام مالک ہیں اور یہی ایک روایت امام احمد کی ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر قاضی نے اپنے حکم میں کسی گواہ کی گواہی کو پایا یعنی قاضی نے اپنی فائل میں اپنا ہی تحریر کردہ ایک حکم دیکھا اور اس حکم میں گواہوں کی گواہی بھی
Giving testimony by seeing one's own writing and its content. He said: It is not permissible for a witness when he sees his own handwriting to testify unless he remembers the testimony, because handwriting resembles handwriting, so certainty is not obtained. It is said this is according to the saying of Abu Hanifa, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is permissible for him to testify. And it is said that this is by agreement, and the difference is only when the judge finds testimony in his register (diwan) or his judgment record, because what is in his file is under his seal, safe from increase and decrease, so he obtains certainty thereby. But this is not the case for testimony in a document (sakk) because it is in the hand of another. And upon this, if he remembers the session in which the testimony occurred, or a trustworthy group informed him, 'We and you witnessed.' Translation: It is not permissible for a witness to testify by seeing his own handwriting unless he remembers the testimony, because one handwriting resembles another, so knowledge is not obtained. It is said that this is according to Abu Hanifa's saying, and according to the two (Sahibayn), it is permissible for him to testify. And it is said that this is agreed upon, and the difference is when the judge finds testimony in his file or his judgment record, because what is in his file is under his seal, safe from increase and decrease, so the judge obtains knowledge from it. And this is not the case for testimony in a document that is missing, because it is in the possession of another person. And upon this difference, when he remembers the session in which the testimony was given, or a trustworthy group informed him, 'We and you witnessed.' Explanation: Al-Quduri said that even if the witness saw his own writing in the document, but he did not remember the event related to the testimony nor the giving of testimony, then it is not permissible for him to testify merely by seeing the writing. Because one handwriting resembles another, and when one handwriting resembles another, it becomes doubtful whether the writing is that of this witness or someone else's. And a doubtful thing does not provide knowledge and certainty. Therefore, knowledge is not obtained from this writing. Although for testimony, knowledge of the event concerning which testimony is given is necessary. So when knowledge of the testifying is necessary and knowledge is not obtained from the writing, then testifying by seeing the writing is also not permissible. Al-Quduri did not mention any difference in this matter; however, Faqih Abu al-Layth and Shams al-A'immah etc. mentioned a difference. According to these gentlemen, testifying by seeing writing is not permissible; this is the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa. Because Imam Abu Hanifa does not act upon writing, but rather stipulates that he remember from the time of the event up to the time of testimony. And according to the two (Sahibayn), testifying by seeing writing is permissible. And some gentlemen said that testifying by seeing writing is not permissible by agreement, and the difference is when the judge saw in his file that witnesses gave testimony in his court but he did not give a verdict. Then the plaintiff requested a verdict from the judge, but the judge did not remember the witnesses giving testimony regarding that event. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is not permissible to give a verdict based on that testimony. This is also the view of Imam Shafi'i and one narration from Imam Ahmad. And according to the two (Sahibayn), when the judge found the witness's testimony in his file and record under his seal, it is permissible for the judge to give a decision based on that testimony. This is the view of Imam Malik and also one narration from Imam Ahmad. Similarly, if the judge found in his judgment the testimony of some witnesses, meaning the judge saw in his file a judgment written by himself and in that judgment the testimony of witnesses also...
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on a witness who sees his own handwriting (khatt) but does not remember the event or the testimony itself. The type is 'intra-Hanafi dispute' because it presents the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the witness cannot testify based solely on seeing his handwriting; he must recall the testimony. The reasoning is that handwriting can be imitated, leading to doubt. The Sahibayn hold that seeing one's own handwriting is sufficient proof for testimony, as it provides certainty. The text also mentions a second dispute related to a judge finding testimony in his own records (diwan or qadiyya). Some say the disagreement is only in that scenario: Abu Hanifa (and al-Shafi'i) do not allow the judge to base a ruling on such records without independent memory, while Sahibayn (and Malik) allow it because the judge's own records under his seal are trustworthy. The commentary by al-Quduri emphasizes Abu Hanifa's view that writing is insufficient without memory, but later scholars like Abu al-Layth and Shams al-A'immah note the difference between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn. The passage thus provides a nuanced understanding of the evidentiary value of one's own handwriting in testimony.

Key Terms
الخط (al-khatt): Handwriting; the writing of the witness himself.
الشهادة بالكتابة (al-shahada bi al-kitaba): Testimony based on written record, specifically one's own handwriting.
الصک (al-sakk): A legal document or instrument, in contrast to the judge's official records.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is it not permissible for a witness to testify based solely on seeing his own handwriting?
A) Because handwriting is not a legal proof at all
B) Because handwriting resembles handwriting, leading to doubt and lack of certainty
C) Because the witness might be lying
D) Because the document may be forged by others

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, testifying by one's own handwriting requires recollection according to Abu Hanifa, but Sahibayn accept handwriting as sufficient; the dispute turns on the standard of certainty in testimony.

Testifying from One's Own Handwriting Without Memory
Ruling with proof on testimony by handwriting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testifying by handwriting alone and distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions.

Core Idea
Handwriting alone is insufficient for testimony—certain knowledge is required.

This passage addresses a key issue in Islamic testimony law: can a witness testify when they see their own handwriting but have no recollection of the event? The Hanafi school's approach hinges on the requirement of certainty (yaqin). Abu Hanifa held that handwriting resemblance prevents certainty, while his two major students allowed it under certain conditions. Let's unpack the ruling and its proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on a witness who sees his own handwriting but does not recall the testimony. According to Abu Hanifa, it is not permissible (haram) to testify. Identify this as the primary ruling.
The ruling is based on lack of certain knowledge.
2
Understand the reasoning (dalil aqli)
The proof given is 'handwriting resembles handwriting' (al-khatt yushbihu al-khatt), so no certainty is attained. Recognize this as a rational proof that testimony requires ilm.
The resemblance prevents certainty.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
The text mentions that according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is permissible to testify. Identify the difference: Abu Hanifa prohibits; Sahibayn allow.
The Sahibayn view is permissible.
4
Distinguish the case of the judge's register (diwan)
The passage explains that the dispute is only for private documents. For the judge's own register under seal, even Abu Hanifa may allow it due to security. Understand the exception: the diwan provides certainty.
The judge's diwan is under seal, preventing tampering.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Abu Hanifa's prohibition, as stated in the matn. Conclude that testifying by handwriting alone without memory is not valid.
The mufta bihi is prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يحل للشاهد اذا راى خطه أن يشهد الا ان يتذكر الشهادة لان الخط يشبه الخط فلم يحصل العلم قيل هذا على قول أبي حنيفة وعندهما يحل له ان يشهد و قيل هذا بالاتفاق وانما الخلاف فيما اذا وجد القاضي شهادة في ديوانه او قضيته لان ما يكون في قمطره فهو تحت ختمه يؤمن عليه من الزيادة والنقصان فحصل له العلم بذلك ولا كذالك الشهادة في الصك لانه في يد غيره وعلى هذا اذا تذكر المجلس الذى كان فيه الشهادة او اخبره قوم ممن يثق به انا شهدنا نحن وانت
He said: It is not permissible for the witness, when he sees his handwriting, to testify unless he remembers the testimony, because handwriting resembles handwriting, so certainty is not attained. It is said this is according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two companions it is permissible for him to testify. And it is said this is by agreement, and the disagreement is only when the judge finds testimony in his register or his judgment document, because what is in his file is under his seal, secure from addition and deletion, so certainty is obtained thereby. But not so for testimony in a deed because it is in another's hand. And on this, if he remembers the session in which the testimony occurred, or a trustworthy group informs him that 'we and you witnessed', then...
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on witnessing based on handwriting. The ruling states that a witness who sees his own handwriting but does not recall the event cannot testify, because handwriting can be similar to other handwriting, leading to doubt. According to al-Quduri, this is the position of Abu Hanifa, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) permit it. However, some later scholars (like Abu al-Layth) say the disagreement is only when the judge finds testimony in his own official records (diwan or qadiyya) under his seal, which provides certainty; otherwise, it's agreed that testifying by handwriting alone is impermissible. The text also mentions that if the witness remembers the council or is informed by reliable people, different rulings apply. The commentary clarifies that the majority (including al-Quduri) hold that testifying by mere handwriting is prohibited, but the Sahibayn allow it. The judge's records are secure, so he can rely on them; a private deed is not.

Key Terms
الخط (al-khatt): Handwriting, the script or writing style of a person.
الشهادة (al-shahada): Testimony, giving witness in court about a fact.
ديوان (diwan): Register or official record of the judge containing case documents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because handwriting can be forged and is not reliable.
B) Because handwriting resembles handwriting, so no certain knowledge is attained.
C) Because the witness must have seen the event directly.
D) Because testimony requires two witnesses.

Key Takeaway
Testimony requires certain knowledge; handwriting alone does not provide it, so it is impermissible to testify without memory.

Testifying Without Direct Observation: Hanafi Exceptions
Exceptions to direct observation requirement for witness testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five exceptions to direct observation in Hanafi witness testimony and apply the conditions required for hearsay testimony.

Core Idea
Hearsay testimony is accepted for five private matters to avoid hardship, overriding the general qiyas.

In Hanafi law, a witness normally must have directly observed the event. However, for certain matters that are difficult to observe — lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and the judge's jurisdiction — hearsay testimony is accepted by istihsan (juristic preference). This lesson explains the reasoning, conditions, and procedural requirements for such testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and the exception
State the default rule: testimony requires direct observation. Then list the five exceptions from the text: lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and judge's jurisdiction.
2
Analyze the qiyas argument for prohibition
Understand why analogy (qiyas) would reject hearsay: testimony (shahada) is derived from witnessing (mushahada), so without observation there is no knowledge, just like in a sale.
3
Understand the istihsan reasoning for the exceptions
These matters are private; only a few witness their causes. If hearsay were not accepted, rulings (e.g., inheritance) would be suspended, causing hardship. This practical necessity justifies the exception.
This is a clear application of istihsan overriding qiyas.
4
List the conditions for valid hearsay testimony
The witness must be informed by two just men or one man and two women (except death: one person suffices). The informant must be trusted. The testimony must be given absolutely, without specifying 'by hearsay'.
Specifying hearsay invalidates the testimony.
5
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., a death witnessed by only one person), determine if hearsay testimony is admissible and under what conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يجوز للشاهدان يشهد بشئ لم يعاينه الا النسب والموت والنكاح والدخول وولاية القاضى فانه يسعه ان يشهد بهذه الاشياء اذا اخبره بها من يثق به وهذا استحسان والقياس ان لا تجوز لان الشهادة مشتقة من المشاهدة و ذالك بالعلم ولم يحصل فصار كالبيع وجه الاستحسان ان هذه الامور تختص بمعاينة اسبابها خواص من الناس ويتعلق بها احكام تبقى على انقضاء القرون فلو لم يقبل فيها الشهادة بالتسامع ادى الى الحرج وتعطيل الاحكام بخلاف البيع لانه يسمع كل واحد وانما يجوز للشاهد ان يشهد با اشتهار و ذالک بالتواتر او باخبار من يثق به كما قال فى الكتاب ويشترط ان يخبره رجلان عدلان او رجل وامرأتان ليحصل له نوع علم وقيان الموت يكتفى باخبار واحدا وواحدة لانه قلما يشاهد حاله غير الواحد اذ الانسان يهابه ويكرهه فيكون في اشتراط العدد بعض الخروج ولا كذالك النسب والنكاح وينبغى أن يطلق اداء الشهادة ولا يفسّر اما اذا فسّر للقاضى انه يشهد بالتسامع لم يقبل شهادته كما ان معاينة اليد في الاملاك مطلق للشهادة ثم اذا فسر لا يقبل كذا لهذا
He said: It is not permissible for the two witnesses to testify to something they have not observed except lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and the judge's jurisdiction. For it is permissible for him to testify to these things when informed by someone he trusts. This is istihsan, and the qiyas is that it is not permissible, because testimony is derived from witnessing, and that requires knowledge, which is not attained, so it becomes like a sale. The basis of istihsan is that these matters are only witnessed in their causes by special people, and rulings related to them persist across generations. If testimony by hearsay were not accepted, it would lead to hardship and suspension of rulings, unlike sale because it is heard by everyone. And it is permissible for the witness to testify based on widespread fame (tawatur) or the report of one he trusts, as stated in the book. And it is required that two just men or one man and two women inform him so that some knowledge is attained. However, for death, the report of one person (man or woman) is sufficient because rarely does more than one witness the death, as people fear and avoid the deceased. So stipulating numbers would cause hardship. Not so for lineage and marriage. And he should state his testimony absolutely and not specify. If he specifies to the judge that he is testifying by hearsay, his testimony is not accepted, just as in the case of witnessing a hand in property matters, the testimony is absolute, but if specified, it is not accepted.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage deals with exceptions to the general rule that a witness must have direct observation (mu'ayana). By qiyas (analogy), testimony on hearsay is invalid, but by istihsan (juristic preference), certain matters are excepted: nasab (lineage), mawt (death), nikah (marriage), dukhul (consummation), and wilayah al-qadi (judge's jurisdiction). The reasoning is that these matters are private or rare, and if hearsay were not accepted, many necessary legal rulings (like inheritance after death) would be impossible. The witness must have heard from trusted sources (two just men or one man and two women) except for death, where one person suffices due to rarity of witnesses at death. The testimony should be given absolutely; if the witness explicitly says he is testifying by hearsay, it is not accepted. This istihsan overcomes the qiyas based on the etymology of shahada (from mushahada, witnessing).

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in exceptional cases for practical necessity.
التسامع (al-tasammu'): Hearsay; receiving information by oral report rather than direct observation.
المشاهدة (al-mushahada): Direct witnessing or observation of an event.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Two just men
B) One man and two women
C) One person, man or woman
D) No informants are needed if the death is well-known

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, five private matters allow hearsay testimony by istihsan, overriding qiyas, with specific conditions on the number of informants and the form of testimony.

Testimony Without Direct Observation: The Five Exceptions and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Written Records
Ruling with proof, intra-Hanafi dispute, and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five matters where hearsay testimony is permitted by istihsan, identify the conditions for each, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding testimony based on written records.

Core Idea
Hearsay testimony is prohibited by qiyas but permitted by istihsan for five matters; reliance on written records is disputed within the Hanafi school.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses two related topics in the law of testimony (shahada). First, it clarifies the general rule that a witness must have directly observed the event, but then lists five exceptional matters where hearsay is acceptable due to juristic preference (istihsan). Second, it presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement over whether a judge or witness can act based on written documents without independent memory. Understanding these nuances is crucial for correctly applying the laws of testimony in court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its basis
Start by noting the default position: testimony requires direct observation (mushahada). The term 'shahada' itself derives from 'mushahada'. The qiyas (analogy) with sale shows that without observation, testimony is invalid.
This establishes the general principle before exceptions.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute on written records
Examine the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding a judge's reliance on his file or a witness's reliance on his own writing. Understand each side's proof: Abu Hanifa cites lack of certainty due to possible forgery; the Sahibayn argue that under seal, the document is secure and provides knowledge.
This dispute is distinct from the five exceptions.
3
Understand the five exceptions and their rationale
List the five matters: lineage (nasab), death (mawt), marriage (nikah), consummation (dukhul), and the authority of a judge (wilayat al-qadi). Recognize that istihsan overrides qiyas to avoid hardship (haraj) and suspension of rulings that persist across generations.
These matters are not easily observed by many people.
4
Apply the conditions for hearsay testimony
For lineage and marriage, the witness must be informed by two just men or one man and two women. For death, one man or one woman suffices due to difficulty in finding multiple witnesses. This condition ensures a degree of reliable knowledge.
The conditions differ based on the nature of the matter.
5
Note the importance of not explaining (tafsir) when testifying
If a witness testifies without stating it is based on hearsay, it is accepted. If he explicitly says he is testifying by hearsay, it is rejected. This parallels the rule for property possession where explaining the basis can invalidate testimony.
The witness should avoid explaining to maintain the apparent validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة
۴۸
اشرف الہدایہ جلد و سمر
چونکہ تحریر تھی اس لئے گواہی کو بھی دیکھا مگر قاضی کو اپنا حکم دینا یاد نہ آیا تو حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ حکم جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔
حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل تو سابق میں گزر چکی ہے کہ ایک تحریر چونکہ مری تحریر کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے اس لئے یقینی علم حاصل نہ ہو گا حالانکہ شہادت کے لئے علم ( جاننا ) شرط ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ و چیز قاضی کے بستہ اور اس کی فائل میں موجود ہے وہ اسکی مہر کے تحت میں ہے اور جو چیز اس کی مہر کے تحت میں ہو وہ کمی بیشی سے بالکل مامون اور محفوظ ہوتی ہے۔ پس جب وہ شہادت جو اس کی فائل یا اس کے حکم نامہ میں ہے کی زیادتی سے محفوظ ہے تو اس کی وجہ سے قاضی کے لئے شہادت کا علم حاصل ہو جائے گا اور جب علم حاصل ہو گیا تو قاضی کیلئے حکم دینا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ اور اگر گواہ نے اپنی گواہی کسی دستاویز میں پائی اور اس کو یہ بھی علم ہو گیا کہ یہ اس کی تحریر ہے تو اس کو محض اپنی تحریرہ دیکھ کر گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ دستاویز قاضی کے علاوہ کے ہاتھ میں ہونے کی وجہ سے کمی زیادتی سے غیر محفوظ ہے۔ اور جب یہ دستاویز غیر محفوظ ہے تو اس سے علم حاصل نہ ہوگا اور جب علم حاصل نہیں ہوا تو اس کو دیکھ کر گواہی دینا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ یہی اختلاف اس وقت سے جب گواہ نے اس مجلس کو تو یاد کر لیا جس میں گواہی دی تھی مگر واقعہ یاد نہ آسکا۔ یا ایسی قوم نے اس کو خبر دی جن پر اس کو اعتماد ہے کہ ہم نے اور تو نے گواہی دی تھی مگر واقعہ یاد نہ آسکا یا ایسی قوم نے اس کو خبر دی جن پر اس کو اعتماد ہے کہ ہم نے اور تو نے گواہی دی تھی مگر گواہی سے متعلق واقعہ یاد نہ آسکا تو بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں بالاتفاق گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور بعض نے فرمایا که امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔
بغیر مشاہدہ کے کن چیزوں کی گواہی دے سکتا ہے
قال ولا يجوز للشاهدان يشهد بشئ لم يعاينه الا النسب والموت والنكاح والدخول وولاية القاضى فانه يسعه ان يشهد بهذه الاشياء اذا اخبره بها من يثق به وهذا استحسان والقياس ان لا تجوز لان الشهادة مشتقة من المشاهدة و ذالك بالعلم ولم يحصل فصار كالبيع وجه الاستحسان ان هذه الامور تختص بمعاينة اسبابها خواص من الناس ويتعلق بها احكام تبقى على انقضاء القرون فلو لم يقبل فيها الشهادة بالتسامع ادى الى الحرج وتعطيل الاحكام بخلاف البيع لانه يسمع كل واحد وانما يجوز للشاهد ان يشهد با اشتهار و ذالک بالتواتر او باخبار من يثق به كما قال فى الكتاب ويشترط ان يخبره رجلان عدلان او رجل وامرأتان ليحصل له نوع علم وقيان الموت يكتفى باخبار واحدا وواحدة لانه قلما يشاهد حاله غير الواحد اذ الانسان يهابه ويكرهه فيكون في اشتراط العدد بعض الخروج ولا كذالك النسب والنكاح وينبغى أن يطلق اداء الشهادة ولا يفسّر اما اذا فسّر للقاضى انه يشهد بالتسامع لم يقبل شهادته كما ان معاينة اليد في الاملاك مطلق للشهادة ثم اذا فسر لا يقبل كذا لهذا
ترجمہ گواہ کے لئے ایسی چیز کی گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے جس کا اس نے مشاہدہ نہیں کیا ہے سوائے نسب موت ، نکاح ، دخول اور ولایت قاضی کے اس کیلئے ان چیزوں کی گواہی جائز ہے بشرطیکہ اسکو ان چیزوں میں کسی ثقہ آدمی نے آگاہ کیا ہو اور یہ استحسان ہے اور قیاس یہ

كتاب الشهادة
اشرف الہدایہ جلد دہم ہے کہ جائز نہ ہو اسلئے کہ شہادت ، مشاہدہ سے مشتق ہے اور مشاہدہ معاینہ سے ہوتا ہے اور یہ حاصل نہیں ہوا تو یہ بیع کے مثل ہو گیا۔ اور استحسان کیوجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ امور ایسے ہیں جنکے اسباب کے معاینہ کیساتھ خاص خاص لوگ مختص ہیں اور ان امور کے ساتھ ایسے احکام متعلق ہوتے ہیں جو مدتیں گذرنے تک باقی رہتے ہیں۔ پس اگر ان امور میں باہم سننے پر گواہی قبول نہ ہو تو حرج لاحق ہوگا اور احکام معطل ہو جائیں گے۔ برخلاف بیع کے اس لئے کہ اس کو ہر شخص سنتا ہے اور سننے پر گواہ کو گواہی دینا اشتہار کے ساتھ جائز ہے اور یہ اشتہار تو اتر سے حاصل ہوگا۔ یا ثقہ آدمی کے خبر دینے سے۔ جیسا کہ قدوری میں کہا ہے اور شرط ہے گواہ کو دو عادل آدمی خبر دیں یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتیں عادل خبر دیں تا کہ اس کیلئے ایک گونہ علم حاصل ہو ۔ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ موت کی گواہی میں ایک مرد یا ایک عورت کے خبر دینے پر اکتفا کرے اسلئے کہ بہت کم ایک آدمی کے علاوہ میت کے حال کا مشاہدہ کرتا ہے۔ کیونکہ آدمی موت سے ہیبت اور کراہت کرتا ہے تو عدد کی شرط لگانے میں کچھ حرج ہوگا۔ اور نسب اور نکاح ایسا نہیں ہے۔ اور مناسب ہے کہ ادائے شہادت کو مطلق رکھے۔ اور اس کی تفسیر نہ کرے لیکن اگر اس نے قاضی کے سامنے تفسیر کر دی کہ وہ سنگر گواہی دیتا ہے تو قاضی اس کی گواہی کو قبول نہیں کرے گا ۔ جیسے املاک میں قبضہ کا مشاہدہ شہادت کی اجازت دیتا ہے پھر اگر گواہ نے تفسیر کر دی تو قبول نہ ہوگی اسی طرح یہاں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ گواہ کیلئے ایسی چیزوں کے بارے میں گواہی دینا جس کا اس نے مشاہدہ نہ کیا ہو جائز نہیں ہے البتہ پانچ چیزیں ایسی ہیں جن کے بارے میں بغیر مشاہدہ کے محض ثقہ لوگوں سے سنکر گواہی دینا جائز ہے۔

نسب سے مراد یہ ہے کہ مثلاً حامد نے لوگوں سے سنا کہ شاہد فلاں کا بیٹا ہے لیکن امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک خبر دینے والی جماعت ایسی ہو جس کا جھوٹ پر اتفاق بعید از عقل ہو اور صاحبین کے نزدیک دو عادل آدمی کافی ہیں ۔ پس اگر جان نے نسب کو اس طرح سُنا ہو تو اس کو یہ گواہی دینا حلال ہے کہ شاہد فلاں کا بیٹا ہے۔ موت کی صورت یہ ہے کہ گواہ مثلاً حامد نے لوگوں سے سُنا کہ فلاح مر گیا ہے یا لوگوں کو دیکھا کہ اس کے ساتھ تکلفین و تدفین مردوں جیسا معاملہ کرتے ہیں تو گواہ کے لئے اسکی موت کی گواہی دینا جائز ہے اگر چہ اس کا مشاہدہ نہ کیا ہو۔ نکاح کی صورت یہ ہے کہ گواہ نے لوگوں سے کہتے ہوئے سُنا کہ فلاں مرد نے فلاں عورت سے نکاح کیا ہے۔ تو گواہ نے اگر چہ نکاح کا مشاہدہ نہیں کیا ہے مگر اس کو نکاح کی گواہی دینا جائز ہے اور دخول کی صورت یہ ہے کہ گواہ نے لوگوں سے سنا کہ فلاں عورت فلاں مرد کی بیوی ہے۔ اور اس نے اس کے ساتھ دخول کیا ہے اگر چہ اس نے عقد نکاح اور دخول کا مشاہدہ نہ کیا ہو ۔ اور ولایت قاضی کی صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے لوگوں سے سنا کہ فلاں اس شہر کا قاضی ہے اور اس کو دیکھا کہ لوگوں میں فیصلے جاری کرتا ہے تو اس آدمی کو یہ گواہی دینا جائز ہے کہ فلاں شخص فلاب شہر کا قاضی ہے۔ اگر چہ امام مسلمین کی طرف سے اس کو قاضی بنانے کا مشاہدہ نہ کیا ہو ۔ بہر حال ان پانچ چیزوں کے بارے میں ثقہ لوگوں سے سنکر گواہی دینا جائز ہے اگر چہ انکا مشاہدہ نہ کیا ہو۔ لیکن یہ حکم استحسانی ہے ورنہ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ محض سنگر گواہی دینا جائز نہ ہو کیونکہ شہادت ، مشاہدہ سے مشتق ہے اور مشاہدہ دیکھ کر ہوتا ہے نہ کہ سُن کر۔ حالانکہ مذکورہ پانچوں چیزوں میں معاینہ اور دیکھنا نہیں پایا گیا تو یہ چیزیں بیچ کے مانند ہوگئیں یعنی جس طرح محض سنکر بغیر دیکھے بیع کی شہادت دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح بمقتضائے قیاس محض سن کر ان چیزوں کی گواہی دینا بھی نا جائز ہے۔ و ذالک بالعلم
He said: It is not permissible for two witnesses to testify to something they did not witness except lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and the authority of the judge. For it is permissible for him to testify to these things if someone he trusts informs him of them. This is istihsan. The qiyas is that it is not permissible, because testimony is derived from witnessing, and that is by knowledge, and it has not been obtained, so it becomes like a sale. The face of istihsan is that these matters are such that only special people are involved in witnessing their causes, and rulings related to them persist over the generations. So if testimony by hearsay were not accepted in them, it would lead to hardship and suspension of rulings, unlike a sale because everyone hears it. And it is permissible for a witness to testify based on notoriety (ishtihar) by tawatur or by the report of someone he trusts, as stated in the book. It is a condition that two just men or one man and two women inform him so that some kind of knowledge is obtained. For death, it is said that the report of one man or one woman suffices, because rarely does anyone other than one person witness his state, since people fear and dislike him, so stipulating a number would involve some difficulty. Not so for lineage and marriage. And it is recommended that he utter the testimony absolutely and not explain it. If he explains to the judge that he is testifying by hearsay, his testimony is not accepted, just as in property (amlak) the witnessing of possession (mu'ayana al-yad) permits testimony, then if he explains, it is not accepted. Similarly here.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya deals with two distinct but related issues in the law of testimony (shahada). The first is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a judge's ruling based on his written records or a witness testifying from his own writing without independent memory of the event. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a judge cannot issue a ruling based solely on his file if he does not independently remember the ruling, because writing can be forged and does not provide certain knowledge, which is a condition for testimony. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that since the document is under the judge's seal, it is protected from tampering and thus provides sufficient knowledge to act upon. Similarly, a witness who finds his own testimony in a document but does not recall the event cannot testify based on that document according to Abu Hanifa, because the document is not in the judge's custody and thus not immune to alteration. The Sahibayn hold it permissible. The second part addresses the general rule that a witness cannot testify to something he did not observe directly, with five exceptions: lineage (nasab), death (mawt), marriage (nikah), consummation (dukhul), and the authority of a judge (wilayat al-qadi). This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) to avoid hardship (haraj) and the suspension of legal rulings, as these matters involve events that cannot always be witnessed by many people and whose effects persist over generations. The qiyas (analogy) with sale would require direct observation, but istihsan overrides this. The conditions for hearsay testimony are that the witness must be informed by reliable people: two just men or one man and two women, except for death where one man or one woman suffices due to the difficulty of finding witnesses. If a witness testifies without explaining that it is by hearsay, it is accepted; but if he explains, it is rejected, analogous to witnessing possession in property cases.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony given in court; the act of bearing witness.
مشاهدة (mushāhada): Direct observation or eyewitness.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a stronger reason, here to avoid hardship.
تسامع (tasāmuʿ): Hearsay; information passed on by others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for a witness to testify about marriage based on hearsay?
A) He must have seen the marriage ceremony.
B) He must be informed by two just men or one man and two women.
C) He must be informed by one man only.
D) He must have read the marriage contract.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits hearsay testimony by istihsan for lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and the judge's authority, with specific conditions, and there is an intra-school dispute on the validity of testimony based on written records.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
8 min
The Five Exceptional Matters for Hearsay Testimony
Lists the five hearsay exceptions and contrasts with qiyās

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five matters where hearsay testimony is permitted by istihsān and identify the default rule of qiyās.

Core Idea
Five matters allow hearsay testimony by istihsān: lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and judge appointment.

The general rule in Hanafi fiqh is that testimony requires direct observation (mushāhadah). However, by istihsān (juristic preference), five specific matters are excepted: lineage (nasab), death (mawt), marriage (nikāh), consummation (dukhūl), and appointment of a judge (wilāyat al-qāḍī). This lesson introduces these exceptions and the basic reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
State the general principle: testimony (shahādah) is derived from mushāhadah (direct observation). Therefore, testifying without seeing is impermissible by qiyās.
The word shahādah shares the root sh-h-d, meaning to witness, which implies presence and observation.
2
List the five exceptional matters
From the passage, extract the five matters: nasab (lineage), mawt (death), nikāh (marriage), dukhūl (consummation), and wilāyat al-qāḍī (appointment of a judge). These are the only cases where hearsay is allowed.
Some texts list 'nikāh' but the passage includes both marriage and consummation as separate matters.
3
Understand the legal status
The ruling is that testifying by hearsay for these five matters is permissible (jā'iz) by istihsān, not obligatory. It is an exception to the general prohibition.
The permissibility is specific to these five; for all other matters, qiyās applies and hearsay is not accepted.

اشرف الہدایہ جلد دہم ہے کہ جائز نہ ہو اسلئے کہ شہادت ، مشاہدہ سے مشتق ہے اور مشاہدہ معاینہ سے ہوتا ہے اور یہ حاصل نہیں ہوا تو یہ بیع کے مثل ہو گیا۔ اور استحسان کیوجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ امور ایسے ہیں جنکے اسباب کے معاینہ کیساتھ خاص خاص لوگ مختص ہیں اور ان امور کے ساتھ ایسے احکام متعلق ہوتے ہیں جو مدتیں گذرنے تک باقی رہتے ہیں۔ پس اگر ان امور میں باہم سننے پر گواہی قبول نہ ہو تو حرج لاحق ہوگا اور احکام معطل ہو جائیں گے۔ برخلاف بیع کے اس لئے کہ اس کو ہر شخص سنتا ہے اور سننے پر گواہ کو گواہی دینا اشتہار کے ساتھ جائز ہے اور یہ اشتہار تو تواتر سے حاصل ہوگا۔ یا ثقہ آدمی کے خبر دینے سے۔ جیسا کہ قدوری میں کہا ہے اور شرط ہے گواہ کو دو عادل آدمی خبر دیں یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتیں عادل خبر دیں تا کہ اس کیلئے ایک گونہ علم حاصل ہو ۔ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ موت کی گواہی میں ایک مرد یا ایک عورت کے خبر دینے پر اکتفا کرے اسلئے کہ بہت کم ایک آدمی کے علاوہ میت کے حال کا مشاہدہ کرتا ہے۔ کیونکہ آدمی موت سے ہیبت اور کراہت کرتا ہے تو عدد کی شرط لگانے میں کچھ حرج ہوگا۔ اور نسب اور نکاح ایسا نہیں ہے۔ اور مناسب ہے کہ ادائے شہادت کو مطلق رکھے۔ اور اس کی تفسیر نہ کرے لیکن اگر اس نے قاضی کے سامنے تفسیر کر دی کہ وہ سنگر گواہی دیتا ہے تو قاضی اس کی گواہی کو قبول نہیں کرے گا ۔ جیسے املاک میں قبضہ کا مشاہدہ شہادت کی اجازت دیتا ہے پھر اگر گواہ نے تفسیر کر دی تو قبول نہ ہوگی اسی طرح یہاں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ گواہ کیلئے ایسی چیزوں کے بارے میں گواہی دینا جس کا اس نے مشاہدہ نہ کیا ہو جائز نہیں ہے البتہ پانچ چیزیں ایسی ہیں جن کے بارے میں بغیر مشاہدہ کے محض ثقہ لوگوں سے سنکر گواہی دینا جائز ہے۔

نسب سے مراد یہ ہے کہ مثلاً حامد نے لوگوں سے سنا کہ شاہد فلاں کا بیٹا ہے لیکن امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک خبر دینے والی جماعت ایسی ہو جس کا جھوٹ پر اتفاق بعید از عقل ہو اور صاحبین کے نزدیک دو عادل آدمی کافی ہیں ۔ پس اگر جان نے نسب کو اس طرح سُنا ہو تو اس کو یہ گواہی دینا حلال ہے کہ شاہد فلاں کا بیٹا ہے۔ موت کی صورت یہ ہے کہ گواہ مثلاً حامد نے لوگوں سے سُنا کہ فلاح مر گیا ہے یا لوگوں کو دیکھا کہ اس کے ساتھ تکلفین و تدفین مردوں جیسا معاملہ کرتے ہیں تو گواہ کے لئے اسکی موت کی گواہی دینا جائز ہے اگر چہ اس کا مشاہدہ نہ کیا ہو۔ نکاح کی صورت یہ ہے کہ گواہ نے لوگوں سے کہتے ہوئے سُنا کہ فلاں مرد نے فلاں عورت سے نکاح کیا ہے۔ تو گواہ نے اگر چہ نکاح کا مشاہدہ نہیں کیا ہے مگر اس کو نکاح کی گواہی دینا جائز ہے اور دخول کی صورت یہ ہے کہ گواہ نے لوگوں سے سنا کہ فلاں عورت فلاں مرد کی بیوی ہے۔ اور اس نے اس کے ساتھ دخول کیا ہے اگر چہ اس نے عقد نکاح اور دخول کا مشاہدہ نہ کیا ہو ۔ اور ولایت قاضی کی صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے لوگوں سے سنا کہ فلاں اس شہر کا قاضی ہے اور اس کو دیکھا کہ لوگوں میں فیصلے جاری کرتا ہے تو اس آدمی کو یہ گواہی دینا جائز ہے کہ فلاں شخص فلاب شہر کا قاضی ہے۔ اگر چہ امام مسلمین کی طرف سے اس کو قاضی بنانے کا مشاہدہ نہ کیا ہو ۔ بہر حال ان پانچ چیزوں کے بارے میں ثقہ لوگوں سے سنکر گواہی دینا جائز ہے اگر چہ انکا مشاہدہ نہ کیا ہو۔ لیکن یہ حکم استحسانی ہے ورنہ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ محض سنگر گواہی دینا جائز نہ ہو کیونکہ شہادت ، مشاہدہ سے مشتق ہے اور مشاہدہ دیکھ کر ہوتا ہے نہ کہ سُن کر۔ حالانکہ مذکورہ پانچوں چیزوں میں معاینہ اور دیکھنا نہیں پایا گیا تو یہ چیزیں بیچ کے مانند ہوگئیں یعنی جس طرح محض سنکر بغیر دیکھے بیع کی شہادت دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح بمقتضائے قیاس محض سن کر ان چیزوں کی گواہی دینا بھی نا جائز ہے۔ و ذالک بالعلم

سے مراد معاینہ اور دیکھنا ہے۔ یعنی مشاہدہ علم (معاینہ ) سے ہوتا ہے۔ استحسان کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ پانچوں چیز میں ایسی ہیں جن کے اسباب کا معائنہ خاص خاص لوگ کرتے ہیں۔ ان پر عام لوگ مطلع نہیں ہو پاتے ۔ حالانکہ ان چیزوں کے ساتھ ایسے احکام متعلق ہوتے ہیں جو مدتیں گذرنے کے باوجود بھی باقی رہتے ہیں۔ مثلاً نسب موت اور نکاح کے ساتھ میراث متعلق ہے اور دخول کے ساتھ کمال مہر عدت ، ثبوت احصان اور نسب متعلق ہیں۔ یعنی اگر مرد کا عورت کے ساتھ دخول متحقق ہو جائے تو مرد پر پورا مہر واجب ہوگا۔ طلاق کی صورت میں عورت پر عدت واجب ہو گی ۔ عورت و مرد دونوں محصن شمار ہوں گے، بچہ پیدا ہو گیا تو اس کا نسب ثابت ہوگا۔ پس اگر ان چیزوں میں محض سنے پر گواہی قبول نہ ہو تو حرج لاحق ہو گا ۔ اور بہت سے احکام معطل ہو جائیں گے ۔ مثلاً پچاس سال کے بعد ایک شخص نے دعوی کیا کہ یہ چیز میرے والد کی میراث ہے یا عورت نے میت پر اپنے مہر کا دعوی کیا حالانکہ نہ اس شخص کی ولادت کے مشاہدہ کے گواہ موجود اور نہ اس عورت کے اس میت کے ساتھ نکاح کے مشاہدہ کے گواہ موجود ہیں۔ اب اگر ان دونوں صورتوں میں اُن حضرات کی گواہی قبول نہ ہو جنھوں نے نہ مدعی کی ولادت کو دیکھا ہے اور نہ اس عورت کے نکاح کا مشاہدہ کیا ہے بلکہ محض لوگوں سے سنا ہے۔ تو پہلی صورت میں میراث اور دوسری صورت میں مہر کا حکم بے کار ہو جائے گا۔ میراث اور مہر کے مدعی حرج میں مبتلا ہو جائیں گے۔ اور سب سے بڑی دلیل تو یہ ہے کہ ہم اس بات کی شہادت دیتے ہیں کہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ، ابو طالب کے بیٹے ہیں۔ اگر چہ ہم نے ان کی ولادت کا مشاہدہ نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور ہم اس بات کے شاہد ہیں کہ تمام صحابہ وفات پاگئے ہیں اگر چہ ہم نے ان میں سے کسی کی موت کا مشاہدہ نہیں کیا اور ہم شہادت دیتے ہیں کہ حضرت عائشہ رسول پاک صلى الله عليه وسلم کی بیوی ہیں ۔ اگر چہ ہم نے انکے نکاح کا مشاہدہ نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور ہم شہادت دیتے ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے عائشہ کے ساتھ دخول کیا ہے اگر چہ ہم نے دخول کا مشاہدہ نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور ہم گواہی دیتے ہیں کہ شریح بن حارث قاضی تھے اگر چہ ہم نے ان کو قاضی بنانے کا مشاہدہ نہیں کیا ہے۔ ان نظائر سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مذکورہ پانچ چیزوں میں محض سُن کر گواہی دینا جائز ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف بیچ کے ایجاب و قبول کا ہر شخص معائنہ کرتا ہے۔ یعنی ہر شخص دیکھتا ہے کہ فلاں نے فلاں کے ہاتھ بیچ کی ہے کسی خاص آدمی کے دیکھنے کی کوئی خصوصیت نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے بغیر، شاہدہ کے محض سنگر بیع کی گواہی دیتا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور نسب وغیرہ مذکورہ پانچوں چیزوں کا معائنہ اور مشاہدہ چونکہ خاص خاص لوگوں کے ساتھ مختص ہوتا ہے اسلئے ان میں سننے پر اکتفاء کیا جائیگا تا کہ حرج لاحق نہ ہو۔

وانما يجوز للشاهد ان يشهد..... الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے،
سوال یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ پانچ چیزوں میں محض سن کر گواہی دینے کا جائز ہونا کتاب اللہ کے مخالف ہے اسلئے کہ کتاب اللہ یعنی الامن شهد بالحق و هم يعلمون میں شہادت کیلئے علم یعنی مشہور بہ کے جاننے کو شرط قرار دیا گیا ہے حالانکہ بغیر معائنہ اور مشاہدہ کے علم حاصل نہیں ہوتا ۔ لہذا مذکورہ چیزوں میں محض سنگر بغیر معائنہ کے استحسانا گواہی کو جائز قرار دینا کتاب اللہ کے خلاف ہے۔ جو سراسر غلط ہے ۔

جواب ... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ علم ، جس طرح مشاہدہ سے حاصل ہوتا ہے اسی طرح کسی بات کے مشتہر ہونے سے بھی ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی اگر کسی نے کوئی بات ایسی سنی جو عام لوگوں میں مشتہر ہو تو اس اشتہار سے بھی سننے والے کو علم حاصل ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور یہ اشتہار یا تو تواتر سے ہوگا یعنی خبر دینے والی اتنی بڑی جماعت ہو جس کا جھوٹ پر اتفاق بعید از عقل ہو۔ یا یہ اشتہار ثقہ آدمی کے خبر دینے سے
The Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume ten: that it is not permissible because testimony is derived from observation, and observation occurs by seeing, and this is not obtained, so it becomes like a sale. And the reason for istihsān is that these matters are such that only specific people are privy to observing their causes, and rulings are attached to these matters that remain in effect for periods of time. So if testimony by hearing is not accepted in these matters, hardship would occur and rulings would be suspended. Unlike sale, because every person hears it, and testifying by hearing is permissible along with notoriety, and this notoriety is obtained through tawātur or through the report of a reliable person. As stated in al-Quduri, and the condition is that two just men inform the witness, or one man and two just women, so that some knowledge is obtained for him. And it has been said that in testimony of death, one man or one woman's report suffices because few people observe the condition of the deceased besides one person, since a person finds death daunting and repugnant, so imposing a condition of number would cause hardship. But lineage and marriage are not like this. And it is appropriate that the giving of testimony be left absolute, and he should not interpret it, but if he interprets before the judge that he is testifying by hearing, the judge will not accept his testimony, just as in properties, observation of possession permits testimony, then if the witness interprets, it is not accepted; similarly here. Explanation: It is not permissible for a witness to testify about matters he has not observed, except five matters regarding which it is permissible to testify merely by hearing from reliable people without observation: lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and appointment of a judge. Lineage: for example, Hamid heard from people that Shahid is so-and-so's son; according to Abu Hanifa, the informing group must be such that their agreement on falsehood is inconceivable, while according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), two just men are sufficient. So if Zaid heard lineage in this way, it is lawful for him to testify that Shahid is so-and-so's son. Death: for example, the witness, e.g., Hamid, heard from people that so-and-so died, or saw people treating him with shrouding and burial as with the dead, then it is permissible for the witness to testify to his death even if he did not observe it. Marriage: the witness heard people saying that a certain man married a certain woman; even if he did not observe the marriage, it is permissible for him to testify to the marriage. Consummation: the witness heard from people that a certain woman is the wife of a certain man and he has consummated with her, even if he did not observe the marriage contract and consummation. Appointment of a judge: a man heard from people that so-and-so is the judge of this city and saw him issuing judgments among people; then it is permissible for him to testify that so-and-so is the judge of that city, even if he did not observe his appointment as judge by the Imam of the Muslims. In any case, regarding these five matters, it is permissible to testify by hearing from reliable people even if they were not observed. But this ruling is by istihsān, otherwise qiyās requires that testifying merely by hearing is not permissible because testimony is derived from observation, and observation occurs by seeing, not by hearing. Since the five mentioned matters do not involve seeing and observation, they become like sale, i.e., just as it is not permissible to testify to a sale merely by hearing without seeing, similarly, by qiyās, testifying to these matters merely by hearing is also impermissible. And that is by knowledge. 'By knowledge' means seeing and observation, i.e., observation occurs by knowledge (seeing). The reason for istihsān is that the five mentioned matters are such that only specific people observe their causes; the general public cannot access them, yet rulings are attached to these matters that remain even after periods of time. For example, inheritance is attached to lineage, death, and marriage; with consummation, the full dower, waiting period, proof of ihsān, and paternity are attached. That is, if consummation occurs, the full dower becomes obligatory, in case of divorce the wife must observe the waiting period, both husband and wife are considered muhsan, and if a child is born, paternity is established. So if testimony by mere hearing were not accepted in these matters, hardship would occur and many rulings would be suspended. For example, after fifty years, a person claims that this property is the inheritance of his father, or a woman claims her dower from the deceased, while there are no witnesses who observed the birth of that person or the marriage contract of that woman with the deceased. If the testimony of those who neither saw the birth nor observed the marriage, but merely heard from people, is not accepted, then in the first case the ruling of inheritance and in the second case the ruling of dower would be futile, and the claimants would fall into hardship. And the greatest proof is that we testify that Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) is the son of Abu Talib, even though we did not observe his birth. And we testify that all the Companions have died, even though we did not observe any of their deaths. And we testify that Aisha is the wife of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), even though we did not observe her marriage. And we testify that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) consummated with Aisha, even though we did not observe the consummation. And we testify that Shurayh ibn al-Harith was a judge, even though we did not observe his appointment. These analogies show that in the five mentioned matters, testifying merely by hearing is permissible. In contrast, every person observes the offer and acceptance of sale; there is no particularity of a specific person seeing it. Therefore, without observation, testifying by mere hearing for sale is not permissible. And since the observation of lineage and the other five matters is restricted to specific people, we suffice with hearing in them to avoid hardship. The phrase 'And it is only permissible for a witness to testify...' is the answer to a question. The question is that the permissibility of testifying merely by hearing in these five matters contradicts the Book of Allah, because the Book of Allah, i.e., 'except those who bear witness to the truth and they know' (Quran 43:86) makes knowledge a condition for testimony, and knowledge is not obtained without seeing and observation. Therefore, declaring testimony permissible by istihsān in these matters merely by hearing without observation is against the Book of Allah, which is completely wrong. The answer: Knowledge is obtained not only through observation but also through a matter being well-known. That is, if a person hears something that is well-known among the common people, the hearer obtains knowledge from that notoriety. And this notoriety either occurs through tawātur, i.e., such a large group of reporters whose agreement on falsehood is inconceivable, or through the report of a reliable person.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the Hanafi ruling on hearsay testimony (al-shahādah bi al-samā'). The general principle is that testimony requires direct observation (mushāhadah). However, by istihsān (juristic preference), five exceptions are allowed: lineage (nasab), death (mawt), marriage (nikāh), consummation (dukhūl), and appointment of a judge (wilāyat al-qāḍī). The text first presents the qiyās (analogy) argument that hearsay testimony is impermissible because shahādah is derived from mushāhadah (seeing). Then it explains the istihsān reasoning: these matters are not easily observed by the public, yet they entail lasting legal consequences (inheritance, dower, waiting period, etc.). Accepting only direct observation would cause hardship (ḥaraj), so the law facilitates by accepting reliable hearsay. The text also discusses conditions: the witness must have some degree of knowledge, achieved through mutawātir reports or reports from reliable individuals. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa requires a group whose agreement on falsehood is inconceivable (tawātur), while the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) suffice with two just men (or one man and two women). For death, a single reliable report may suffice due to the repugnance of death. The text also addresses a potential objection from the Quranic verse 'إِلَّا مَنْ شَهِدَ بِالْحَقِّ وَهُمْ يَعْلَمُونَ' (except those who bear witness to the truth and they know), arguing that knowledge can be obtained through notoriety (ishtihār) without direct observation. Examples from the Companions (e.g., testifying that Ali is the son of Abu Talib without seeing his birth) are cited as practical precedents. The commentary emphasizes that this ruling is specific to Hanafi fiqh and is based on istihsān overriding qiyās.

Key Terms
شہادت (shahādah): Testimony given in court; in this context, it is defined as derived from mushāhadah (direct observation).
مشاہدہ (mushāhadah): Direct observation or seeing with one's own eyes.
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyās due to necessity, custom, or public interest.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; here it is the default rule that testimony requires direct observation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Death

D) Marriage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits hearsay testimony in five specific matters (lineage, death, marriage, consummation, judge appointment) by istihsān to prevent hardship.

Shahadat — Testimony

6 min
The Permissibility of Hearsay Testimony in Five Matters
States the ruling and istihsan justification for hearsay testimony in five matters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five matters in which hearsay testimony is permissible and explain the Hanafi istihsan rationale.

Core Idea
Hearsay testimony is valid in five matters to prevent hardship, even though it deviates from the general rule requiring direct observation.

In this passage from the Hidayah, al-Marghinani establishes an important exception in the law of testimony. While the general rule requires witnesses to have directly observed the event, hearsay (samā'/'istifāḍa) is accepted in five specific matters. This ruling is based on istihsan to avoid hardship (ḥaraj). Let's explore the reasoning and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five exceptional matters
The passage lists lineage (nasab), death (mawt), marriage (nikāḥ), intercourse (dukhūl), and appointment of a judge (taqlīd al-qāḍī). These are the five matters where hearsay testimony is permitted.
2
Understand the rationale of hardship
These events are observed only by a few people; if direct witnesses were required, many legal rights (inheritance, dower, ʿidda, etc.) would be lost over time. This would create intolerable hardship (ḥaraj).
3
Examine the evidence from Islamic consensus
The author cites examples: we testify that ʿAlī is the son of Abū Ṭālib, that the Companions have died, and that ʿĀʾisha is the Prophet's wife, all without direct observation. This shows that the Sharia accepts hearsay in well-known matters.
4
Contrast with public transactions
Sales are public and observed by many, so their occurrence can be directly witnessed. Hence, hearsay is not accepted for sales—this highlights the scope of the exception.
5
State the ruling
The ruling is that hearsay testimony in these five matters is permissible (jāʾiz) and valid. It is an exception justified by istihsan to remove hardship.

مہر کا دعوی کیا حالانکہ نہ اس شخص کی ولادت کے مشاہدہ کے گواہ موجود اور نہ اس عورت کے اس میت کے ساتھ نکاح کے مشاہدہ کے گواہ موجود ہیں۔ اب اگر ان دونوں صورتوں میں اُن حضرات کی گواہی قبول نہ ہو جنھوں نے نہ مدعی کی ولادت کو دیکھا ہے اور نہ اس عورت کے نکاح کا مشاہدہ کیا ہے بلکہ محض لوگوں سے سنا ہے۔ تو پہلی صورت میں میراث اور دوسری صورت میں مہر کا حکم بے کار ہو جائے گا۔ میراث اور مہر کے مدعی حرج میں مبتلا ہو جائیں گے۔ اور سب سے بڑی دلیل تو یہ ہے کہ ہم اس بات کی شہادت دیتے ہیں کہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ، ابو طالب کے بیٹے ہیں۔ اگر چہ ہم نے ان کی ولادت کا مشاہدہ نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور ہم اس بات کے شاہد ہیں قاضی بنانے کا مشاہدہ نہیں کیا ہے۔ ان نظائر سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مذکورہ پانچ چیزوں میں محض سن کر گواہی دینا جائز ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف بیچ کے ایجاب و قبول کا ہر شخص معائنہ کرتا ہے۔ یعنی ہر شخص دیکھتا ہے کہ فلاں نے فلاں کے ہاتھ بیچ کی ہے کسی خاص آدمی کے دیکھنے کی کوئی خصوصیت نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے بغیر مشاہدہ کے محض سن کر بیع کی گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور نسب وغیرہ مذکورہ پانچوں چیزوں کا معائنہ اور مشاہدہ چونکہ خاص خاص لوگوں کے ساتھ مختص ہوتا ہے اسلئے ان میں سننے پر اکتفاء کیا جائیگا تا کہ حرج لاحق نہ ہو۔
The Book of Testimony. By 'مشاہدہ' (eyewitnessing) is meant seeing and observing, so knowledge comes from eyewitnessing. The reason for istihsan (juristic preference) is that the five mentioned matters are such that their causes are observed only by specific people; common people are not aware of them. Yet these matters are connected to rulings that remain even after long periods. For example, inheritance is connected to lineage, death, and marriage; and the completion of dower, waiting period, establishing ihsan (status of being married), and lineage are connected to intercourse. So if a man has intercourse with a woman, the full dower becomes obligatory; in case of divorce, the woman must observe the waiting period; both become muhsan (protected from hadd punishment for adultery); and if a child is born, its lineage is established. Therefore, if testimony based merely on hearing were not accepted in these matters, hardship would occur and many rulings would be suspended. For example, after fifty years a person claims that a certain property is his father's inheritance, or a woman claims her dower from a deceased man, while there are no witnesses to the birth of that person or to the marriage of that woman. If testimony from those who have merely heard from people is not accepted, then the rulings of inheritance and dower would become invalid. The strongest proof is that we testify that Ali ibn Abi Talib is the son of Abu Talib, even though we did not witness his birth; we testify that all the Companions have died, even though we did not witness any of their deaths; we testify that Aisha is the wife of the Prophet (peace be upon him), even though we did not witness her marriage; we testify that the Prophet entered upon Aisha, even though we did not witness it; and we testify that Shurayh ibn al-Harith was a judge, even though we did not witness his appointment. From these examples it is clear that it is permissible to testify based on hearing in the five matters. In contrast, the offer and acceptance in a sale are observed by everyone, so testifying without direct observation is not permissible. Since witnessing the five matters is restricted to specific individuals, hearing suffices to avoid hardship.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling from the chapter on testimony, providing the principle that hearsay testimony is permissible in five specific matters to avoid hardship. The author begins by defining 'مشاہدہ' (eyewitnessing) as direct observation that produces knowledge. Then he explains the istihsan (juristic preference) for allowing testimony based on hearsay in these matters: lineage, death, marriage, intercourse (dukhul), and appointment of a judge. The reason is that these events are not ordinarily witnessed by the public; only a few people observe them. Yet crucial legal rulings, such as inheritance, dower, 'idda, and legitimacy, depend on establishing these facts. If testimony required direct observation, many rights would be lost due to the passage of time. To prevent hardship (haraj), the law permits testimony based on widespread reputation (ishtihar) or reliable hearsay. The author strengthens this with examples from Islamic history: Muslims testify about the lineage of Ali ibn Abi Talib, the deaths of the Companions, the marriage of Aisha, and the judgeship of Shurayh, all without having directly observed these events. This establishes the precedent. He contrasts these with sales, which are public transactions observed by many, thus requiring direct testimony. In summary, the ruling is that hearsay testimony is valid for these five matters, and the underlying rationale is istihsan to remove hardship.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsān): A method of juristic preference where a ruling is adopted based on equity and hardship avoidance, even if it contradicts a general analogy (qiyas).
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony given before a qadi to establish a right; it requires specific conditions including knowledge, justice, and number of witnesses.
حرج (ḥaraj): Hardship or difficulty that the Shari'ah seeks to alleviate; it is a key rationale for istihsan in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Quran explicitly commands it
D) Because the two disciples (Sahibayn) prefer it

Key Takeaway
Hearsay testimony is permissible in five matters (lineage, death, marriage, intercourse, judge appointment) to avoid hardship, justified by istihsan.

Shahadat — Testimony

Conditions for Hearsay Testimony and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Resolves Quranic objection and details conditions for hearsay testimony with Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for hearsay testimony in the five matters, distinguish the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Hearsay testimony is valid if based on widespread reputation, but the number of informants is disputed within the Hanafi school.

This passage addresses a powerful objection: the Quran requires knowledge for testimony, and knowledge is normally gained by direct observation. Yet the Hanafi school permits hearsay in certain matters. How? The answer lies in the concept of ishtihar (widespread reputation), which can produce knowledge just as observation does. Once this is established, the text then explores the conditions for such hearsay, revealing a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection and its Hanafi response
First, recognize the Quranic objection: testimony requires 'ilm, and 'ilm is only through observation. Then see how the Hanafi response refutes this by introducing ishtihar as a source of knowledge.
The key term is ishtihar, which can be actual (tawatur) or constructive (report of trustworthy persons).
2
Distinguish the two types of ishtihar
Note that ishtihar haqiqi comes from tawatur (mass transmission), while ishtihar hukmi comes from the report of a trustworthy person. Both produce sufficient knowledge for hearsay testimony.
3
Trace the positions of al-Quduri, al-Hidayah, and the Sahibayn
Al-Quduri only requires a trustworthy source. Al-Hidayah adds a number: two just men or one man and two women. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) specify this number. Imam Abu Hanifa insists on actual widespread reputation only.
The Sahibayn's view is often considered the mufta bihi.
4
Analyze the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Compare scenarios: if two just men report a marriage, the Sahibayn would permit hearsay testimony, but Abu Hanifa would not unless the witness heard it from the general public.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position
In fatwa today, the position of the Sahibayn (two men or one man and two women) is preferred for its practicality and certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وانما يجوز للشاهد ان يشهد..... الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے، سوال یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ پانچ چیزوں میں محض سن کر گواہی دینے کا جائز ہونا کتاب اللہ کے مخالف ہے اسلئے کہ کتاب اللہ یعنی الامن شهد بالحق و هم يعلمون میں شہادت کیلئے علم یعنی مشہور بہ کے جاننے کو شرط قرار دیا گیا ہے حالانکہ بغیر معائنہ اور مشاہدہ کے علم حاصل نہیں ہوتا ۔ لہذا مذکورہ چیزوں میں محض سنگر بغیر معائنہ کے استحسانا گواہی کو جائز قرار دینا کتاب اللہ کے خلاف ہے۔ جو سراسر غلط ہے ۔ جواب ... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ علم ، جس طرح مشاہدہ سے حاصل ہوتا ہے اسی طرح کسی بات کے مشتہر ہونے سے بھی ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی اگر کسی نے کوئی بات ایسی سنی جو عام لوگوں میں مشتہر ہو تو اس اشتہار سے بھی سننے والے کو علم حاصل ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور یہ اشتہار یا تو تواتر سے ہوگا یعنی خبر دینے والی اتنی بڑی جماعت ہو جس کا جھوٹ پر اتفاق بعید از عقل ہو۔ یا یہ اشتہار ثقہ آدمی کے خبر دینے سے ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ قدوری میں مذکور ہے البتہ تو اتر کی صورت میں اشتہار حقیقی ہوگا۔ اور ثقہ آدمی کے خبر دینے بھی صورت میں اشتہار حکمی ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ ہوا کہ سننے پر گواہ کو گواہی دینا اس وقت جائز ہے جب یہ سنا اشتہار کے ساتھ ہو یعنی وہ بات مشتہر ہوگئی ہو یا اشتہار خواہ حقیقی ہو خواہ حکمی ہو ۔ صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ ثقہ آدمی سے سن کر مذکورہ پانچ چیزوں میں گواہی دینا جائز ہے مگر خبر دینے والے ثقہ لوگوں کے سلسلہ میں کوئی عدد ذکر نہیں کیا۔ البتہ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ عدد شرط ہے ۔ چنانچہ صاحبین کے نزدیک دو عادل مرد خبر دیں یا ایک عادل مرد اور دو عادل عورتیں خبر دیں، تو اُن سے سُن کر گواہی دینا جائز ہے، اور یہ شرط اس لئے ہے تا کہ گواہ کو مشہور بہ کے بارے میں ایک گونہ علم حاصل ہو سکے۔ اور حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک فقط اشتہار حقیقی معتبر ہے یعنی گواہ کے لئے سن کر گواہی دینا اسی وقت جائز ہے جبکہ اس نے عام طور پر لوگوں سے سنا ہو، ان کے نزدیک دو عادل مردوں سے سننا گواہی دینے کے لئے کافی نہ ہوگا۔
The text from 'وانما يجوز للشاهد' onwards is an answer to a question: The question is that permitting testimony based on mere hearing in the five matters contradicts the Book of Allah, because in the verse 'except those who testify to the truth while they know' (Quran 43:86) knowledge is a condition, and knowledge is not acquired without direct observation. So to allow it by istihsan is against the Quran. This is false. The answer: Knowledge can be acquired through widespread reputation (ishtihar) just as through observation. If a person hears something that is widespread among people, that reputation produces knowledge. This reputation can be actual (haqiqi) through tawatur (mutually corroborated reports) or constructive (hukmi) through the report of a trustworthy person. So hearsay testimony is valid when accompanied by reputation, whether actual or constructive. Al-Quduri said it is permissible to hear from a trustworthy person without specifying a number, but al-Hidayah states that a number is required: according to the Sahibayn, if two just men or one just man and two just women report, then hearing from them is valid. Imam Abu Hanifa says only actual reputation is valid, i.e., the witness must have heard generally from people; hearing from two just men is not sufficient.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its refutation, followed by the conditions for hearsay testimony and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The objector argues that the Quran requires 'ilm (knowledge) for testimony, which is only obtained through direct observation, so allowing hearsay by istihsan contradicts revelation. The Hanafi response clarifies that knowledge is also produced by widespread reputation (ishtihar), which can be either actual (tawatur) or constructive (report of a trustworthy person). Therefore, hearsay testimony is valid if based on such reputation. Then the author discusses the conditions: al-Quduri simply requires a trustworthy source, while the Hidayah adds a number requirement. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require two just men or one man and two women to report, so that the witness gains a measure of certainty. Imam Abu Hanifa insists on actual widespread reputation, meaning the witness must hear it from the general public, not just two individuals. This gives four positions: (1) any trustworthy person (Quduri), (2) two men or one man and two women (Sahibayn), (3) only general reputation (Abu Hanifa). The text also notes that the Hidayah's condition of number is for the witness to acquire certainty.

Key Terms
اشتہار (ishtihār): Widespread reputation of a matter among the public, which produces knowledge in the listener.
توتر (tawātur): A report transmitted by so many narrators that collusion on falsehood is inconceivable; it yields certain knowledge.
صاحبین (al-Ṣāḥibayn): The two disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Hearing from two just men or one just man and two just women
C) Hearing from any three people
D) Hearing from any one person

Key Takeaway
Hearsay testimony is valid in Hanafi fiqh only if based on widespread reputation (actual or constructive), with the Sahibayn's number condition (two men or one man and two women) being the relied-upon position.

Special Exception for Death Testimony and the Rule of Absolute Testimony
Special exception and testimony rule for hearsay

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for death testimony (one reliable witness suffices) and explain why testimony based on hearsay must be stated absolutely to be accepted.

Core Idea
Death's hardship justifies a single witness; hearsay testimony must be absolute to reflect certainty.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses two exceptional rules within Hanafi testimony law. First, due to the natural aversion to witnessing death, the requirement of two witnesses is relaxed to one reliable person. Second, when a witness testifies based on hearsay (e.g., lineage), they must state the fact absolutely, without revealing its hearsay basis, to maintain the appearance of certainty and ensure acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two special rulings
The passage gives two rules: (1) for death testimony, one just man or woman suffices; (2) for hearsay matters, the witness must testify absolutely without explaining the basis.
2
Analyze the death exception
Understand the proof: people avoid the dead, so requiring multiple witnesses would cause hardship, which Shari'ah removes. Contrast with lineage, marriage, and judgeship, which naturally involve crowds.
The exception is limited to death.
3
Understand the absolute testimony rule
When testifying to hearsay (e.g., lineage, possession-based ownership), the witness must state the fact as if directly known. Saying 'I heard' reveals hearsay and casts doubt, leading to rejection.
The rationale is that absolute statement reflects inner certainty, treated as knowledge.
4
Apply the examples
The text gives examples: for lineage, say 'Zayd is the son of Amr', not 'I heard Zayd is...'. For possession-based ownership, say 'This house belongs to Amr', not 'I saw Amr in possession and heard he owns it'.
Qualification invalidates the testimony.
