كتاب الشهادة
اشرف الہدایہ جلد- و ہم و غیر سامان کسی کے قبضہ میں دیکھ کر چونکہ قابض کے مالک ہونے کی گواہی دینا جائز ہے اس لئے مذکورہ صورت میں بھی گواہی و بینا جائز ہے کہ قابض اس غلام اور باندی کا مالک ہے اور اگر وہ سمجھدار ہوں خواہ بالغ ہوں یا غیر بالغ ہوں تو یہی صورت استثناء (سوی العبد و الامة ) کا محل ہے یعنی اس صورت میں محض کسی کا قبضہ دیکھ کر یہ گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے کہ قابض اس غلام یا با ندی کا مالک ہے ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں غلام اور باندی کو اپنی ذات پر قابو حاصل ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر وہ اپنے پیدائشی آزاد ہونے کا دعوی کر دے تو اسی کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور اس پر کسی کا قبضہ ثابت نہ ہوگا پس جب ان کو اپنی ذات پر قابو حاصل ہے تو یہ ان دونوں سے دوسرے کا قبضہ دور کر دیگا اور جب ان سے دوسرے کا قبضہ دور ہو گیا تو ملکیت کی دلیل (یعنی قبضہ ) معدوم ہوگئی اور جب ملکیت کی دلیل معدوم ہو گئی تو دیکھنے والے کے لئے قابض کے مالک ہونے کی گواہی دینا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ اگر وہ غلام اور باندی کبیر یعنی سمجھدار ہوں تو بھی دیکھنے والے کو قابض کے مالک ہونے کی گواہی دینا حلال اور جائز ہے اس روایت کی دلیل کپڑوں اور دیگر سامانوں پر قیاس ہے یعنی جس طرح کسی کے قبضہ میں کپڑے دیکھ کر قابض کے مالک ہونے کی گواہی دینا جائز ہے اگر چہ غلام اور باندی کبیر ہوں یعنی سمجھ دار ہوں جو اپنے مافی الضمیر کو اداء کر سکتے ہوں یہی صاحبین سے مروی ہے گویا تینوں حضرات نے مذکورہ تمام صورتوں میں قبضہ کو ملکیت کی دلیل قرار دیا ہے چنانچہ اگر کسی نے یہ دعوی کیا کہ حامد کے قبضہ میں جو غلام یا باندی ہے میں اس کا مالک ہوں اور قابض اپنے مالک ہونے کا دعویٰ کرتا ہے تو قابض کا ہی قول قبول ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ قبضہ کی وجہ سے ظاہر حال اسی کے موافق ہے لیکن فرق وہ ہے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں یعنی کپڑوں کا اپنے اور ذاتی اختیار نہیں ہوتا ہے لہذا ان پر قابض کا قبضہ معتبر ہو گا اور سمجھ دار غلام اور باندی کا چونکہ اپنے اوپر ذاتی اختیار ہوتا ہے اس لئے ان پر کسی کا قبضہ معتبر نہ ہوگا۔ پس جب کپڑوں میں قابض کا قبضہ معتبر ہے تو اس کا قبضہ دلیل ملک ہو گا اور سمجھ دار غلام اور باندی میں چونکہ کسی کا قبضہ معتبر نہیں ہے اس لئے قابض کا ظاہری قبضہ اس کے مالک ہونے کی دلیل نہ ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب ! جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume -: Seeing cloth and other goods in someone's possession, since it is permissible to testify that the possessor is the owner, therefore in the mentioned case also testimony and proof are permissible that the possessor is the owner of this male slave and female slave. But if they are discerning, whether adult or non-adult, then this is the place of the exception (except the male slave and female slave), meaning in this case merely seeing someone's possession, it is not permissible to testify that the possessor is the owner of this male slave or female slave. Because in this case the male slave and female slave have control over themselves. So if they claim to be free-born, their statement is credible, and someone's possession over them is not established. Since they have control over themselves, they will remove another's possession from themselves. And when another's possession is removed from them, the evidence of ownership (i.e., possession) becomes extinct. And when the evidence of ownership becomes extinct, then for the observer it is also not permissible to testify that the possessor is the owner. It is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that if the male slave and female slave are adult, i.e., discerning, still it is permissible and lawful for the observer to testify that the possessor is the owner. The proof of this narration is analogy (qiyas) on cloth and other goods, i.e., just as seeing cloth in someone's possession, it is permissible to testify that the possessor is the owner, even if the male slave and female slave are adult, i.e., discerning, who can express their inner thoughts. This is also narrated from the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). It is as if all three imams have deemed possession as evidence of ownership in all mentioned cases. So if someone claims that the male slave or female slave in Hamid's possession is mine, and the possessor claims to be the owner, then the statement of the possessor will be accepted, because due to possession, the apparent state is in his favor. But there is a difference we have explained: cloth has no choice of its own, so the possessor's possession over them is valid; but discerning slaves have personal choice over themselves, so no one's possession over them is valid. Thus, when the possessor's possession over cloth is valid, his possession is evidence of ownership; and in discerning slaves, since no one's possession is valid, the possessor's apparent possession is not evidence of his ownership. And Allah knows best the correct! Jamil Ahmad, may he be forgiven.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Book of Testimony (Kitab al-Shahada) discussing the evidentiary value of possession (qabd) in establishing ownership, specifically comparing inanimate goods (clothing) with slaves. The author first states the general rule: seeing an item in someone's possession allows one to testify that the possessor is the owner, because possession is a common indicator of ownership. This applies to clothing and other goods. However, an exception is made for slaves: if the slave is discerning (kabir, meaning capable of independent speech and action), merely seeing someone in possession is not sufficient to testify that the possessor owns the slave. The reason is that a discerning slave has self-control and can claim to be free; such a claim would be credited, removing the possessor's apparent ownership. The author then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. A narration from Imam Abu Hanifa states that even for discerning slaves, possession can still be the basis for testifying to ownership. This view is supported by analogy (qiyas) with clothing, where possession is accepted regardless of any independent will of the object. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) are also reported to hold this view. Thus, all three imams effectively consider possession as evidence of ownership in all cases, but the author notes a distinction: clothing has no independent choice, so possession is a reliable indicator; discerning slaves have their own volition, so their mere presence undermines the evidentiary force of another's possession. The practical outcome: if a dispute arises between a claimant and the possessor of a slave, the possessor's statement is accepted due to apparent ownership through possession, but unlike with inanimate goods, the slave's own statement could override. The author concludes with a prayer for divine guidance.

Key Terms
قبضہ (qabd): Physical possession or control over an item, which serves as evidence of ownership in testimony.
قابض (qabid): The person who has physical possession of the item, presumed to be the owner in testimony.
ملکیت (malkiyyah): Ownership or right of property over the slave or item.
سوی العبد و الامة (sawi al-'abd wa al-amah): Exception: except the male slave and female slave, referring to the rule that possession of a discerning slave does not prove ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason given in the passage for the exception that possession of a discerning slave does not allow testimony to ownership?
A) Slaves cannot be owned according to Islamic law.
B) The discerning slave has self-control and can claim to be free, which undermines the possessor's apparent ownership.
C) Possession is not recognized as evidence in Hanafi law.
D) The Hanafi school does not allow testimony based on indirect evidence.

Key Takeaway
For testimony purposes, possession is strong evidence of ownership for inanimate goods, but when the object has independent will, the presumption weakens – though the majority Hanafi view still accepts it.

The Principle of Accusation (Tuhmah) in Witness Testimony
Introduction to chapter on witness qualifications with principle of tuhmah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why tuhmah is the basis for rejecting testimony and identify the four categories of tuhmah from the text.

Core Idea
Testimony is rejected when accusation tilts the balance against truthfulness.

This passage introduces the core principle governing witness disqualification in Hanafi law: the presence of accusation (tuhmah). It explains how accusation undermines the probative value of testimony and categorizes the sources of tuhmah. Understanding these categories is essential for determining who may testify.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis for rejection
The text states that the origin and basis for rejection of testimony is accusation (tuhmah), citing the hadith 'la shahada li-mutaham'. Recognize that tuhmah is the root cause.
The hadith is a primary textual evidence.
2
Understand the epistemological reasoning
Testimony is a report (khabar) that can be true or false. For it to be accepted as legal proof, the probability of truth must outweigh falsehood. Accusation disturbs this balance, making the testimony unreliable.
This is based on the principle that testimony is a hujjah only when truth predominates.
3
Classify the sources of tuhmah
The text lists four sources: (1) fisq (sinfulness) in the witness himself; (2) kinship relation between witness and beneficiary; (3) physical defect like blindness causing confusion; (4) legal punishment for false accusation (hadd al-qadhf). Classify each as inherent, relational, incapacity, or legal history.
Each source independently triggers rejection.

Source Text

باب من يقبل شهادته ومن لا يقبل
ترجمہ یہ باب ان لوگوں کے بیان میں ہے جنکی گواہی قبول کی جاتی ہے اور ان لوگوں کے بیان میں ہے جنکی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جاتی ہے۔ تشریح گزشتہ فصل میں ان چیزوں کا بیان تھا جس میں شہادت سنی جاتی ہے اور ان چیزوں کا بیان تھا جس میں شہادت نہیں سنی جاتی ۔ اس سے فراغت کے بعد اس باب میں ان لوگوں کا بیان کیا جائیگا جن کی شہادت قبول کی جاتی ہے اور جن کی شہادت قبول نہیں کی جاتی مگر چونکہ وہ چیزیں جن میں شہادت قبول کی جاتی ہے یا قبول نہیں کی جاتی شہادت کا محل ہیں اور محل شرط ہوتے ہیں۔ اور شرط ، مشروط پر مقدم ہوتی ہیں اس لئے ان چیزوں کا بیان جن کی شہادت قبول کی جاتی ہیں یا نہیں قبول کی جاتی، پہلے کہا گیا اور ان لوگوں کا بیان جن کی شہادت قبول کی جاتی ہے یا قبول نہیں کی جاتی بعد میں کیا گیا۔ صاحب عنایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ شہادت کے رد ہونے کی اصل اور بنیاد تہمت ہے چنانچه صاحب شریعت کا ارشاد لا شهادة متهم متہم آدمی کی شہادت معتبر نہیں ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ شہادت ایک خبر ہے جو صدق اور کذب کا احتمال رکھتی ہے مگر حجت شرعی اسکا اسوقت ثابت ہوگا۔ جب اس میں صدق کی جانب راج ہو اور تہمت کے ساتھ جانب صدق راج نہیں ہوتی پس جب تہمت کے ساتھ جانب صدق راج نہیں ہوتی تو تہمت کی صورت میں اس کا حجت شرعی ہونا بھی ثابت نہ ہوگا اور جب تہمت کیوجہ سے اسکا حجت شرعی ہونا ثابت نہ ہوا تو اس کو رد کر دیا جائیگا تہ پس معلوم ہوا کہ تہمت کی وجہ سے شہادت کو رد کر دیا جاتا ہے اور تہمت کبھی تو ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے جو خود گواہ میں موجود ہوتے ہیں جیسے فسق کیونکہ جو شخص کذب کے علاوہ دوسرے ممنوعات دین سے باز نہ رہتا ہو وہ کذب اور جھوٹ بولنے سے بھی باز نہ رہیگا۔ اور جب جھوٹ بولنے سے باز نہ رہا تو وہ یقینا متہم بالکذب ہوگا اور کبھی تہمت ایسے معنی کیوجہ سے ہوتی ہے جو معنی مشہود لہ میں ہوتے ہیں۔ مثلاً ولادت کا رشتہ یعنی اگر شاہد اور مشہودلہ کے درمیان ولادت کی قرابت ہو تو شاہد اس بات کے ساتھ متہم ہوگا کہ وہ قرابت کی وجہ سے مشہولہ کو مشہود علیہ پر ناجائز ترجیح دیتا ہے۔ اور کبھی تہمت ایسے خلل کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے جو مشہودلہ اور مشہود علیہ کے درمیان امتیاز کی قدرت نہ ہونے کے وجہ سے ہو۔ جیسے گواہ کا نا بینا ہونا۔ اور تہمت بھی اس چیز سے عاجز ہونے کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے جس کو شریعت نے صدق کی دلیل بنایا ہے جیسے محدود فی القذف
Chapter on whose testimony is accepted and whose is not accepted. Translation: This chapter is about the statement of those people whose testimony is accepted and the statement of those people whose testimony is not accepted. Explanation: In the previous section, there was a statement about those things in which testimony is heard and a statement about those things in which testimony is not heard. After finishing that, in this chapter a statement will be made about those people whose testimony is accepted and those whose testimony is not accepted. But since those things in which testimony is accepted or not accepted are the locus (mahall) of testimony, and the locus is a condition, and the condition precedes the conditioned, therefore the statement about those things whose testimony is accepted or not was made first, and the statement about those people whose testimony is accepted or not was made later. The author of al-'Inayah said: The origin and basis for rejection of testimony is accusation (tuhmah). Just as the author of the Shari'ah said: There is no testimony for an accused person (la shahada li-mutaham). A second evidence is that testimony is a report (khabar) which contains the possibility of truth and falsehood, but it becomes a legal proof (hujjah shar'iyyah) only when the side of truth is predominant. And with accusation, the side of truth does not predominate. So when with accusation the side of truth does not predominate, then in the case of accusation its being a legal proof will not be established. And when due to accusation its being a legal proof is not established, then it will be rejected. Thus it is known that testimony is rejected due to accusation. And accusation is sometimes due to a meaning that exists in the witness himself, like fisq (sinfulness), because a person who does not refrain from other prohibited things besides falsehood will also not refrain from lying. And when he does not refrain from lying, then he is certainly accused of falsehood. And sometimes accusation is due to a meaning that exists in the one for whom testimony is given (mashhud lahu). For example, the relationship of birth (wiladat): if there is a kinship of birth between the witness and the one for whom testimony is given, then the witness will be accused that due to kinship he gives an improper preference to the one for whom testimony is given over the one against whom testimony is given. And sometimes accusation is due to a defect (khalal) that arises from the inability to distinguish between the one for whom testimony is given and the one against whom testimony is given, like the witness being blind. And accusation is also due to inability regarding that which the Shari'ah has made a proof of truth, like the one who has been punished for slander (mahdud fi al-qadhf).
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a new chapter in the Book of Testimony, focusing on the qualifications of witnesses. The author first justifies the order of presentation: the previous section discussed the subject matter (mahall) of testimony—what types of claims testimony is acceptable for. Since the subject matter is a condition for testimony, it was discussed first. Now the chapter turns to the witnesses themselves: whose testimony is accepted and whose is rejected. The key principle, derived from the author of al-'Inayah, is that the rejection of testimony is based on accusation (tuhmah). A hadith is cited: 'There is no testimony for an accused person' (la shahada li-mutaham). The reasoning is that testimony is a form of news (khabar) which can be true or false. For it to be accepted as legal proof, the probability of truth must outweigh falsehood. Accusation upsets this balance, making the testimony unreliable. The text then categorizes the sources of accusation: (1) Inherent in the witness: fisq (sinfulness) implies that if a person is not careful about religious prohibitions, he may also not hesitate to lie; (2) In the relationship with the beneficiary: e.g., a blood relative such as a father or son may be biased in favor of the person for whom he testifies; (3) A defect in the witness's ability: blindness prevents proper identification, leading to potential confusion; (4) Legal punishment: a person punished for false accusation of adultery (hadd al-qadhf) is considered unreliable because his credibility in truthful reporting has been compromised. The passage sets the stage for detailed rulings on specific categories of witnesses.

Key Terms
تہمت (tuhmah): Accusation, suspicion, or a situation that undermines the reliability of a witness, making his testimony subject to rejection.
محل (mahall): The subject matter or the thing about which testimony is given; the context in which testimony is heard.
لا شهادة متهم (la shahada li-mutaham): The hadith declaring that an accused person (one under suspicion) cannot be a valid witness.
فسق (fisq): Sinfulness or open violation of Islamic law, which renders a witness unreliable due to likely falsehood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the fundamental reason for rejecting a witness's testimony?
A) Lack of intelligence.
B) The presence of accusation (tuhmah).
C) The witness being a minor.
D) The witness being a female.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school identifies accusation (tuhmah) as the root cause for rejecting testimony, categorizing its sources into inherent flaws, relational bias, physical incapacity, and legal punishment.

Testimony of a Blind Person: Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute on blind testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the testimony of a blind person and explain the reasoning behind the disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
A blind person's testimony is rejected because they cannot point to distinguish parties, though exceptions exist for hearsay.

This passage presents a detailed inter-madhhab dispute over the admissibility of a blind person's testimony. The Hanafi school generally rejects it, while Imam Zufar and a narration from Abu Hanifa accept it for hearsay matters. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i accept it if the witness was sighted at the time of witnessing. The passage also discusses the intra-Hanafi scenario of a witness who becomes blind after testifying.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Hanafi Ruling
Start with the matn's statement: 'The testimony of a blind person is not accepted.' This is the default position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
Note that the word 'tashahhud' (testimony) refers to giving evidence in court.
2
Trace the Intra-Hanafi Exceptions
Look at Zufar's view and the narration from Abu Hanifa: they accept blind testimony in 'tasamu'' matters (common hearsay) because only hearing is needed.
Tasamu' covers widely known facts where visual identification isn't crucial.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i/Abu Yusuf Position
Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i argue that if the witness was sighted at the time of bearing witness (tahammul), the knowledge is already acquired, and performance only requires speech.
They compare it to identifying a deceased person by lineage (nisbah).
4
Examine the Hanafi Response
The text gives the Hanafi rebuttal: performance requires pointing to distinguish between the claimant and defendant. A blind person can only rely on voice, which is uncertain. Lineage is only for absent persons, not present ones. Therefore, the testimony is like hudud and qisas cases.
This highlights the principle that eligibility must be present at the time of performance (ada').
5
Apply the Rule to the Post-Testimony Blindness Scenario
If a witness becomes blind after testifying but before judgment, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say judgment cannot be based on it because eligibility is required at the time of judgment. This contrasts with death or absence, where eligibility is either finalized or not voided.
This shows the Hanafi condition that the witness must retain the capacity for pointing at the time of judgment.

Source Text

قال ولا تقبل شهادة الاعمى وقال زفر وهو رواية عن ابي حنيفة تقبل فيما يجرى فيه التسامع لان الحاجة فيه الى السماع ولا خلل فيه وقال ابو يوسف والشافعى يجوز اذا كان بصيرا وقت التحمل لحصول العلم بالمعاينة والاداء يختص بالقول ولسانه غير مؤف والتعريف يحصل بالنسبة كما في الشهادة على الميت ولنا ان الاداء يفتقر الى التمييز بالاشارة بين المشهود له والمشهود عليه ولا يميز الاعمى الا بالنغمة وفيه شبهة يمكن التحرز عنها بجنس الشهود والنسبة لتعريف الغائب دون الحاضر فصار كالحدود والقصاص ولو عمى بعد الاداء يمتنع القضاء عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد فان قيام الاهلية للشهادة شرط وقت القضاء لصيرورتها حجة عندة وقد بطلت وصار كما اذا خرس او جنّ او فسق بخلاف ما اذا ماتوا أو غابوا لان الاهلية بالموت قد انتهت وبالغيبة ما بطلت
ترجمہ اور نابینا آدمی کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جاتی ہے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا اور یہی روایت ابوحنیفہ سے ہے کہ نابینا کی گواہی ان چیزوں میں قبول کی جائے گی جن چیزوں میں تسامع جاری ہوتا ہے کیونکہ ایسی گواہی میں صرف سنے کی ضرورت ہے اور نابینا کی سماعت میں کوئی خلل نہیں ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ نابینا کی گواہی جائز ہے بشرطیکہ وہ حمل شہادت کے وقت بینا ہو کیوں کہ اُس کو معائنہ سے علم حاصل ہو چکا ہے اور اداء کرنا قول کے ساتھ مختص ہے اور اس کی زبان عیب دار نہیں ہے اور شناخت کرانا نسب بیان کرنے سے حاصل ہو جاتا ہے جیسے میت پر گواہی میں ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ادا مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے درمیان اشارہ کے ساتھ امتیاز کرنے کی طرف محتاج ہے اور نا بینا بغیر آواز کے امتیاز نہیں کر سکتا ہے اور آواز میں ایک اشتباہ ہے جس سے جنس گواہوں کے ذریعہ احتراز ممکن ہے اور نسب بیان کرنا غائب کی شناخت کے لئے ہے نہ کہ حاضر کی پس حدود و قصاص کے مانند ہو گیا ہے اور اگر ادائے شہادت کے بعد نا بینا ہوا تو طرفین کے نزدیک قاضی کا فیصلہ دینا منع ہو گا۔ کیونکہ قضائے قاضی کے وقت شہادت کیلئے اہلیت کا موجود ہونا شرط ہے اس لئے کہ شہادت قضائے قاضی کیوقت ہی حجت ہوئی ہے حالانکہ حجت باطل ہو گئی اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا ہے جیسے جب گواہ گونگایا مجنون یا فاسق ہو گیا۔ برخلاف اس کے جب گواہ مر گئے ہوں یا غائب ہو گئے ہوں اس لئے کہ شہادت کی اہلیت موت کی وجہ سے پوری ہوگئی اور غائب ہونے کی
He said: The testimony of a blind person is not accepted. And Zufar said, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa, that his testimony is accepted in matters where tasamu' (common hearsay) occurs, because the need there is for hearing, and there is no defect in that. And Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible if he was sighted at the time of bearing witness (tahammul), because he acquired knowledge by direct observation, and performance (ada') is specific to speech, and his tongue is not defective, and identification is achieved by lineage (nisbah) as in testimony over a deceased. Our evidence is that performance requires distinction by pointing between the one for whom testimony is given and the one against whom it is given, and a blind person can only distinguish by voice, and in voice there is uncertainty which can be avoided by the type of witnesses. And lineage is for identifying an absent person, not a present one, so it becomes like hudud and qisas. And if he becomes blind after performance, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the judge is prevented from passing judgment, because the existence of eligibility for testimony is a condition at the time of judgment, since it becomes a proof at that time, and it has become void. So it becomes like when a witness becomes dumb, insane, or sinful. Contrary to when they die or are absent, because eligibility has ended by death, and by absence it has not become void.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the testimony of a blind person (al-a'ma) and the disagreements among scholars. The base matn states that a blind person's testimony is not accepted. Imam Zufar, and in one narration from Abu Hanifa, accepts it in matters where tasamu' (common knowledge or hearsay) is involved, because only hearing is needed. Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i accept it if the witness was sighted at the time of bearing witness (tahammul), so he observed the event directly, and performance merely requires speech. They also argue that identification can be done by lineage (nisbah) as in testimony over a deceased person. The Hanafi position (Imam Muhammad and the dominant view of Abu Hanifa) is that testimony is not accepted, because the witness must be able to distinguish between the claimant and defendant by pointing, which a blind person cannot do reliably; he can only distinguish by voice, which is uncertain. Identifying by lineage is only for an absent person, not a present one. Therefore, a blind person's testimony is analogous to hudud and qisas cases where strict conditions apply. Then the text discusses a scenario where a witness becomes blind after giving testimony. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if a witness loses his sight after testifying but before the judge's judgment, the judge cannot rule based on that testimony because the eligibility condition (being sighted) must exist at the time of judgment. This is similar to a witness becoming dumb, insane, or sinful. However, if the witness dies or goes absent after testifying, the testimony remains valid because eligibility is complete at the time of performance. The passage cuts off but the incomplete thought likely contrasts death/absence with loss of sight. The Urdu commentary repeats these rulings.

Key Terms
تسامع (tasamu'): Common hearsay or widely known matters; public knowledge that does not require visual identification.
حمل شہادت (tahammul al-shahadah): The bearing or receiving of testimony, i.e., the time when the witness observes the event.
اداء (ada'): The performance or delivery of testimony in court.
حدود و قصاص (hudud wa qisas): Fixed criminal penalties and retaliation; cases where the strictest evidentiary requirements apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the dominant Hanafi view, if a blind person testifies about a matter that is not common hearsay (tasamu'), what is the ruling?
A) The testimony is accepted because hearing is sufficient.
B) The testimony is not accepted because the blind person cannot point to distinguish the parties.
C) The testimony is accepted only if the witness was sighted at the time of witnessing.
D) The testimony is accepted only if the matter involves hudud.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school generally rejects blind testimony due to the inability to point, but allows it in hearsay matters where only hearing is needed.

Shahadat — Testimony
advanced
12 min
Testimony of a Blind Person: Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Analysis of rulings on blind testimony with inter-madhhab differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on the testimony of a blind person and compare them with the views of the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools.

Core Idea
A blind person's testimony is rejected in hudud/qisas by consensus, but its acceptance in other matters varies by madhhab and condition.

This lesson examines the intricate rulings on the testimony of a blind person (شهادة الأعمى), a subject of significant disagreement across and within madhhabs. The Hanafi school alone contains multiple positions, from absolute rejection to conditional acceptance. Understanding these positions requires distinguishing between hudud/qisas and other cases, between hearsay and observational testimony, and between the stages of bearing (tahammul) and performance (ada'). We will navigate these distinctions as presented in the commentary Ashraf al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish hudud/qisas from other matters
Understand that in hudud and qisas cases, all schools agree that a blind person's testimony is rejected because these penalties are averted by doubts. For other matters, disagreement exists.
This is the starting point of the taxonomy.
2
Identify the Hanafi sub-positions
List the three main Hanafi positions: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: absolute rejection in non-hudud. Abu Yusuf: acceptance with conditions (sighted at tahammul and immovable object). Zufar: acceptance in hearsay matters.
Also note the narration from Abu Hanifa via Ibn Shuja' similar to Zufar.
3
Analyze the proofs for each position
For each position, extract the dalil: for hudud rejection, the 'substitute involves doubt' argument; for absolute rejection, the necessity of pointing; for conditional acceptance, the validity of tahammul when sighted; for hearsay acceptance, the sufficiency of hearing.
Focus on the wajh al-dalalah – how the proof yields the ruling.
4
Compare with other madhhabs
State the positions of Malik, Ahmad (absolute acceptance) and Shafi'i (similar to Abu Yusuf). Understand their proof: 'adala and wilaya are sufficient; analogy to narration.
This step highlights the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and its justification
Determine that the relied-upon Hanafi position is the strict view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and understand why it is preferred: caution and avoidance of doubt.
This is the operative ruling for Hanafi fatwa.

تشریح اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے کہ نابینا آدمی کی شہادت قبول کی جائے گی یا نہیں ۔ سو اس میں قدرے تفصیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ نابینا حدود و قصاص میں شاہد ہو گا یا حدود و قصاص کے علاوہ میں۔ اگر اس نے حدود و قصاص میں شہادت دی ہے تو یہ بالاتفاق غیر مقبول ہے۔ اور اگر حدود و قصاص کے علاوہ میں شاہد ہے تو اس کی بھی دو صورتیں ہیں یا تو ان چیزوں میں شاہد ہوگا جن میں عام لوگوں سے سنکر گواہی دینا جائز ہے جیسے نسب ، موت اور یا ان چیزوں میں شاہد ہو گا جن میں لوگوں سے سنکر گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے بلکہ ان میں مشاہدہ اور معائنہ شرط ہے جیسے بیع ، شراء ، پس اگر اول ہے یعنی نابینا ان چیزوں میں گواہ ہے جن میں لوگوں سے سن کر گواہی دینا جائز ہے تو امام زفر کے نزدیک نابینا کی گواہی قبول کر لی جائے گی یہی امام ابوحنیفہ سے ابن شجاع کی روایت ہے اور اگر نانی ہے یعنی نا بینا ان چیزوں میں گواہ ہے جن میں لوگوں سے سنکر گواہی دینا جائز نہیں پس نابینا اگر تحمل شہاد کے وقت بینا اور مشہود به غیر منقول ہو تو امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس صورت میں اس کی گواہی قبول کیجائے گی اور اگر ان دونوں باتوں میں سے کوئی ایک بات منفی ہو جائے یعنی نابینا تحمل شہاد کے وقت دینا نہ ہو یا مشہود به غیر منقول نہ ہو بلکہ شی منقول ہو تو ائمہ ثلثہ ( ابوحنیفہ صحابہ ) کا اس پر اتفاق ہے کہ اس صورت میں نابینا کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ بہر حال ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تحمل شہادت کے وقت گواہ کا بینا ہونا شرط ہے اور طرفین کے نزدیک متحمل شہادت کے وقت سے لیکر قضائے قاضی تک گواہ کا بینا ہونا شرط ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر گواہ ادائے شہادت کے بعد قضائے قاضی سے پہلے نابینا ہو گیا تو قاضی اس شہادت پر فیصلہ دینے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا۔ مذکورہ مذاہب کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ حدود وقصاص میں نابینا کی گواہی مقبول نہ ہوگی البتہ حدود و قصاص کے علاوہ میں طرفین کے نزدیک نابینا کی گواہی مطلقا قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ مشہود بہ خواہ ان چیزوں میں سے ہو جن میں لوگوں سے سنکر گواہی دینا جائز ہے خواہ ان چیزوں میں سے ہو جن میں لوگوں سے سنکر گواہی دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام مالک اور امام احمد کے نزدیک نابینا کی گواہی مطلقاً جائز ہے۔ حضرت امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ جن چیزوں میں لوگوں سے سنکر گواہی دینا جائز . ہے ان چیزوں میں نابینا کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔ یہی امام صاحب سے ابن شجاع کی روایت ہے اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی
نے فرمایا کہ نابینا کی شہادت دو شرطوں کے ساتھ جائز ہے ایک تو یہ کہ نابینا آدمی مکمل شہادت کے وقت بینا ہو۔ دوم یہ کہ مشہور یہ کہ جسکے بارے میں گواہی دیجائیگی ) شی سغیر منقول ہو حدود و قصاص میں نابینا آدمی کی گواہی مقبول نہ ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ حدودو قصاص شبہات کی وجہ سے دور کر دئیے جاتے ہیں اور نابینا کے حق میں آواز چونکہ مشاہدہ کے قائم مقام ہوتی ہے یعنی بینا آدمی کو جن چیزوں کا علم مشاہدہ سے حاصل ہوتا ہے نابینا آدمی کو ان کا علم سننے سے حاصل ہوتا ہے پس نابینا آدمی کے حق میں سننا اور آواز مشاہدہ اور دیکھنے کے قائم مقام ہوئے اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ اصل کی بہ نسبت قائم مقام میں ایک گونہ شبہ ہوتا ہے اور یہ بھی مسلم ہے کہ شبہات کی وجہ سے حدود و قصاص ثابت نہیں ہوتے بلکہ ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں لہذا نا بینا آدمی کی گواہی سے حدود و قصاص ثابت نہ ہوں گے اور قاضی حدود و قصاص میں نابینا کی گواہی قبول نہیں کرے گا۔
حضرت امام مالک اور امام احمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو از شہادت کیلئے شاہد کا صاحب ولایت اور صاحب عدالت ہونا ضروری ہے اور نا بینا آدمی کی ولایت اور عدالت میں کوئی نقص نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ نابینا کی روایت احادیث قبول کیجاتی ہے پس جب شاہد کا صاحب ولایت اور صاحب عدالت ہونا ضروری ہے اور نابینا کی ولایت اور عدالت میں کوئی نقص نہیں ہے نا بینا کی گواہی قبول کرنے میں

كتاب الشهادة
۶۲
اشرف الہدایہ جلد وہم
کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے حضرت امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جن چیزوں میں لوگوں سے منکر گواہی دینا جائز ہے ان چیزوں میں صرف سننے کی ضرورت ہے اور نا بینا کی سماعت میں کوئی خلل نہیں ہے بلکہ نا بینا سماعت میں بینا آدمی کی مانند ہے پس جب ان چیزوں میں صرف سننے کی رت ہے اور نابینا آدمی کی سماعت میں کوئی خلل نہیں ہے تو ان چیزوں میں نابینا کی گواہی قبول کر لی جائیگی ۔ ہاں نابینا آدمی اگر بہرہ بھی ہو تو اس کی گواہی بالا تفاق قبول نہ ہوگی۔
حضرت امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نابینا جب تحمل شہادت کے وقت ( گواہی اٹھانے کیوقت ) بینا اور آنکھوں والا تھا۔ تو اس کو مشہور بہ کا علم حاصل ہو چکا ہے۔ اور جس شخص کو عمل شہادت کیوقت مشاہدہ سے مشہور بہ کا علم حاصل ہو جاتا ہے اس کا مقتل ( گواہی اٹھانا ) درست ہوتا ہے۔ بہر حال جو شخص فی الحال نابینا ہے مر تحمل شہادت کے وقت آنکھوں والا تھا اس کا قتل شہادت درست ہو گیا۔ اب رہا شہادت کا ادا کرنا تو وہ صرف کلام سے ہوتا ہے اور نابینا کی زبان میں چونکہ کوئی عیب نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کے کلام میں کوئی خلل بھی نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب نابینا کی زبان میں عیب نہ ہونے کیوجہ سے اس کے کلام میں کوئی خلل نہیں ہے تو اس کا شہادت ادا کرنا بھی درست ہو گا۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ مذکورہ نابینا کا تحمل شہادت بھی درست ہے اور ادائے شہادت بھی درست ہے اور مانع شہادت یعنی مشہور عالیہ ( مدعی علیہ ) کا نہ پہچانا منتفی ہے۔ کیونکہ نابیٹا کو مشہود علیہ کا نسب بیان کرنے سے مشہود علیہ کی . شناخت ہو جائے گی۔ مثلاً نا بینا سے کہا گیا کہ فلاں بن فلاں کے واسطے ، مدعی علیہ فلاں بن فلاں پر گواہی دے تو اس نسب بیان کرنے سے نا بینا مدعی علیہ کو پہچان جائے گا۔ جیسے میت پر گواہی دینے میں ہوتا ہے مثلاً میت کے قرض خواہوں نے دعوی کیا اور گواہ پیش کئے تو گواہ کے لئے میت کی طرف اشارہ کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے۔ پس وہ اس طرح گواہی دے سکتے ہیں کہ مدعی کا فلاں بن فلاں میت پر اس قدر قرضہ ہے۔ بہر حال جب مذکورہ بینا کا عمل شہادت اور ادائے شہادت دونوں درست ہیں اور مانع شہادت منتفی ہے تو مذکورہ نا بینا کی گواہی قبول کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ادائے شہادت کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ گواہ مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے درمیان اشارہ کے ساتھ امتیاز کرے اور نابینا آدمی صرف ان کی آواز سے ان کے درمیان فرق کر سکتا ہے۔ اشارہ کے ساتھ فرق نہیں کر سکتا۔ اور چونکہ ایک کی آواز دوسرے کی : آواز کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے اس لئے آواز میں ایک گونہ اشتباہ ہوگا۔ اور جنس گواہوں کے ذریعہ اس اشتباہ سے بچنا بھی ممکن ہے اسطور پر کہ آنکھوں والے بہت سے گواہ موجود ہیں جو مدعی اور مدعلی علیہ کے درمیان اشارہ کے ساتھ فرق کر سکتے ہیں۔ پس جب آنکھوں والے گواہ موجود ہیں تو نا بینا جو مدگی اور بدگی عالیہ کے درمیان اشارہ کے ساتھ فرق نہیں کر سکتا اس کو گواہ بنا نا کس طرح درست ہو گا۔ والنسبة تعريف للغائب دون الحاضر سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ نابینا آدمی کا مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے درمیان فرق کرنا مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے نسب بیان کرنے سے ممکن ہے یعنی صرف ان کے آواز پر اکتفاء نہ کیا جائے بلکہ ان کا نسب بھی دریافت کر لیا جائے اس نسب دریافت کرنے سے نابینا گواہ مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے درمیان بآسانی فرق کر سکتا ہے۔ اور جب نا بینا گواہ
مدگی اور مدعی علیہ کے درمیان نسب کے ذریعہ فرق کر سکتا ہے تو نابینا کی گواہی قبول کر لینی چاہئے ۔
جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ نسب بیان کرنا غائب (غیر موجود ) کی شناخت کے واسطے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ حاضر کی شناخت کے واسطے اور زیر بحث مسئلہ میں مدعی اور مدعی علیہ دونوں حاضر ہیں تو بیان نسب انکی شناخت کے واسطے کیسے ہوگا ۔ اور جب بیان نسب ان کی
Ashraf al-Hidayah, Volume Ten, Explanation: There is disagreement about whether the testimony of a blind person is accepted or not. There is some detail, the gist of which is: the blind person either testifies in hudud and qisas or in other matters. If he testifies in hudud and qisas, it is unanimously unacceptable. If he testifies in other than hudud and qisas, there are two cases: either he testifies in matters where it is permissible to give testimony based on hearing from people, such as lineage and death, or he testifies in matters where it is not permissible to give testimony based on hearing from people, but rather observation and inspection are required, such as sale and purchase. If the first (i.e., the blind person testifies in matters where testimony based on hearing is allowed), then according to Imam Zufar, the blind person's testimony will be accepted; this is also a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa through Ibn Shuja'. If the second (i.e., the blind person testifies in matters where testimony based on hearing is not allowed), then if the blind person was sighted at the time of bearing testimony and the testified matter is immovable, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i, his testimony will be accepted. If either of these two conditions is absent—i.e., the blind person was not sighted at the time of bearing testimony or the testified matter is movable—then the three Imams (Abu Hanifa and his companions) agree that in this case the blind person's testimony will not be accepted. In any case, according to Abu Yusuf, it is a condition that the witness be sighted at the time of bearing testimony. According to the two sides (the Hanafi side and the Shafi'i side?), it is a condition that the witness be sighted from the time of bearing testimony until the judge's verdict. Thus, if the witness becomes blind after giving testimony but before the judge's verdict, the judge is not authorized to decide based on that testimony. The summary of these madhhabs is: In hudud and qisas, the testimony of a blind person is not accepted. However, in other than hudud and qisas, according to the two sides, the testimony of a blind person is absolutely not accepted, whether the testified matter is from those things in which testimony based on hearing is allowed or from those things in which it is not allowed. According to Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad, the testimony of a blind person is absolutely valid. Imam Zufar said: In matters where testimony based on hearing from people is allowed, the blind person's testimony will be accepted. This is also the narration from Imam Abu Hanifa through Ibn Shuja'. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i said: The testimony of a blind person is valid with two conditions: first, that the blind person was sighted at the time of bearing testimony; second, that the testified matter is immovable. The reason why a blind person's testimony is not accepted in hudud and qisas is that hudud and qisas are averted by doubts, and for a blind person, sound stands in place of sight—that is, what a sighted person knows through observation, a blind person knows through hearing—so for a blind person, hearing and sound are substitutes for observation and sight. It is established that a substitute has some doubt compared to the original, and it is also established that hudud and qisas are not proven due to doubts but are rather dropped; therefore, hudud and qisas will not be proven by the testimony of a blind person, and the judge will not accept the blind person's testimony in hudud and qisas. The proof of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad is that for testimony, it is necessary that the witness be competent (sahib wilaya) and just (sahib 'adala), and there is no defect in the competence and justice of a blind person. For this reason, the narration of hadith from a blind person is accepted. So when it is necessary for a witness to be competent and just, and there is no defect in the competence and justice of a blind person, there is no harm in accepting the blind person's testimony. The proof of Imam Zufar is that in matters where testimony based on hearing from people is allowed, only hearing is needed, and there is no impairment in the hearing of a blind person; rather, a blind person is like a sighted person in hearing. So when only hearing is needed in those matters and there is no impairment in the hearing of a blind person, then in those matters the blind person's testimony will be accepted. However, if the blind person is also deaf, then his testimony is unanimously not accepted. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i is that when the blind person, at the time of bearing testimony, was sighted and had eyes, he had acquired knowledge of the testified matter. A person who acquires knowledge of the testified matter through observation at the time of bearing testimony has valid bearing (tahammul). In any case, a person who is currently blind but was sighted at the time of bearing testimony, his bearing of testimony is valid. As for the performance (ada') of testimony, it is only through speech, and since there is no defect in the tongue of a blind person, his speech will have no impairment. And if there is no impairment in his speech, then his performance of testimony will also be valid. The conclusion is that the said blind person's bearing of testimony is valid and his performance of testimony is also valid, and the impediment to testimony (i.e., not recognizing the defendant) is negated, because the blind person will recognize the defendant by mentioning his lineage. For example, the blind person is told: 'For so-and-so son of so-and-so, give testimony against the defendant so-and-so son of so-and-so,' then by mentioning this lineage, the blind person will recognize the defendant. This is like what happens in testimony concerning a deceased person. For example, the creditors of the deceased file a claim and produce witnesses; it is not possible for the witnesses to point to the deceased. So they can testify by saying: 'The claimant so-and-so son of so-and-so has such-and-such debt upon the deceased so-and-so son of so-and-so.' In any case, when the said blind person's bearing and performance of testimony are both valid and the impediment is negated, there is no harm in accepting the said blind person's testimony. The proof of the two sides is that for the performance of testimony, it is necessary for the witness to distinguish between the plaintiff and defendant by pointing, and a blind person can only distinguish between them by their voices, not by pointing. And because one person's voice may resemble another's, there will be some confusion in voice. It is also possible to avoid this confusion through other witnesses, insofar as there are many sighted witnesses who can distinguish between the plaintiff and defendant by pointing. So when sighted witnesses are available, how can it be valid to appoint a blind person who cannot distinguish between the plaintiff and defendant by pointing? The phrase 'al-nasbu ta'rifun lil-gha'ibi duna al-hadiri' is an answer to a question. The question is: A blind person can distinguish between the plaintiff and defendant by mentioning their lineage—i.e., not relying only on their voices but also inquiring about their lineage—by this inquiry into lineage the blind witness can easily distinguish between plaintiff and defendant. And when the blind witness can distinguish between plaintiff and defendant through lineage, then the blind person's testimony should be accepted. The answer: The mention of lineage is for identifying the absent (non-present), not for identifying the present. In the case under discussion, both the plaintiff and defendant are present, so how can mentioning lineage be for their identification? And when mentioning lineage is

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah, addresses the complex issue of the testimony of a blind person (شهادة الأعمى). It is an inter-madhhab dispute, presenting and comparing various positions within and outside the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating the general disagreement and then provides a detailed taxonomy of cases. The central distinction is between hudud and qisas (where testimony is unanimously rejected due to the principle that these penalties are averted by doubts—shubuhat) and other matters. For non-hudud matters, the passage further distinguishes between matters where hearsay testimony is permitted (like lineage and death) and those where direct observation is required (like sale and purchase). This distinction is pivotal: Imam Zufar accepts the blind person's testimony in the first category, and this is also reported from Imam Abu Hanifa via Ibn Shuja'. For the second category, Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i accept it if the blind person was sighted at the time of bearing the testimony (tahammul) and the object of testimony is immovable. The 'two sides' (طرفین)—likely referring to the majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) along with al-Shafi'i?—hold a stricter view: for non-hudud cases, the blind person's testimony is absolutely rejected, regardless of the type of matter. Their reasoning is that a blind person cannot point to the parties, relying solely on voice which is prone to confusion, and sighted witnesses are preferable. The passage then refutes an objection that lineage could identify the parties, using the principle that lineage identification is for absent persons, not present ones. The proofs from various imams are presented: Malik and Ahmad argue that the witness's 'adala (justice) and wilaya (competence) are sufficient; Zufar emphasizes the sufficiency of hearing in hearsay cases; Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i focus on the validity of tahammul when the witness was sighted at that time; and the 'two sides' stress the necessity of pointing for ada' (performance). The Hanafi mufta bihi position derived from this passage is that the testimony of a blind person is not accepted in hudud and qisas by consensus, and in other than hudud and qisas, the relied-upon view is that of the majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) that it is absolutely rejected, though there is a weak narration from Abu Hanifa accepting it in hearsay matters. The authority weight is from the commentary tradition, drawing on the Hidayah and its sources, thus representing the later Hanafi authoritative position.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court to establish a right or obligation.
تحمل الشهادة (tahammul al-shahada): The act of bearing or witnessing the event that forms the basis of testimony.
اداء الشهادة (ada' al-shahada): The act of giving testimony in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, under what condition is the testimony of a blind person accepted in non-hudud cases?
A) In all non-hudud matters without restriction.
B) Only if the blind person was sighted at the time of bearing testimony and the object is immovable.
C) It is absolutely rejected in all non-hudud matters.
D) Only in matters where hearsay testimony is allowed, such as lineage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the testimony of a blind person is generally rejected because the requirement to point to parties cannot be fulfilled, introducing unacceptable doubt, unlike in narrating hadith.

Shahadat — Testimony
advanced
8 min
Testimony of a Blind Person: Disputes and Hanafi Position
Intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute on blind testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on the testimony of a blind person, identify the key arguments of the opposing views (Imam Zufar, Imam Abu Yusuf/Shafi'i), and explain why the majority holds that pointing (isharah) is essential.

Core Idea
A blind witness cannot point – this procedural need invalidates testimony, even if lineage identifies.

The testimony of a blind person raises a fundamental question: what exactly is required for valid testimony? The Hanafi school produced multiple opinions on whether hearing alone suffices, or whether sight at the time of bearing testimony is necessary, or whether the inability to point at performance invalidates. This lesson unpacks the competing proofs from Imam Zufar, Imam Abu Yusuf/Imam al-Shafi'i, and the majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad), culminating in the relied-upon position that blindness at the time of performance renders testimony invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Positions
List the three distinct views: Imam Zufar (accepts if based on hearing), Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i (accept if sighted at bearing), and the majority (tarfayn: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad – reject absolutely).
The 'tarfayn' in this passage refer to the two companions Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but the majority position includes Abu Hanifa.
2
Examine Imam Zufar's Proof
Imam Zufar argues that for matters of property and contracts, testimony relies on hearing alone; a blind person's hearing is perfect, so testimony is valid.
His reasoning is qiyas: analogy to sighted witnesses who only hear the transaction.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf/Shafi'i Proof
They argue that if the witness was sighted at the time of bearing (tahammul), the later blindness does not affect validity; the performance (ada') is merely oral, and identification can be achieved through lineage (nisba), as with a deceased person.
This position uses a combination of istihsan and analogy to testimony about the dead.
4
Analyze the Majority (Tarfayn) Response
The majority respond that performance requires physical pointing (isharah) to distinguish plaintiff and defendant. A blind person cannot point reliably, and lineage is only for identifying absent persons, not present ones. Moreover, sighted witnesses are available, so there is no necessity.
This argument prioritizes the procedural integrity of the court over alternative methods of identification.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi and Thamarah
The majority view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is relied upon. The practical consequence: a blind person's testimony is not accepted in any case, even if he was sighted at bearing or can identify by lineage.
Imam Zufar's view is a minority opinion and not acted upon in fatwa.

گواہی دے سکتے ہیں کہ مدعی کا فلاں بن فلاں میت پر اس قدر قرضہ ہے۔ بہر حال جب مذکورہ بینا کا عمل شہادت اور ادائے شہادت دونوں درست ہیں اور مانع شہادت منتفی ہے تو مذکورہ نا بینا کی گواہی قبول کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ادائے شہادت کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ گواہ مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے درمیان اشارہ کے ساتھ امتیاز کرے اور نابینا آدمی صرف ان کی آواز سے ان کے درمیان فرق کر سکتا ہے۔ اشارہ کے ساتھ فرق نہیں کر سکتا۔ اور چونکہ ایک کی آواز دوسرے کی : آواز کے مشابہ ہوتی ہے اس لئے آواز میں ایک گونہ اشتباہ ہوگا۔ اور جنس گواہوں کے ذریعہ اس اشتباہ سے بچنا بھی ممکن ہے اسطور پر کہ آنکھوں والے بہت سے گواہ موجود ہیں جو مدعی اور مدعلی علیہ کے درمیان اشارہ کے ساتھ فرق کر سکتے ہیں۔ پس جب آنکھوں والے گواہ موجود ہیں تو نا بینا جو مدگی اور بدگی عالیہ کے درمیان اشارہ کے ساتھ فرق نہیں کر سکتا اس کو گواہ بنا نا کس طرح درست ہو گا۔ والنسبة تعريف للغائب دون الحاضر سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ نابینا آدمی کا مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے درمیان فرق کرنا مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے نسب بیان کرنے سے ممکن ہے یعنی صرف ان کے آواز پر اکتفاء نہ کیا جائے بلکہ ان کا نسب بھی دریافت کر لیا جائے اس نسب دریافت کرنے سے نابینا گواہ مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے درمیان بآسانی فرق کر سکتا ہے۔ اور جب نا بینا گواہ مدگی اور مدعی علیہ کے درمیان نسب کے ذریعہ فرق کر سکتا ہے تو نابینا کی گواہی قبول کر لینی چاہئے ۔ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ نسب بیان کرنا غائب (غیر موجود ) کی شناخت کے واسطے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ حاضر کی شناخت کے واسطے اور زیر بحث مسئلہ میں مدعی اور مدعی علیہ دونوں حاضر ہیں تو بیان نسب انکی شناخت کے واسطے کیسے ہوگا ۔ اور جب بیان نسب ان کی شناخت کے واسطے نہیں ہوا تو نا بینا گواہ ان دونوں کے درمیان فرق کرنے پر بھی قادر نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب نا بینا گواہ مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کے درمیان فرق کرنے پر قادر نہیں ہے تو نا بینا کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ادائے شہادت کے لئے مدعی اور مدعلی علیہ کے درمیان فرق اور امتیاز کرنا ضروری ہے۔ بہر حال مذکورہ چیزیں حدود و قصاص کے مانند ہو گئیں۔ پس جس طرح نابینا کی گواہی بالا جماع حدود و قصاص میں جائز نہیں اسی طرح حدود و قصاص کے علاوہ دوسری چیزوں میں بھی قبول نہ ہوگی۔
There is no harm. The proof of Imam Zufar is that in those matters in which testimony is permissible from people, only hearing is needed, and the hearing of a blind person has no deficiency; rather, the blind person is like a sighted person in hearing. So when in those matters only hearing is needed and the hearing of a blind person has no deficiency, then in those matters the testimony of the blind person will be accepted. Yes, if a blind person is also deaf, his testimony is unanimously not accepted. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Shafi'i is that when a blind person was sighted and possessed eyes at the time of bearing testimony (tahammul), he has acquired knowledge of the testified matter. And a person who acquires knowledge of the testified matter through observation at the time of bearing testimony, his bearing (tahammul) is valid. In any case, a person who is currently blind but was possessed of eyes at the time of bearing testimony, his bearing of testimony is valid. As for the performance (ada') of testimony, it is only through speech, and since there is no defect in the tongue of a blind person, there will be no deficiency in his speech. And when there is no deficiency in the blind person's speech due to no defect in his tongue, his performance of testimony is also valid. In summary, the said blind person's bearing of testimony is valid and his performance is valid, and the impediment to testimony — i.e., not recognizing the defendant (mashhud 'alayhi) — is negated. Because the blind person will identify the defendant by stating his lineage. For example, if the blind person is told: 'Testify for so-and-so son of so-and-so against the defendant so-and-so son of so-and-so,' by stating this lineage the blind person will recognize the defendant. Just as happens in testifying about a deceased person: e.g., the creditors of the deceased claim and produce witnesses, it is not possible for the witness to point at the deceased. So they can testify as: 'So-and-so son of so-and-so has such a debt upon the deceased.' In any case, when the said blind person's bearing and performance of testimony are both valid and the impediment to testimony is negated, there is no harm in accepting the said blind person's testimony. The proof of the two (al-tarfayn) is that for the performance of testimony it is necessary for the witness to distinguish between the plaintiff and the defendant by pointing, and a blind person can only differentiate between them by their voices. He cannot differentiate by pointing. And since one person's voice resembles another's voice, there will be some confusion in voices. And it is possible to avoid this confusion by means of [other] witnesses, as there are many sighted witnesses present who can distinguish between the plaintiff and defendant by pointing. So when sighted witnesses are present, how can it be valid to make a blind person a witness who cannot differentiate between the plaintiff and defendant by pointing? The phrase 'al-nisbatu ta'rifun lil-gha'ibi duna al-hadiri' is an answer to a question. The question is: Can a blind person differentiate between the plaintiff and defendant by stating their lineage? i.e., not only rely on their voices but also inquire about their lineage; by this inquiry the blind witness can easily differentiate between the plaintiff and defendant. And when the blind witness can differentiate between the plaintiff and defendant through lineage, then the blind person's testimony should be accepted. The answer to this is that stating lineage is for the identification of the absent (gha'ib) party, not for the identification of the present (hadir) party. In the issue under discussion, both the plaintiff and defendant are present, so how can stating lineage serve for their identification? And when stating lineage does not serve for their identification, the blind witness will not be able to differentiate between the two. And when the blind witness is not able to differentiate between the plaintiff and defendant, his testimony will not be accepted, because for the performance of testimony it is necessary to differentiate and distinguish between the plaintiff and defendant. In any case, the mentioned matters become like hudud and qisas. So just as the testimony of a blind person is unanimously not permissible in hudud and qisas, similarly it will not be accepted in other matters besides hudud and qisas.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed juristic dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding the admissibility of a blind person's testimony (shahadat al-nabina). It opens with the proof of Imam Zufar (a Hanafi) who argues that for matters where testimony is accepted based on hearing alone (e.g., contracts, debts, other transactions not requiring visual identification), a blind person's hearing is as good as a sighted person's, so his testimony should be accepted. However, Imam Zufar's view is not the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position; the majority of the Hanafi school (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) along with Imam al-Shafi'i hold that the blind person's testimony is only valid if he was sighted at the time of bearing testimony (tahammul). Their reasoning: the essence of bearing testimony requires visual observation (mushahada), and if that was present at the time of bearing, the later blindness does not affect the validity of the testimony's performance (ada') which is merely oral. They further argue that identification of the defendant can be achieved through lineage (nisba), as is done for deceased persons. The passage then presents the counter-argument by the 'two sides' (tarfayn — referring to Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, or possibly the two companions Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? In Hidayah context, 'tarfayn' often means Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but here it seems to be the opposing view to Abu Yusuf's earlier position. The 'tarfayn' argue that a witness must be able to physically point to the parties, which a blind person cannot do, leading to confusion. The rebuttal via lineage is dismissed because lineage is for identifying absent persons, not present ones. The passage concludes that just as blind testimony is rejected in hudud and qisas by consensus, it is also rejected in other matters. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of combining textual evidence (nas), qiyas (analogy), and istihsan (juristic preference) in a contested ruling.

Key Terms
تحمل شہادت (tahammul al-shahadah): The act of bearing or acquiring testimony; the phase where the witness sees or hears the event.
ادائے شہادت (ada' al-shahadah): The performance or delivery of testimony in court.
اشارہ (isharah): Physical pointing or gesturing to identify the plaintiff and defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the majority of Hanafi imams (tarfayn) reject the testimony of a blind person who is blind both at bearing and performance?
A) Because his hearing is defective.
B) Because he cannot distinguish between plaintiff and defendant by pointing.
C) Because he cannot speak clearly.
D) Because he is not qualified to bear testimony at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi rejects blind testimony because the witness cannot perform the required physical pointing (isharah) to distinguish the parties in court.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on a Witness Who Becomes Blind After Bearing Testimony
Intra-Hanafi dispute on blindness after testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on a judge's ruling when a witness becomes blind after testimony, and explain why capacity must continue until the verdict.

Core Idea
A witness's capacity must continue until verdict; blindness after testimony invalidates capacity, barring the judge's ruling.

This passage addresses a critical question in the law of testimony: does a witness's later blindness affect a judge's ability to rule on that testimony? Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad argue that capacity must persist until judgment, so blindness invalidates it. Imam Abu Yusuf draws an analogy to absence, but the passage shows why the two's view prevails.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position of the two (tarfayn)
Identify the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the judge cannot rule based on the testimony of a witness who became blind after performance.
The 'two' here refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, opposed to Abu Yusuf.
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's dissenting view
Abu Yusuf holds that the judge may rule, drawing an analogy to a witness who becomes absent after testimony.
Absence does not destroy capacity.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's proof (qiyas)
His analogy: just as absence after testimony does not prevent a ruling, blindness should not either. The condition for ruling is that the testimony was valid at performance.
Qiyas based on shared attribute of not affecting the testimony given.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response distinguishing the cases
The two respond by distinguishing blindness from absence and death. Death completes capacity (it does not invalidate), absence leaves capacity intact, but blindness directly destroys the physical ability to identify parties, thus invalidates capacity at the time of judgment.
Key distinction: blindness is analogous to insanity, muteness, or fasiq, all of which invalidate capacity.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
According to the two, the judge cannot rule, and any ruling given would be invalid. According to Abu Yusuf, the judge can rule. The Hidayah sides with the two, making their view the mufta bihi.
The practical consequence: the case would need to be dismissed or retried with new witnesses.

Source Text

صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ گواہ اگر ادائے شہادت کے وقت بینا ہو ۔ اور ادائے شہادت کے بعد قضائے قاضی سے پہلے نابینا ہو گیا ہو تو طرفین کے نزدیک اس شہادت کی بنیاد پر قاضی کے لئے حکم کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ البتہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ اس بارے میں ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ عمل شہادت ( گواہی اٹھانے) کے بعد جو چیز ادائے شہادت کے لئے مانع ہے وہی چیز ادائے شہادت کے بعد قضائے قاضی کے لئے مانع ہے پس محمل شہادت کے بعد نا بینا ہو جانا چونکہ طرفین کے نزدیک ادائے شہادت کے لئے مانع ہے اس لئے ادائے شہادت کے بعد گواہ کا نابینا ہو جانا طرفین کے نزدیک قضائے قاضی کے لئے بھی مانع ہوگا۔ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک تحمل شہادت کے بعد نا بینا ہو جانا چونکہ ادائے شہادت کے لئے مانع نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ادائے شہادت کے بعد نا بینا ہو جانا قضائے قاضی کے لئے بھی مانع نہ ہوگا۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل . قیاس ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح ادائے شہادت کے بعد قضائے قاضی سے پہلے گواہ کے غائب ہو جانے کی صورت میں قاضی کے لئے فیصلہ صادر کرنا جائز ہے اس طرح نابینا ہو جانے کی صورت میں بھی قضائے قاضی جائز ہوگا۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی کے فیصلہ دیتے وقت گواہ کے اندر گواہی کی اہلیت کا ہونا شرط ہے۔ کیونکہ گواہی فیصلہ کے وقت ہی حجت ہوتی ہے۔ حالانکہ فیصلہ کے وقت نابینا گواہ میں گواہی کی اہلیت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے گواہی کا حجت ہونا باطل ہو گیا اور جب گواہی کا حجت ہونا باطل ہو گیا تو قاضی فیصلہ کرنے کا بھی مجاز نہ ہوگا کیونکہ قاضی بلا حجت حکم اور فیصلہ صادر نہیں کر سکتا اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے گواہ ادائے شہادت کے بعد قضائے قاضی سے پہلے دیوانہ ہو گیا ہو۔ یا گونگا ہو گیا ہو یا فاسق ہو گیا ہو یعنی جس طرح ان صورتوں میں گواہوں کے اندر بطلان اہلیت کی وجہ سے قاضی کے لئے حکم دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح گواہ کے نابینا ہونے کی صورت میں بھی قاضی فیصلہ دینے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا۔ بخلاف ما اذاما تو اوغا بوا الخ سے امام ابو یوسف کے قیاس کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ادائے شہادت کے بعد اور قضائے قاضی سے پہلے اگر گواہ مرجائیں تو مرنے کی وجہ سے ان کی اہلیت باطل نہیں ہوتی ۔ بلکہ موت کی وجہ سے ان کی اہلیت اپنی انتہا کو پہنچ گئی ہے اور شی اپنی انتہا کو پہنچ کر ثابت ہوتی ہے باطل نہیں ہوتی ۔ بہر حال جب موت کی وجہ سے گواہوں کی اہلیت باطل نہیں ہوئی بلکہ ثابت ہوئی ہے تو قاضی ، ان گواہوں کی گواہی پر فیصلہ دے سکتا ہے۔ اسی طرح ادائے شہادت کے بعد گواہوں کے غائب ہونے سے چونکہ گواہوں کی اہلیت باطل نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے گواہوں کے غائب ہونے کے باوجود قاضی ان کی گواہی پر فیصلہ صادر کر سکتا ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر ادائے شہادت کے بعد قضائے قاضی سے پہلے گواہ نابینا ہو گئے تو نا بینا ہونے کی وجہ سے ان کی اہلیت باطل ہو جاتی ہے اور جب نابینا کی اہلیت باطل ہو جاتی ہے تو قاضی ان کی گواہی پر فیصلہ دینے کا بھی مجاز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ فیصلہ کے وقت تک گواہوں کے اندر اہلیت کا موجود رہنا شرط ہے۔
The author of al-Hidayah said: If a witness was sighted at the time of performing testimony and became blind after performing testimony but before the judge's verdict, then according to the two (tarfayn), it is not permissible for the judge to rule based on that testimony. However, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, it is permissible. The principle in this regard is: whatever is an impediment to the performance of testimony after the bearing of testimony is also an impediment to the judge's verdict after the performance. So, since becoming blind after bearing testimony is an impediment to the performance according to the two, therefore the witness becoming blind after performance is also an impediment to the judge's verdict according to the two. According to Abu Yusuf, since becoming blind after bearing testimony is not an impediment to the performance, therefore becoming blind after performance is not an impediment to the judge's verdict either. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is qiyas (analogy): just as when a witness becomes absent after performance but before the judge's verdict, it is permissible for the judge to issue a verdict, similarly in the case of becoming blind, the judge's verdict is permissible. The proof of the two is that at the time of the judge's decision, the presence of capacity (ahliyyah) for testimony in the witness is a condition. Because testimony is proof (hujjah) only at the time of decision. Since at the time of decision the blind witness lacks capacity for testimony, the testimony's status as proof becomes invalid, and when the testimony's being proof becomes invalid, the judge is not authorized to decide, because the judge cannot issue a ruling without proof. This is like the witness becoming insane after performance but before the verdict, or becoming mute, or becoming a sinner (fasiq) — i.e., just as in those cases it is not permissible for the judge to rule due to the invalidation of capacity, similarly in the case of the witness becoming blind, the judge is not authorized to rule. The phrase 'bikhilafi ma idhā mātū au ghābū' is the answer to Imam Abu Yusuf's qiyas. The gist of the answer is: If the witnesses die after performance but before the judge's verdict, their capacity is not invalidated by death. Rather, their capacity reaches its extreme due to death, and a thing that reaches its extreme is established, not invalidated. In any case, since capacity is not invalidated but rather established by death, the judge can rule on their testimony. Similarly, if the witnesses become absent after performance, their capacity is not invalidated, so the judge can rule on their testimony despite their absence. In contrast, if the witnesses become blind after performance but before the judge's verdict, their capacity is invalidated due to blindness, and when the blind person's capacity is invalidated, the judge is not authorized to rule on their testimony, because the continuance of capacity in the witnesses until the time of decision is a condition.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific scenario: a witness who was sighted at the time of performing testimony, but after delivering the testimony and before the judge pronounces the verdict, becomes blind. The 'Tarfayn' (the two: generally meaning Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, but here 'tarfayn' is contrasted with Imam Abu Yusuf) hold that the judge cannot rule based on that testimony, because the witness lacks capacity (ahliyyah) at the time of decision. Imam Abu Yusuf dissents, using qiyas: just as a witness's absence after testimony does not prevent a ruling, blindness should not either. The passage then refutes Abu Yusuf's analogy by distinguishing absence/ death from blindness. Death does not invalidate capacity but completes it — 'a thing reaching its extreme is established' — and absence does not destroy capacity either. Blindness, however, directly destroys the capacity to perform testimony (which requires the ability to identify parties by sight). Hence, the judge cannot rule. The principle: the witness's capacity must exist at the time of testimony-performance and continue until the judge's decision. This is a clear intra-Hanafi dispute with clear tarjih (preference) for the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).

Key Terms
طرفین (tarfayn): In this passage, 'the two sides' refers to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (as opposed to Imam Abu Yusuf).
اہلیت (ahliyyah): Legal capacity of a witness to testify; includes the physical ability to identify parties and mental soundness.
حجت (hujjah): Proof or legal evidence. Testimony becomes a hujjah only at the time of the judge's decision.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a witness becomes blind after performing testimony but before the judge's verdict, what is the ruling?
A) The judge may still rule because the testimony was valid when performed.
B) The judge cannot rule because the witness's capacity is invalidated.
C) The testimony becomes void automatically.
D) The witness must repeat the testimony with a sighted person.

Key Takeaway
The judge cannot rely on testimony when the witness loses capacity before the decision, as capacity must persist until the moment of judgment.
